Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
10 min
Diyat for Shibh Amd and Khata: Liability and Payment Methods
Rulings on diyat for shibh amd and khata, and kaffara obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears diyat for accidental and quasi-intentional murder, and explain the flexibility in payment methods according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Diyat for accidental murder is on the aqila, not the killer, and can be paid in any form of wealth.

In Hanafi law, the blood money (diyat) for quasi-intentional (shibh amd) and accidental (khata) murder is not a personal fine on the killer but a collective responsibility of his paternal relatives (aqila). This lesson unpacks the ruling and explores the flexibility in payment methods — a point of difference between the Hanafis and other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which type of killing is discussed (shibh amd and khata) and state the legal consequence: diyat on aqila and kaffara on killer.
Shibh amd is quasi-intentional; khata is accidental. Kaffara is wajib on the killer personally.
2
Locate the dalil
Examine the proof cited: the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argued that severity (taghleez) is specific to camels, implying other forms are permissible.
The proof is derived from the Sunnah's fixing of diyat in camels, with interpretation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the proof supports the Hanafi position: since the Prophet set diyat in camels but did not restrict it, other items of equivalent value are acceptable.
This leads to the flexibility view of Imam Abu Hanifa.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference (Shaykhayn vs. Imam Muhammad) and the cross-madhhab difference with Imam Shafi'i regarding permissible payment forms.
Imam Shafi'i restricts to camels, gold, silver; Imam Muhammad had a separate view.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi position: the Hanafi school favors flexibility, allowing payment in any form of money or property, as this gives leniency.
This is the relied-upon view in fatwa.

Source Text

قتل شبه عمد کی دیت عاقلہ پر اور کفارہ قاتل پر ہے قتل شبہ عمد کا کفارہ کیا ہے
كتاب الديات
قتل خطاء کا کفارہ قتل شبه عمد والا ہے قبل خطاء کی دیت میں شیخین کا مسلک قتل خطا ء کی دیت میں امام شافعی اور امام محمد کا مسلک

قتل خطاء کی دیت

استدلال
قاتل ، اونٹوں ، سونے، چاندی کے علاوہ سے دیت ادا کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل
The blood money for quasi-intentional murder is on the aqila, and the expiation is on the killer. What is the expiation for quasi-intentional murder? The Book of Blood Money. The expiation for accidental murder is the same as for quasi-intentional murder. Regarding the blood money for accidental murder, the madhhab of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The madhhab of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad regarding blood money for accidental murder. The proof of the two shaykhs. Severity is specific only to camels. In accidental murder, the blood money is on the aqila and the expiation is on the killer. The blood money for accidental murder. There is a small difference between Imam Shafi'i and the Hanafis regarding the blood money for accidental murder. The blood money for accidental murder is one thousand gold dinars and ten thousand silver dirhams. The reasoning of Imam Shafi'i and the Hanafis. Can the killer pay the blood money with other than camels, gold, or silver? Statements of jurists, proof of Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Diyat discusses the blood money (diyat) and expiation (kaffara) for quasi-intentional murder (qatl shibh amd) and accidental murder (qatl khata). The author begins by stating that for shibh amd, the diyat is on the aqila (the killer's paternal relatives who are liable for blood money) and the kaffara is on the killer. He then transitions to diyat for accidental murder, noting that the kaffara is the same as for shibh amd. He mentions a difference between the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad regarding the amount and type of diyat. The Shaykhayn hold that the diyat is heavy (mugallazah) only when paid in camels, not in other forms. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad have a different view. The passage then states the standard Hanafi position: the diyat for accidental murder is 1000 gold dinars or 10,000 silver dirhams. The text mentions a small difference between Shafi'i and Hanafis, likely about the permissibility of paying in other than those four types (camels, gold, silver, etc.). It ends by raising the question of whether the killer can pay in other forms, and mentions the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa on this.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (a'qila): The paternal relatives of the killer who are responsible for paying diyat in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional murder.
کفارہ (kaffara): Expiation for killing; for accidental murder, it is fasting two consecutive months or feeding 60 poor people.
شبه عمد (shibh amd): Quasi-intentional murder: an act intended to cause harm but not death, and death results.
خطأ (khata): Accidental murder: death caused by mistake without intent to harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the amount of diyat for accidental murder in silver?
A) 1,000 dirhams
B) 10,000 dirhams
C) 12,000 dirhams
D) 5,000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Diyat for accidental and quasi-intentional murder is a collective obligation on the aqila, and Hanafi law permits payment in any form of wealth of equivalent value.

Liability for Arrow Shooting with Change of Victim's Status
Rules on liability when victim's status changes between shooting and impact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for injury when the victim's legal status changes between the act and the injury, and apply the principle that the status at impact determines liability.

Core Idea
Liability for injury is determined at impact, not at the act.

In Hanafi fiqh, a critical principle for liability (daman) in unintentional injuries is that the time of impact decides the victim's protected status (isma). This lesson presents three scenarios from classical texts: shooting at an apostate (murtadd) or combatant (harbi) who converts before impact, shooting at a slave who is freed before impact, and shooting at a condemned person whose witness retracts before the arrow hits. In each, the status at the moment the arrow strikes determines whether the shooter is liable for blood money (diyat) or other compensation. Understanding this principle prevents confusion about when liability attaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and note the three distinct cases: (1) arrow shot at a murtadd/harbi who becomes Muslim, (2) arrow shot at a slave who is freed, (3) arrow shot at a person under a death verdict where a witness retracts testimony.
2
Check status at shooting vs. at impact
For each scenario, determine the victim's legal status (protected or unprotected) at the moment the arrow was shot and at the moment it struck. In case (1), unprotected at shooting, protected at impact. In case (2), slave (unprotected? Actually slaves are protected but with lower value) but becomes free protected at impact. In case (3), protected at shooting? The verdict makes the victim unprotected (since death sentence), but retraction restores protection? Actually the text says no liability because the retraction removes the basis of the verdict.
The status at impact is pivotal.
3
Determine liability based on impact status
Apply the rule: the shooter is liable only if the victim is protected (ma‘sum) at the moment of impact. In case (1), the victim is Muslim at impact, so one might expect liability, but the rule says no liability because the act was not transgressive against a protected person at the time of shooting? Actually the text says 'this does not entail liability' – this indicates that the shooter cannot be liable because the victim was not protected at the time of the act. This is an exception? Upon reflection, the Hanafi position is that for liability to arise, the act must involve transgression (ta'addi) against a protected person. The shooting itself was done against an unprotected person, so it was not transgressive. The change of status does not retroactively make it transgressive. Hence no liability.
The act must be transgressive at the time of the act; subsequent protection does not create liability.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute in the slave case
The passage mentions proofs from Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the slave case. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that liability attaches only upon impact, so if the slave is freed before impact, the shooter becomes liable for a free person's diyat. Imam Muhammad may have held that the moment of shooting is the basis, so the shooter would only be liable for a slave's compensation. Recognize that this ikhtilaf is about the time of attaching liability.
The dispute highlights the importance of determining the relevant moment for transgression.
5
Conclude the principle
The general principle from all three cases: liability (daman) for injury from a projectile depends on the victim's legal protection status at the moment of impact, not the moment of shooting. However, the act must have been transgressive at the time it was performed. In case (1), the act was not transgressive; in case (2), the act was transgressive (shooting a slave is transgressive?), and the impact on a free person makes the liability for a free person. In case (3), the act was transgressive but the victim was unprotected at impact due to the retraction, so no liability. This principle is consistent across the examples.
Memorize the three cases as anchors for the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی پر تیر پھینکا اس حالت میں مرمی الیہ مرتد یا حربی ہے پھر وہ مسلمان ہوا اور اسے تیر لگا تو یہ موجب ضمان نہیں کسی نے غلام کو تیر مارا تیر لگنے سے پہلے اس کے آقا نے اسے آزاد کر دیا پھر تیر لگا تو رامی پر کیا چیز واجب ہے، اقوال فقہاء امام محمد کی دلیل شیخین کی دلیل تیر لگنے سے پہلے کچھ واجب نہیں جب تیز لگے گا پھر ضمان واجب ہوگا جس پر رحم کا فیصلہ ہو گیا اس کو کسی نے تیر مارا پھر ایک گواہ نے گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا پھر اسکو تیر لگا تو رامی پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوگا
Someone shot an arrow at a person while that person was an apostate or a combatant. Then he became Muslim and the arrow hit him, so this does not entail liability. Someone shot an arrow at a slave; before the arrow hit, his master freed him; then the arrow hit. What is obligatory upon the shooter? Statements of the jurists. Imam Muhammad's proof. Proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Nothing is obligatory before the arrow hits; when the arrow hits, then liability becomes obligatory. Someone shot an arrow at a person against whom a [court] verdict of mercy had been passed; then one witness retracted his testimony; then the arrow hit him; then nothing is obligatory upon the shooter.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage presents multiple rulings on liability for shooting an arrow when the status of the target changes between the act of shooting and the impact. The first rule: if a person shoots at an apostate or a combatant (harbi) and that person converts to Islam before being hit, then there is no liability because at the time of impact the target is a protected person (ma‘sum) but the shooting occurred when he was not protected, and liability is attached to the act of transgression, which is not present here. The second rule: if a slave is shot and his master frees him before the arrow hits, the shooter's liability is debated; the text mentions proofs from Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The general principle is that nothing is owed before the arrow hits; once it hits, liability arises. The third rule: if a person has been sentenced to death (rahm) by two witnesses, then one witness retracts before the arrow hits, the shooter is not liable because the retraction removes the basis for the sentence, making the victim's blood unprotected at the time of impact. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi position that the time of impact determines the legal protection (isma) of the victim.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate from Islam, whose blood is unprotected until repentance or execution.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim from a hostile territory (dar al-harb) with no covenant.
ضمان (daman): Legal liability, particularly monetary compensation for injury or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rulings in this passage, what determines whether an arrow shooter is liable?
A) The status of the victim at the time of shooting
B) The status of the victim at the time of impact
C) The intention of the shooter
D) The distance of the shot

Key Takeaway
Liability for injury is determined by the victim's legal protection status at the moment of impact, not the moment of the act.

Hunting by a Magian: The State at Shooting Governs
Ruling on game shot by a Magian who converts, and a Muslim who apostatizes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for game shot by a Magian who converts before the arrow hits, and explain why the state at shooting determines permissibility.

Core Idea
The hunter's state at the moment of shooting determines the game's permissibility, not subsequent conversion.

This passage addresses an important timing issue in Islamic hunting law: does a change in the hunter's religious status between the shot and the impact retroactively affect the game's permissibility? The Hanafi position is clear — the ruling is fixed at the time the arrow is released. We will examine two scenarios: a Magian who becomes Muslim, and a Muslim who apostatizes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the first part of the passage: a Magian who shoots then converts, and a Muslim who shoots then apostatizes. Note the different outcomes.
The Magian case: game not eaten. The apostasy case: game eaten.
2
State the ruling for each
State clearly: if a non-Muslim (Magian) shoots, the game is haram even if he converts before impact. If a Muslim shoots, the game is halal even if he apostatizes before impact.
Opposite outcomes.
3
Identify the common principle
The principle is that the state at the time of shooting (time of the shot) governs the ruling, not the state at the time the arrow strikes.
This is a key Hanafi rule.
4
Understand the rationale
The act of shooting is the effective cause (sabab) of the hunting. Its validity depends on the condition of the hunter at that moment. Subsequent changes do not affect it.
This is based on the principle that a cause is evaluated at its inception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجوسی نے شکار کو تیر مارا پھر مسلمان ہوگیا پھر تیر شکار کولگا تو شکار نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور اگر حالت اسلام میں تیر مارا پھر العیاذ باللہ مرتد ہو گیا تو شکار کھایا جائے گا محرم نے شکا کو تیر مارا پھروہ حلال ہو گیا پس تیر شکار کو گا تو اس پر جزا ملا زم ہوگی اور اگر حلال نے تیر مارا پھر محرم بن گیا تو اس پر جزا و لازم نہیں ہوگی
A Magian shot an arrow at game, then he became Muslim, then the arrow hit the game: the game will not be eaten. And if he shot the arrow while in the state of Islam, then (God forbid) he became an apostate, then the game will be eaten. A muhrim (one in ihram) shot an arrow at game, then he became halal (ended his ihram), then the arrow hit the game: so upon him the penalty (jaza) is binding. And if a halal (non-muhrim) shot the arrow, then he became a muhrim, then upon him the penalty is not binding.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage presents two pairs of rulings concerning hunting when the hunter's state changes between shooting and impact. The first pair concerns a Magian (majusi) who shoots game. If he converts to Islam before the arrow hits, the game is not lawful to eat because the hunting was done as a non-Muslim whose slaughter is invalid; the conversion after shooting does not retroactively validate the hunting. Conversely, if a Muslim shoots while Muslim then apostatizes before impact, the game is lawful because the hunting was valid at the time of shooting. The second pair concerns a muhrim (person in ihram) who hunts. If he shoots while in ihram then exits ihram before the arrow hits, he still incurs the penalty (jaza) for hunting in ihram because the prohibited act occurred at the moment of shooting. But if a non-muhrim (halal) shoots and then enters ihram before impact, no penalty is due because the shooting itself was done without the prohibition. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that the validity of hunting is determined at the time the arrow is released, not when it strikes.

Key Terms
مجوسی (majusi): A Zoroastrian/Magian; considered non-Ahl al-Kitab in Hanafi school, so their hunting is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a Muslim shoots an arrow at game and then becomes an apostate before the arrow hits, the game is:
A) haram because he apostatized
B) halal because he was Muslim at the time of shooting
C) halal only if he repents
D) haram because the arrow was not shot with proper intention

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hunting is determined by the hunter's state at the moment of shooting, not at the moment of impact.

Hunting by a Muhrim: Penalty Depends on State at Shooting
Ruling on hunting by a muhrim who ends ihram, and a halal who enters ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a muhrim incurs a penalty (jaza) when his state changes between shooting and impact, and apply the principle that the state at shooting determines liability.

Core Idea
The obligation of jaza for hunting in ihram is fixed at the moment of shooting, not when the arrow strikes.

This passage addresses a similar timing issue for a person in ihram (muhrim). The muhrim is prohibited from hunting. But what if he shoots while in ihram and then exits ihram before the arrow hits? Or vice versa? The Hanafi ruling is consistent with the earlier principle: the state at the time of shooting decides. We will see that a muhrim who shoots incurs the penalty regardless of later becoming halal, and a halal person who shoots does not incur penalty even if later enters ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the second part of the passage: a muhrim who shoots then becomes halal, and a halal who shoots then becomes muhrim. Note the outcomes.
First: penalty is binding. Second: no penalty.
2
State the ruling for each
If a muhrim shoots, jaza is obligatory even if he exits ihram before impact. If a non-muhrim shoots, no jaza even if he later enters ihram.
The penalty is incurred based on ihram status at shooting.
3
Identify the common principle
The principle is that the prohibition of hunting during ihram applies at the time the act of hunting is initiated, i.e., at the moment of shooting.
The state at impact is irrelevant.
4
Understand the rationale
The act of shooting is the prohibited act; its prohibition depends on the hunter's state at that moment. Later changes do not alter the ruling.
Consistent with the principle from the first part.

Source Text

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, prohibited from hunting.
جزا (jaza): The penalty (compensation) for hunting while in ihram, typically slaughtering an animal equivalent to the game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The obligation of jaza for hunting in ihram is fixed at the moment of shooting, regardless of later changes in the hunter's state.

Legal Consequences of Qatl Shibh Amd
Stating the rulings for Qatl Shibh Amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three consequences of Qatl Shibh Amd and explain why each is wajib.

Core Idea
In Qatl Shibh Amd, sin is on the killer, kaffarah wajib, heavy diyah on the aqila.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the agreed-upon consequences of Qatl Shibh Amd (quasi-intentional homicide). While the definition of Shibh Amd is disputed, the rulings for sin, expiation, and blood money are settled. The text clarifies that the heavy diyah is borne by the aqila, not the killer, and is payable over three years, based on the precedent of Caliph Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three consequences
List what becomes wajib (obligatory) due to Qatl Shibh Amd: sin (ithm), kaffarah, and heavy diyah (blood money).
Sin is inherent in the act; kaffarah and diyah are external obligations.
2
Understand the rationale for sin
The sin exists because the killer intended the strike (qasada fī al-ḍarb), even if death was not intended. Intentional harmful action is sinful.
The sin is separate from the diyah obligation.
3
Understand the rationale for kaffarah
Kaffarah is wajib because Shibh Amd resembles accidental killing (khata) in that the tool was not meant to kill. By analogy (qiyas), expiation is required.
Resemblance to khata triggers kaffarah.
4
Identify the rule for diyah
The diyah is mughallazah (heavy), payable by the aqila (agnatic relatives), not the killer. It is paid in three annual installments based on the judgment of Umar ibn al-Khattab.
The principle: any diyah that becomes obligatory at the outset due to killing is on the aqila, by analogy to khata.
5
Note the principle and deferred detail
The text states the general principle that diyah from initial killing is on the aqila and promises to describe the exact composition of heavy diyah later.
The quality of mughallazah (e.g., specific mix of camels) will be explained in a subsequent lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قتل شبه عمد کا موجب و حکم
قال وموجب ذلك على القولين الاثم لانه قتل وهو قاصد فى الضرب والكفارة لشبهه بالخطا والدية مغلظة على العاقلة والاصل ان كل دية وجبت بالقتل ابتداء لا بمعنى يحدث من بعد فهي على العاقلة اعتباراً بالخطا وتجب فى ثلث سنين لقضية عمر بن الخطاب رضى الله عنه وتجب مغلظة وسنبين صفة التغليظ من بعد ان شاء الله تعالى
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور شبہ عمد کا موجب دونوں قولوں کے مطابق گناہ ہے اس لئے کہ قاتل نے قتل کیا حالانکہ وہ مارنے کا قصد کرنے والا ہے اور کفارہ واجب ہے اس کے مشابہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قتل خطا سے (اور اس کا موجب ) عاقلہ پر دیت مغلظہ ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ہر دیت جو قتل کی وجہ سے شروع میں واجب ہو بعد کے معنی سے نہیں تو وہ عاقلہ پر ہے قتل خطا کے اعتبار سے اور تین سال میں واجب ہے عمر بن خطاب رضی اللہ عنہ کے فیصلہ کے مطابق اور وہ دیت مغلظہ ہے اور ہم تغلیظ کی صفت بعد میں بیان کریں گے ان شاء اللہ تعالیٰ۔
The cause and ruling of Qatl Shibh Amd: He said: Its consequence according to the two opinions is sin because he killed while intending the strike, and kaffarah because of its resemblance to Khata, and heavy diyah upon the aqila. The principle: every diyah that becomes obligatory by killing initially, not by a meaning that occurs later, is upon the aqila by analogy to Khata. It is obligatory in three years following the judgment of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him). It is heavy diyah, and we will describe the quality of intensification later, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri states the legal consequences of Qatl Shibh Amd, which are agreed upon by both views (Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn). The killer commits a sin because the strike was intentional. Kaffarah (expiation) is wajib because the act resembles Khata (accidental killing) in that the tool was not intended to kill. The diyah (blood money) is mughallazah (heavy/aggravated) and is to be paid by the aqila (the male agnatic relatives of the killer), not from the killer's own wealth. The reason is that the diyah is imposed at the outset due to the killing itself, not due to a subsequent cause, so it is borne by the aqila by analogy to accidental killing. It is payable in installments over three years, based on the precedent set by Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab. The commentary notes that the description of 'mughallazah' (heavy) will be explained later. This ruling applies to Shibh Amd regardless of the dispute over definition, as both positions agree on the consequences once the act is classified as Shibh Amd.

Key Terms
دية مغلظة (diyah mughallazah): Heavy blood money: 100 camels, with specific conditions like 30 hiqqah, 30 jadh'ah, etc., as will be detailed.
عاقلة (aqila): The male agnatic relatives (asabah) of the killer who bear the diyah in cases of khata and shibh amd.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor persons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, in Qatl Shibh Amd, who is responsible for paying the heavy diyah?
A) The killer from his own wealth
B) The state treasury
C) The aqila (agnatic relatives of the killer)
D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
In Qatl Shibh Amd, the three consequences are sin on the killer, wajib kaffarah, and heavy diyah on the aqila over three years.

Types and Rulings of Accidental Killing (Qatl Khata)
Defines two types of accidental killing and their rulings with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two types of qatl khata (error in intention vs. error in action) and state the Hanafi ruling that both require kaffarah and diyah on the aqilah, citing the Quranic proof from Surah An-Nisa 4:92.

Core Idea
Accidental killing requires kaffarah and diyah on the aqilah—negligence of precaution explains why kaffarah is prescribed.

In the Hanafi school, accidental killing (qatl khata) is not treated as a single monolithic category. This lesson, drawn from Al-Hidayah and its commentaries, dissects two distinct subtypes: error in intention and error in action. Although both lead to the same legal consequences, understanding the classification sharpens your ability to apply the rulings correctly. We will also examine the Quranic proof and the subtle discussion about whether any sin attaches to such acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types from examples
Read the passage carefully to see how Quduri classifies qatl khata. The first type is error in intention: shooter mistakes a protected human for game or an enemy. The second is error in action: shooter misses the intended target and hits a person instead.
The key distinction is the locus of the mistake: the intended person (first) versus the intended action (second).
2
State the legal consequences for both
Both types trigger exactly the same obligations: kaffarah (expiation) on the killer personally, and diyah (blood money) on the killer's aqilah (paternal relatives), payable over three years.
Kaffarah is freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months; diyah is compensation to the victim's heirs.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The author cites the Quranic verse from Surah An-Nisa, verse 92, which explicitly commands both kaffarah and diyah for accidental killing. Locate the phrase in the passage and note its authority.
The verse is general and covers all forms of accidental killing, hence it applies to both subtypes.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah (how proof indicates ruling)
The imperative form of the verse (فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ - 'then the freeing of a slave') indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. The explicit mention of 'diyah' confirms the second obligation.
Although the transmission (thubut) is definitive, the meaning (dalala) is open to interpretation regarding some details, making it zanni.
5
Address the sin nuance
The passage clarifies that there is no sin of intentional murder (ithm al-qatl), but there is a lesser sin due to negligence of precaution (tark al-azimah) at the time of shooting. The prescription of kaffarah itself signals this, as kaffarah is only prescribed for acts involving some degree of fault.
This nuance affects whether the killer is considered sinful for missing the taklif of caution, but does not change the obligation of kaffarah and diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا قتل خطا دو قسم پر ہے ایک رادہ کی خطا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ تیر مارے کسی ایسے شخص کو جس کو وہ شکار سمجھ رہا ہے پس اچانک وہ آدمی ہے یا اس کو حر بی سمجھ رہا ہے پس اچانک وہ مسلمان ہے اور دوسری خطاً فی فعل میں اور وہ یہ ہے کہ کسی نشانہ پر تیر مارے ہیں وہ کسی آدمی کو لگ جائے اور اسکا موجب کفارہ اور دیت ہے عاقلہ پر اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة الى اهله الآية " کی وجہ سے اور دیت قاتل کے عاقلہ پر تین سال میں ہوگی اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح قتل خطا کا موجب کفارہ اور دیت ہے اور دیت عاقلہ پر ہوگی اور اس کی ادائیگی تین سال میں ہوگی جس کی دلیل او پر گذر چکی ہے۔ اور خطا کی دوقسمیں ہیں ایک ارادہ کی خطاً اور دوسرے فعل کی خطا ۔ اول کی مثال جیسے ماررہاتھا ہرن کونگر وہ آدمی نگا ، یا مار رہا تھا حربی کو وہ مسلمان اگا ، سیہ ارادہ کی خطا ہے۔ ثانی کی مثال جیسے کسی نشانہ ہی مارا مگر وہاں نہیں لگا بلکہ کسی آدمی کو لگ گیا یہ فعل کی خطا ہے، بہر حال حکم دونوں کا ایک ہے کہ کفار اور دیت واجب ہے جس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے جو متن میں مذکور ہے۔
قتل خطا میں گناہ نہیں خواہ خطاً فی الارادہ ہو یا خطاً فی الفعل
ولا اثم فيه يعنى فى الوجهين قالو المراد اثم القتل فاما فى نفسه فلا يعرى عن الاثم من حيث ترك العزيمة والمبالغة في التثبت في حال الرمي اذ شرع الكفارة يوذن باعتبار هذا المعنى اور قتل خطا میں دونوں صورتوں میں گنا نہیں ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ مرا قتل کا گناہ ہے بہر حال فی نفسہ یہ فعل گناہ سے خالی نہیں ہے عزیمت کے ترک اور احتیاط میں مبالغہ کو ترک کرنے کی وجدت پھینکنے کے وقت اس لئے کہ کفارہ کا شروع ہوتا اس معنی کے اعتبار کی خبر ہ دیتا ہے۔
Chapter of Jinayat (Homicide). Translation: Quduri said: Qatl khata (accidental killing) is of two types: first, error in aim: one shoots an arrow at a person he considers game, but suddenly it is a human, or he considers him a harbi (enemy), but suddenly he is a Muslim. Second, error in action: one shoots at a target, but it hits a person. Its consequence is kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) on the aqilah (tribe), due to Allah's command: '...then the freeing of a believing slave and compensation delivered to his family...' and the diyah will be paid by the killer's aqilah over three years, based on the proof we have mentioned. Explanation: The cause of qatl khata is kaffarah and diyah, and diyah is on the aqilah, paid over three years, as previously proofed. And khata has two types: error in intention and error in action. First example: he was shooting at a deer [but] he hit a man, or shooting at a harbi but the person was a Muslim. This is error in intention. Second example: he shot at a target but it did not hit there, rather hit a person. This is error in action. In any case, the ruling for both is the same: kaffarah and diyah are wajib. The proof is the verse mentioned in the text. There is no sin in qatl khata, whether error in intention or error in action. 'Wa la ithma fihi' meaning in both ways. They said: the intended meaning is the sin of killing. But in itself, the act is not free from sin due to leaving the resolved determination and not being sufficiently cautious at the time of shooting, since the legislation of kaffarah indicates consideration of this meaning. And in qatl khata, there is no sin in both cases. The mashayikh said: the intended meaning is the sin of killing. In itself, the act is not free from sin due to leaving the 'azimah and not being excessively cautious at the time of throwing, because the prescription of kaffarah indicates this meaning.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah explains the fiqh of accidental killing (qatl khata). The author, following Imam Quduri, states that qatl khata has two types: error in intention (khatta fi al-iradah) and error in action (khatta fi al-fi'l). The first occurs when a person aims at what he thinks is game or an enemy but hits a human or a Muslim. The second occurs when he aims at a target but accidentally hits a person. Both types incur the same legal consequences: kaffarah (freeing a believing slave or its equivalent) and diyah (blood money) payable by the killer's aqilah (tribe) over three years. The proof is Quran 4:92. The text then discusses whether there is sin in accidental killing. The apparent statement that there is no sin refers specifically to the sin of intentional murder. However, the act itself is not free from sin because the killer neglected the required precaution and determination. The fact that kaffarah is legislated indicates that some level of sin is present, as kaffarah is not prescribed for sinless acts. This nuance is important for later rulings on inheritance and liability.

Key Terms
قتل خطا (qatl khata): Accidental killing where there is no intent to kill a specific protected person.
خطا فی الارادہ (khatta fi al-iradah): Error in intention: the killer intended to hit a permissible target but mistakenly hit a protected human.
خطا فی الفعل (khatta fi al-fi'l): Error in action: the killer intended a specific action but it went astray and caused death.
دیت (diyah): Blood money compensation paid by the aqilah to the victim's heirs.
عاقلہ (aqilah): The paternal relatives (asabah) of the killer who are liable to pay diyah.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for accidental killing: freeing a believing slave, or fasting two months consecutively if unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of accidental killing (qatl khata) for the killer's relatives (aqilah)?
A) They must pay qisas (retaliation) to the victim's family.
B) They must pay diyah (blood money) over three years.
C) They must perform kaffarah (expiation) on behalf of the killer.
D) They have no obligation; the killer alone is responsible.

Key Takeaway
Accidental killing (both error in intention and error in action) obligates kaffarah on the killer and diyah on the aqilah, with the Quranic verse 4:92 as the primary proof, and a subtle sin arising from negligence of precaution.

Killing by Cause (Qatl Sabab) and the Shafi'i Dispute
Discusses actions treated as accidental killing and killing by cause with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between killing treated as accidental (ma ajra majra al-khata) and killing by cause (qatl bi sabab), state the Hanafi ruling for each, and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Killing by cause: liability only, not full khata rulings.

This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah clarifies a critical distinction in the law of homicide. Some acts are treated exactly like accidental killing (such as a sleeper rolling onto someone), while others—like digging a well in another's property—are only partially analogous, triggering financial liability but not all consequences. Imam Shafi'i disagreed, arguing for full equivalence. Let's unpack the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Note that the author first mentions acts 'treated as accidental killing' (ma ajra majra al-khata) and then separately discusses 'killing by cause' (qatl bi sabab). Recognize that they have different legal treatments.
The sleeper rolling is fully like qatl khata; the well-digger is only partially like it.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for killing by cause
The Hanafi position: only diyah on the aqilah is wajib; no kaffarah, no deprivation of inheritance. The reasoning is that the killing is not real from the cause-maker (ma'dum haqiqatan), so it is attached only for liability (daman).
The cause-maker sins for the transgressive act (digging), not for the death itself.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam Shafi'i holds that killing by cause is fully like accidental killing in all rulings because 'the Shariah placed him as a killer' (al-shar' anzalahu qatilan). This is a dalil naqli based on the Shariah's treatment.
For Shafi'i, the Shariah's classification overrides the physical reality.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the killing is non-existent from him in reality, so it is only attached in the right of daman, not for other rulings like kaffarah and inheritance. The Shariah's placement is limited to liability.
This is a usul principle: attaching a ruling to a non-existent thing is valid only where specified (daman), not by extension.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In Hanafi, the killer of a deceased person by cause can inherit from that person and does not have to pay kaffarah (e.g., fasting). In Shafi'i, he is deprived of inheritance and must pay kaffarah.
This can affect estate distribution and expiation obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جاری مجری ( قائم مقام ) کا تعارف اور حکم
قال وما اجرى مجرى الخطاء مثل النائم ينقلب على رجل فيقتله فحكمه حكم الخطاء في الشرع واما القتل بسبب كحافر البير وواضع الحجر فى غير ملكه وموجبه اذا تلف فيه ادمى الدية على العاقلة لانه سبب وهو متعد فيه فانزل موقعا فوجبت الدية ولا كفارة فيه ولا يتعلق به حرمان الميراث التلف
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو قتل خطا کے قائم مقام ہے وہ جیسے سونے والا کسی شخص پر پلٹ جائے پس اس کو مار ڈالے تو اس کا حکم قتل خطاء کا حکم ہے شریعت میں اور بہر حال قتل سبب کے ذریعہ جیسے اپنی ملک کے غیر میں کنواں کھودنے والا اور پتھر رکھنے والا اور اس کا موجب جب کہ کوئی آدمی اس میں مرجائے عاقلہ پر دیت ہے اس لیے کہ یہ تکلف کا سبب ہے اور قاتل اس میں متعدی ہے تو اس کو گرانے والے اور دھکیلنے والے کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا پس دیت واجب ہو گی اور اس میں کفارہ نہیں ہے اور اس کے ساتھ میراث سے محروم ہو نا متعلق نہیں ہوتا ۔ تشریح قتل خطا سے فراغت کے بعد مصنف اس قتل کا بیان فرماتے ہیں جو تل خطا کے قائم مقام ہے۔ جیسے آدمی سور ہا تھا اس نے کروٹ لی مگر کسی آدمی کے اوپر پڑ گیا جس کی وجہ سے وہ مر گیا تو اس کا حکم وہی ہو گا جو قتل خطأ ہوتا ہے اس کے بعد پھر مصنف نے قتل کا سبب ذکر فرمایا۔ جیسے کسی آدمی نے ایسی زمین میں کنواں کھودا جو اس کی ملک نہیں ہے اور کوئی اس میں گر کر مر گیا یا اس نے ایسی ہی زمین میں پتھر رکھ دیا جس سے ٹکرا کر کوئی مر گیا تو اس میں عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ کھودنا اور پتھر رکھنا ہلاکت کا سبب ہے۔ اور جب سبب کا مرتکب متعدی ہوتا ہے تو سبب کو علت کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں اس کی تعدی ظاہر ہے لہذا یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ گویا اس نے خود اس کو کنویں میں ڈالا ہے اور خود اس کو پتھر پر دھکیل دیا ہے لہذاد بیت واجب ہوگی البتہ اس میں کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور نہ یہ قاتل میراث سے محروم ہو گا ۔ تنبیہ موقعاً : کنویں میں گرانے والا ، دافعا پتھر پر پھینکنے والا ۔
امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
و قال الشافعي يلحق بالخطأ فى احكامه لان الشرع انزله قاتلا ولنا ان القتل معدوم منه حقيقة فالحق به في حق الضمان فبقى في حق غيره على الاصل وهو ان كان ياثم بالحفر فى غير ملكه لا يأثم بالموت على ما
Introduction and ruling of what is treated as (ma ajra majra) accidental killing. He said: And what is treated as accidental killing, like a sleeping person rolling onto a man and killing him, its ruling is the ruling of accidental killing in the Shariah. As for killing by cause (sabab), like the digger of a well and the placer of a stone in other than his own property, its consequence when a person perishes in it: diyah on the aqilah, because it is a cause and he is transgressive (muta'addi) in it. So he is placed in the position of the one who pushes, so diyah is wajib, and there is no kaffarah in it, and deprivation of inheritance is not attached to it. Translation: Quduri said: And what is treated as accidental killing, like a sleeping person rolling onto a person and killing him, its ruling is the ruling of accidental killing in the Shariah. As for killing by cause, like the digger of a well and the placer of a stone in other than his own property, its consequence when a person perishes therein: diyah on the aqilah, because it is a cause and the killer is transgressive, so he is placed in the position of the one who pushes and the one who shoves. Thus diyah is wajib, and there is no kaffarah in it, and deprivation of inheritance is not attached to it. Explanation: After finishing accidental killing, the author (muharrir) mentions killing that is treated as accidental killing. For example, a person who was sleeping turned over and fell on another, causing death; its ruling is the same as qatl khata. Then the author mentions killing by cause: e.g., someone dug a well in land that is not his property, and someone fell in and died, or placed a stone in such land, and someone hit it and died. In such cases, diyah is wajib on the aqilah because the digging and stone placement are causes of destruction. And when the committer of the cause is transgressive, the cause is downgraded to the level of direct act (illah). Here his transgression is clear, so it is as if he himself pushed him into the well or shoved him onto the stone. Hence diyah is wajib, but kaffarah is not wajib, nor is the killer deprived of inheritance. Note: The one who pushes into the well, the one who thrusts onto the stone. Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint: And al-Shafi'i said: It is attached to accidental killing in its rulings because the Shariah regards him as a killer. Our (Hanafi) argument: The killing is non-existent from him in reality, so it is attached to it in terms of liability (daman), but remains in other rulings on the original principle: that although he sins by digging in other's property, he does not sin for the death as it is.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah addresses two categories: (1) actions that are treated like accidental killing (ma ajra majra al-khata) such as a sleeper rolling onto another and causing death. This gets the exact same ruling as qatl khata: kaffarah, diyah on aqilah, and deprivation of inheritance. (2) Killing by cause (qatl bi sabab) such as digging a well or placing a stone in someone else's property, causing a person to die. Here, the ruling is partial: diyah on aqilah is wajib because the person is transgressive and the act is a cause of death, so he is treated like a direct pusher. However, kaffarah is not wajib because the killing is not directly by his act, and he is not deprived of inheritance because the sin is in the transgression (digging in non-owned land), not in the death itself. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, holding that such cases are fully like qatl khata in all rulings because the Shariah considers him a killer. The Hanafi response is that the killing is not real (ma'dum haqiqatan) from him; it is attached only for liability (daman), not for other rulings like kaffarah and inheritance.

Key Terms
ما اجرى مجرى الخطاء (ma ajra majra al-khata): What is treated as accidental killing; actions that are not direct killing but get the same ruling as qatl khata (e.g., sleeper rolling onto someone).
قتل بسبب (qatl bi sabab): Killing by indirect cause, such as digging a well or placing a stone in someone else's property, leading to death.
سبب متعدی (sabab muta'addi): A transgressive cause: the act is unlawful and oversteps bounds (e.g., digging in another's land).
ضمان (daman): Liability for financial compensation, here diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person who digs a well in another's property and someone falls in and dies?
A) Full qatl khata ruling: kaffarah, diyah, and inheritance deprivation
B) Diyah on aqilah only; no kaffarah, no inheritance deprivation
C) No liability because it was not intentional
D) Qisas, because it is like direct killing

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, killing by cause (qatl bi sabab) only incurs diyah on the aqilah, not kaffarah or inheritance deprivation, because the killing is not directly attributable to the cause-maker in reality.

Killing with a Wooden Instrument: Diya, Not Qisas
Ruling that hitting with wood entitles diya, not qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person is killed by a blow from a wooden instrument, and explain why diya is due instead of qisas.

Core Idea
A blow with wood is quasi-intentional: diya is wajib, qisas is not.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: a killing with the wooden handle of a spade. The Hanafi school distinguishes between intentional murder (qatl 'amd) and quasi-intentional (shibh 'amd). The instrument used is a key factor. Here, the author rules that diya is obligatory to protect the victim's blood, but qisas is withheld because the act lacks full intentionality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the instrument
The act is striking with a wooden handle ('ud). Identify the object used in the killing.
The specific instrument matters for the legal category.
2
Determine the category of killing
Because wood is not typically a lethal weapon, this killing is classified as quasi-intentional (shibh 'amd), not intentional murder (qatl 'amd).
The Hanafi school uses instrument type to infer intent.
3
State the ruling
The ruling is that diya (blood money) is wajib, and qisas is not applicable.
Diya is obligatory to prevent the victim's blood from being wasted.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The reason diya is imposed is the existence of a protected soul (nafs ma'suma) and the prevention of qisas, so that the blood not be wasted.
The principle: any killing of a protected person must be compensated, but qisas requires full intent.
5
Note the authority weight
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, the relied-upon position of the school.
It is authoritative and mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما اذا ضربه بالعود فائماتجب الدية لوجود قتل النفس المعصومة وامتناع القصاص حتى لا يهدر الدم.
And as for when he strikes him with the wood, then diya becomes obligatory due to the existence of killing a protected soul and the prevention of qisas, so that the blood not be wasted.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This is a clear ruling: if the blow is with the wooden handle of the spade (or any wooden instrument), it is not considered intentional murder (qatl 'amd) that warrants qisas. Rather, it falls under quasi-intentional killing (shibh 'amd), for which the penalty is diya (blood money) on the killer's 'aqila (tribe). The reason is that wood is not typically a lethal weapon, so the act is not fully intentional. To prevent the victim's blood from going unpunished (la yuhdar al-dam), diya is imposed. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عود (‘ud): Wooden part of the spade; hitting leads to diya
دية (diya): Blood money payable for quasi-intentional killing
نفس معصومة (nafs ma‘suma): A protected life whose killing must be compensated

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qisas is due
B) Diya is due
C) No penalty
D) Kaffarah only

Key Takeaway
When killing occurs with a wooden instrument, the Hanafi school imposes diya (blood money) and does not apply qisas, because the act is quasi-intentional.

Diyah for a Muslim Killed in Mixed Battle or Enemy Ranks
Ruling on diyah with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah for a Muslim killed in a mixed battle versus in the enemy's ranks, and explain the proof from the hadith of al-Yaman.

Core Idea
A Muslim in the enemy's ranks loses immunity; diyah is not due.

The Hanafi school addresses a critical scenario: a Muslim is mistakenly killed by fellow Muslims during battle. Is diyah (blood money) obligatory? The answer depends on whether the Muslim was among the Muslim ranks or had joined the enemy. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the underlying principle of inviolability (ismah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) a Muslim killed in a mixed battle (intermingled forces) and (2) a Muslim killed while in the ranks of the polytheists. Note the difference in ruling.
Mixed battle = Muslims and non-Muslims are intermingled, making identification difficult.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For scenario 1: diyah is wajib. For scenario 2: diyah is not wajib. Memorize this core distinction.
3
Examine the proof: the incident of al-Yaman
The Prophet ﷺ ruled diyah when al-Yaman (father of Hudhayfah) was mistakenly killed during the Battle of the Trench. This establishes the principle that diyah is due when Muslims and non-Muslims are intermingled.
The incident is a specific case (qadiyah fi al-waqi') that scholars use to derive a general rule.
4
Analyse the qualification by the scholars
The scholars ('they said') qualify that the Prophet's ruling applies only when the forces are intermingled (mukhtaliteen). If the Muslim is in the enemy's rank, diyah is not due because his ismah is forfeited.
The commentary explains the rationale: the Muslim increases the enemy's numbers and therefore becomes one of them.
5
Connect to the hadith principle
The hadith 'Whoever increases the numbers of a people is one of them' is cited as the evidence for loss of immunity. Identify how the text uses this hadith to justify the ruling.
This hadith is used to establish that a Muslim who joins the enemy's rank loses the protection of ismah.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵
مٹھ بھیڑ میں کوئی مسلمان مارا جائے دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر کوئی مسلمان مشرکین کی صف میں ہو اور اسے قتل کر دیا جائے تو دیت واجب نہ ہوگی
ولما اختلفت سيوف المسلمين على اليمان ابي حذيفة قضى رسول الله عليه السلام بالدية قالوا انما. الدية اذا كانو امختلطين فان كان في صف المشركين لا تجب لسقوط عصمته بتكثير سواد هم قال عليه السلام من كثر سوا د قوم فهو منهم.

Book of Homicides. Page 58. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya vol 15. If a Muslim is killed in a mixed battle, diyah is obligatory; but if a Muslim is in the ranks of the polytheists and is killed, diyah is not obligatory. And when the swords of the Muslims differed (fell upon) al-Yaman, the father of Hudhayfah, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ruled diyah (to be paid). They said: Indeed, diyah (is due) when they are intermingled. But if he is in the rank of the polytheists, it is not obligatory because his immunity is forfeited by his increasing their numbers. He ﷺ said: 'Whoever increases the numbers of a people is one of them.' Translation: When the swords of the Muslims fell upon al-Yaman, father of Hudhayfah, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ruled diyah. The scholars said: Diyah will be obligatory when Muslims and non-Muslims are intermingled. So if a Muslim is in the polytheists' rank, diyah will not be obligatory because his immunity is forfeited due to his increasing their numbers. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever increases the numbers of a people is from them.' Commentary: During the Battle of the Trench, Hudhayfah's father al-Yaman was with women and children in a fort due to his old age. A desire for martyrdom overcame him and he descended. The Muslims thought he was a polytheist and attacked. Hudhayfah kept shouting that he was his father, but they did not hear until they killed him. The Prophet ﷺ ruled diyah. Thus, in such a situation, diyah is obligatory. The scholars said: The ruling of diyah applies when the battle has begun. But if a Muslim is in the polytheists' rank, killing him does not make diyah obligatory because this Muslim has become one who increases their numbers, so his immunity is forfeited, as the hadith says: 'Whoever causes an increase in a group's number will be counted among them.'
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage. The author begins by stating the general principle: diyah is due when a Muslim is killed in a mixed battle, but not when he is in the enemy's ranks. The proof is the incident of al-Yaman, the father of Hudhayfah, during the Battle of the Trench. The Prophet ﷺ ordered diyah for him because he was killed by mistake while the forces were intermingled. However, the scholars qualify this: the condition for diyah is that the Muslim should be among the Muslim ranks or at least not be fighting on the enemy's side. If a Muslim goes into the polytheists' ranks and is killed, no diyah is due because he has forfeited his ismah (inviolability) by swelling their numbers. The hadith 'Whoever increases the numbers of a people is one of them' is used as the proof. Thus, the ruling is based on the hadith and the principle of immunity (ismah).

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid for unlawful killing or injury
عصمت (ismah): Immunity, inviolability; the legal protection of life and property of a Muslim
مٹھ بھیڑ (mutth bheŗ): Mixed battle; hand-to-hand combat where Muslims and non-Muslims are intermingled

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is diyah not obligatory for killing a Muslim in battle?
A) When the Muslim is fighting on the side of the Muslims
B) When the Muslim is in the ranks of the polytheists
C) When the Muslim is a woman
D) When the battle is at sea

Key Takeaway
Diyah is obligatory for a Muslim killed in a mixed battle, but not if he was in the enemy's ranks due to loss of immunity (ismah) as per the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ.

Apportioning Diyah When Multiple Causes Lead to Death
Explains diyah division when self-wound, another's wound, and animal attacks cause death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of classifying causes by their legal effect (hādir/considered) to apportion diyah among multiple independent causes leading to death.

Core Idea
When multiple causes lead to death, diyah is apportioned according to the number of independent legal classes of causes.

Imagine a person inflicts a wound on himself, then another person wounds him, a lion attacks, and a snake bites, and he dies from the combination. Who bears responsibility for the diyah? The Hanafi school provides a precise method: classify each cause by whether it is legally irrelevant (hādir) in this world and the Hereafter, and then count the types. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its application to a real case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the causes
List all independent causes contributing to death: self-wound, wound by another (ajnabi), lion attack, snake bite.
2
Classify each cause by legal effect
Determine whether each cause is hādir (legally irrelevant) in this world and/or the Hereafter, or considered (mu'tabar) in one or both worlds.
Lion and snake: hādir in both worlds. Self-wound: hādir in this world, considered (sinful) in Hereafter. Ajnabi's wound: considered in both worlds.
3
Group causes into types
Causes with identical legal effect in both worlds are grouped as one type. Lion and snake share the same status (hādir in both), so they become one type. Self-wound is a second type. Ajnabi's wound is a third type.
4
Count the types and apportion diyah
The death is attributed equally to each type. Since there are three types, each type accounts for one-third of the death. The ajnabi's type is one-third, so he pays one-third of the full diyah.
5
Apply to the side dispute
The self-wound is considered in the Hereafter (sinful) – evidence: disagreement on funeral prayer for suicide. Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the mufta bihi position.
The relied-upon position: funeral prayer is performed.

Source Text

A person wounded his own head, then another person wounded that same head, then a snake bit him, then a lion attacked him, and finally he died in that wounded state. Is diyah obligatory or not? He (the author) said: Whoever wounds his own head, and a man wounds him, and a lion mauls him, and a snake bites him, and he dies from all that, then upon the stranger (the third party) is one-third of the diyah, because the action of the lion and the snake are one type, since they are wasted (hādir) in this world and the Hereafter. And his own action is wasted in this world but is considered in the Hereafter so that he will be sinful for it. Translation: The author said: The one who wounds his own head, and someone else wounds his head, and a lion mauls him, and a snake bites him, and he dies from all these causes, then upon the stranger is one-third of the diyah, because the actions of the lion and snake are one type, as they are wasted in this world and the Hereafter. And his own action is wasted in this world but is considered in the Hereafter, to the extent that he will be sinful. Commentary: Zayd wounded his own head, Khalid also wounded his head, a lion mauled Zayd, and a snake bit him. He died from all these causes. How much diyah is obligatory upon Khalid? It is said: one-third diyah is obligatory upon Khalid, because he died from three causes, and Khalid's action is one-third of those causes, so the diyah is one-third. Question: How is Khalid's action one-third of the cause? Answer: Because the actions of the lion and snake become one type, so they count as one action; one action is Zayd's own; and one action is Khalid's. So Khalid's action is one-third of the causes. Question: Why are the actions of the lion and snake one type and not separate? Answer: The actions of the lion and snake are wasted (hādir) in this world and the Hereafter, meaning there will be no accountability for the lion or snake here or in the Hereafter. So they become one type. Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter (he will be sinful) but wasted in this world. Khalid's action is considered in this world and the Hereafter. Therefore Zayd's action cannot be joined with the lion/snake nor with Khalid's action. Hence Khalid's action becomes one-third of the total actions, so one-third of the diyah is imposed on him. Question: What is the proof that Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter? Answer: Zayd becomes sinful because of it, and because of that sin, the scholars differed whether the funeral prayer should be performed over him or not. And that is because he is sinful. Thus they say: Statements of the Jurists: In al-Nawadir: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he is washed and prayed upon; according to Abu Yusuf, he is washed but not prayed upon. In Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, the difference of the scholars regarding the prayer is mentioned as we have written in Kitab al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. Translation: In al-Nawadir, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), he is washed and the funeral prayer is performed; according to Abu Yusuf, he is washed but not prayed upon. In Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, the difference of scholars about the prayer is mentioned, as the author has written in his book al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. Commentary: The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say that a suicide should be washed and prayed upon; Abu Yusuf says he should be washed but not prayed upon. The relied-upon opinion is that the prayer is performed and he is washed. For details, see Hawashi, page 584, vol. 1. The action of the stranger is considered in this world and the Hereafter. Then it (Zayd's action) is not absolutely wasted, and it becomes a second type. The stranger's action is considered in this world and the Hereafter. So the actions become three types. The person died from three actions, so the death is from each action by one-third. So one-third diyah is obligatory upon him. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on the division of diyah when multiple independent causes contribute to death. The scenario: a man (Zayd) wounds his own head, another man (Khalid) wounds him, a lion mauls him, and a snake bites him. He dies from the combination. The ruling: Khalid (the 'ajnabī) pays one-third of the full diyah. The reasoning is based on classifying the causes into three types: (1) the actions of the lion and snake together count as one type because they are both 'hādir' (legally irrelevant) in this world and the Hereafter—no one is liable for them. (2) Zayd's own action is hādir in this world (no worldly liability) but is considered in the Hereafter (he is sinful, so it counts for his accountability). (3) Khalid's action is considered in both worlds (he is liable for the wound). Therefore, Khalid's action is one of three equal types, so he bears one-third of the diyah. The passage also includes a useful side-discussion: the fact that Zayd's self-wound is sinful in the Hereafter is proven by the disagreement among scholars about whether to perform the funeral prayer over a suicide. This disagreement is cited from al-Nawadir and Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir. The mufta bihi position (according to the text) is that the prayer is performed and the person is washed, siding with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Thus, the self-wound is indeed considered in the Hereafter (it causes sin), which justifies treating it as a separate type.

Key Terms
ہدر (hādir): Wasted; legally irrelevant; no liability or reward in this world or the Hereafter.
اجنبی (ajnabī): A stranger; the third party (Khalid) who is not the victim nor the self-inflictor.
دیت (diyah): Blood money; compensation for causing death or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of multiple causes (self-wound, another's wound, lion, snake), why does the ajnabi pay one-third of the diyah?
A) Because the ajnabi's wound caused one-third of the damage
B) Because the causes are classified into three legal types, and the ajnabi's type is one-third
C) Because the lion and snake cancel each other out
D) Because the victim's own wound reduces the liability

Key Takeaway
When multiple causes lead to death, diyah is apportioned according to the number of independent legal classes of causes.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Diyah for Defensive Killing of Minors, Insane, or Animals
Dispute on diyah for killing insane/minor/animal attacker

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on diyah for killing a minor/insane/animal attacker and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Lack of sound free will means the attacker's inviolability remains, so diyah is due even in self-defense.

This lesson explores a nuanced inter-madhhab dispute: when a sane person kills an attacker who is a minor, insane, or an animal, is diyah (blood money) obligatory? The Hanafi school (Tarafayn) insists yes, because the attacker lacks sound free will and remains inviolable. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that self-defense exempts the killer from any liability, analogizing to a sane adult attacker who forfeits his own sanctity. Imam Abu Yusuf adds a middle position. We will analyze each proof and understand why the Hanafi view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Tarafayn)
Identify the relied-upon Hanafi ruling: diyah is wajib on the killer for killing any inviolable being (minor, insane, animal) even in self-defense.
The killer's act is mubah (permissible) to repel evil, but inviolability is not dropped.
2
Identify the opposing views
Two opposing views: 1) Al-Shafi'i: no diyah in any case. 2) Abu Yusuf: diyah for animal only, not for human attacker.
Abu Yusuf's position is intra-Hanafi; the Tarafayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject it.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof (qiyas)
Al-Shafi'i analogizes the insane/minor to a sane adult brandishing a weapon; the killer acts in self-defense, so no liability. Also compares the killer to a coerced person (mukrah).
The key analogy: if killing a sane adult attacker exempts, so should killing an insane one.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the analogy fails because a sane adult has sound free will, so his attack drops his own inviolability. Minors, insane, and animals lack sound free will; their inviolability remains despite their action.
The factor is ikhtiyar sahih (sound free will), not the nature of the attacker's inviolability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Shafi'i, no financial liability; under Hanafi, diyah or compensation is due from the killer's own wealth.
This affects the killer's financial responsibility in self-defense cases.

ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور اگر مجنون نے اپنے غیر پر ہتھیار سونت لیا پس مشہور علیہ نے اس کو عمد اقتل کر دیا تو قاتل پر اس کے مال میں دیت واجب ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاتل پر کچھ نہیں ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر بچہ اور چوپایہ ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ چوپایہ میں ضمان واجب ہے اور بچہ اور مجنون میں واجب نہیں ہے۔ شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاتل نے اس کو اپنے نفس کی جانب سے مدافعت کی عرض سے قتل کیا ہے تو اس کو شاہر بالغ پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور اس لئے کہ قاتل مقتول کے قتل کے فعل سے ابھارا گیا ہے تو قاتل مکرہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح کسی مجنون اور پاگل نے یا بچہ نے زید پر تلوار وغیرہ کھینچ لی یا زید پر پھینے نے مثلا حملہ کر دیا جس کی وجہ سے زید نے ان کو قتل کر کے اپنی جان بچائی تو زید پر قصاص تو بالاتفاق کسی صورت میں نہیں ہے اب رہی بات دیت کی اس میں اختلاف ہے بالفاظ دیگر اس میں تین قول ہیں
1- طرفین کا قول کہ دیت اور بھینسے کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
2- قول شافعی یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی صورت میں بھی دیت اور ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
3- قول ابو یوسف یہ ہے کہ مجنون اور بچہ کی صورت میں دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ البتہ بھینس کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل شافعی ۔ یہ ہے کہ اگر تلوار سونچنے والا بالغ ہوتا اور قاتل اس کو قتل کرتا تو دیت واجب نہ ہوتی ایسے ہی یہاں بھی دیت واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ دونوں صورتوں میں زید کا مقصد اپنی حفاظت ہے اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ مجنون وغیرہ نے ہی قاتل کو قتل پر ابھارا ہے۔ اگر وہ پیش قدمی نہ کرتے تو یہ قتل نہ کرتا۔ اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے کہ زید نے خالد کے سینے پر ریوالور لگا دیا کہ بکر کو گولی مار، ورنہ میں تجھے ختم کروں گا۔ لہذا خالد نے بکر پر گولی چلا دی جس سے بکر مر گیا تو خالد پر جو مکرہ ہے کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا یہ امام شافعی کی دلیل ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
في الجملة
ولابي يوسف ان فعل الدابة غير معتبر اصلاحتى لو تحقق لا يوجب الضمان اما فعلهما معتبر حتى لو حققاه يجب عليهما الضمان وكذا عصمتهما لحقهما وعصمة الدابة لحق ما لكها فكان فعلهما مسقطا للعصمه دون فعل الدابة
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چوپایہ کا فعل بالکل غیر معتبر ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر چوپایہ کا فعل متفق ہو جا تا تو وہ ضمان کو واجب نہ کرتا بہر حال ان دونوں کا فعل فی الجملہ معتبر ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر یہ دونوں اس فعل کو تحقیق کر دیتے تو ان دونوں پر ضمان واجب ہوتا اور ایسے ہی ان دونوں کی عصمت ان دونوں کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اور چوپایہ کی عصمت اس کے مالک کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے تو ان دونوں کا فعل عصمت کو ساقط کرنے والا ہوگا نہ کہ چوپایہ کا فعل ۔
تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ چوپایہ اور مجنون و بچہ میں فرق ہے یعنی چوپایہ کا فعل غیر معتبر ہے اور بچہ اور مجنون کا فعل فی الجملہ معتبر ہے اور دوسرا فرق یہ ہے کہ مجنون اور بچہ کی عصمت خود ان کی ذاتی ہے اور ان دونوں کا حق ہے اور چوپایہ کی عصمت ذاتی نہیں بلکہ اس کے مالک کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے۔ جب یہ فرق واضح ہو گیا تو چوپایہ کے فعل نہ ہونے کے درجہ میں ہے لہذا چوپایہ کے فعل سے چوپایہ کی عصمت ساقط نہ ہوگی اور جب عصمت ساقط نہ ہوگی تو اس کو قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے ضمان قیمت واجب ہوگا۔ اور بچہ اور مجنون کا فعل فی الجملہ معتبر ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کے فعل سے ان کی عصمت کو ساقط شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور جب عصمت ساقط ہوگئی تو پھر قتل کا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور ان دونوں کا فعل معتبر ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ کسی کو قتل کر دیں تو ان پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ مکلف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ان سے قصاص واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
حضرات طرفین کی دلیل
و لنا انه قتل شخصا معصوما او اتلف ما لا معصوما حقا للمالك وفعل الدابة لا يصلح مسقطا وكذا فعلهما و ان كانت عصمتهما حقهما لعدم اختيار صحيح ولهذا لا يجب القصاص بتحقق الفعل منهما بخلاف العاقل البالغ لان له اختيارا صحيحا وانما لا يجب القصاص لوجود المباح وهو دفع الشر فتجب الدية
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے معصوم شخص کو قتل کیا ہے یا ایسے مال کو تلف کیا ہے جو حق مالک کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے اور چوپایہ کا فعل مسقط ( عصمت) بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا اور ایسے ہی ان دونوں کا فعل اگر چہ ان دونوں کی عصمت ان دونوں کا حق ہے اختیار صحیح نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس وجہ سے ان دونوں سے فعل کے تحقق کی وجہ سے قصاص واجب نہیں ہوتا بخلاف عاقل بالغ کے اس لئے کہ اس کے لئے اختیار صحیح ہے اور قصاص واجب نہیں ہوتا مباح کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور مباح شر کو دور کرنا ہے تو دیت واجب ہوگی ۔
تشریح یہ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں دیت اور ضمان قیمت واجب ہے کیونکہ اول صورت میں قاتل نے معصوم الدم شخص کو قتل کیا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں ایسا مال تلف کیا ہے جو حق مالک کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے۔ اور اے ابو یوسف یہ کیا فرمایا کہ چوپایہ کا فعل مسقط عصمت نہیں اور مجنون اور بچہ کا فعل عصمت کو ساقط کرنے والا ہے۔ یہ صحیح نہیں جبکہ دونوں کا فعل غیر مسقط ہے چوپایہ کا تو ظاہر ہے اور مجنون اور بچہ کا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں اختیار صحیح نہیں ہے اور اختیار صحیح نہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر بچہ اور مجنون کسی کو قتل کر دیں تو قصاص واجب نہیں ہوگا وہ دوسری بات ہے کہ ان دونوں کی عصمت اپنا حق ہے اور چوپایہ کی عصمت حق مالک کی وجہ سے ہے لیکن اختیار صحیح نہ ہونے میں سب برابر ہیں ۔ اور رہا بالغ جس نے تلوار سونت لی تھی اور اس کو قتل کر دیا گیا تھا تو قاتل پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوا تھا کیونکہ اس بالغ میں اختیار صحیح موجود ہے۔
Book of Homicide. The minor and the insane: According to al-Shafi'i, he (the killer) killed him defending himself, so he is analogized to the adult who brandishes (a weapon), and because he is made bear the killing by his (the victim's) action, so he resembles the coerced one. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If an insane person brandished a weapon at someone else, then the well-known one (the person attacked) killed him intentionally, then diyah is obligatory on the killer from his wealth. Al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is on the killer. And on this same difference is the child and the animal. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that for the animal, compensation is obligatory, and for the child and the insane, it is not. The proof of al-Shafi'i is that the killer killed him in defense of himself, so he is analogized to the adult brandisher, and because the killer was provoked by the action of the killed one, so the killer resembles the coerced one. Explanation: If an insane or mad person or a child drew a sword against Zayd, or attacked him, so Zayd killed them to save his life, then qisas is not obligatory on Zayd by consensus. Now regarding diyah, there is disagreement. In other words, there are three opinions: 1) The opinion of the two sides (Tarafayn) that diyah and the price of the buffalo are obligatory. 2) The opinion of al-Shafi'i that in any of these cases, diyah or compensation is not obligatory. 3) The opinion of Abu Yusuf that in the case of the insane and the child, diyah is not obligatory; but in the case of the buffalo, its price as compensation is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i's proof: If the one who brandished the sword were an adult and the killer killed him, diyah would not be obligatory; likewise here, diyah is not obligatory because in both cases Zayd's intention is self-preservation, and because the insane etc. provoked the killer to kill. If they had not initiated, he would not have killed. An example: Zayd put a revolver on Khalid's chest and said: Shoot Bakr or I will kill you. So Khalid shot Bakr and killed him, then nothing is obligatory on Khalid because he is coerced. This is al-Shafi'i's proof. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf: In summary, and for Abu Yusuf: The action of the animal is completely disregarded; even if it occurs, it does not necessitate compensation. But the action of these two (child and insane) is somewhat regarded; even if they commit the action, compensation becomes obligatory on them. Likewise, their inviolability (isma) is for their own right, while the inviolability of the animal is for the right of its owner. So their action drops inviolability, not the animal's action. Translation: Abu Yusuf's proof is that the action of the animal is completely disregarded; even if the animal's action occurs, it does not make compensation obligatory. However, the action of these two is somewhat regarded; even if they actualize the action, compensation becomes obligatory on them. Similarly, their inviolability is for their own right, and the animal's inviolability is for the right of its owner. So their action will drop inviolability, not the animal's action. Explanation: This is Abu Yusuf's proof, the gist of which is that there is a difference between the animal and the insane/child: the animal's action is disregarded, while the child's and insane's action is somewhat regarded. A second difference is that the inviolability of the insane and child is personal to them and their right, while the animal's inviolability is not personal but due to the right of its owner. When this difference is clear, the animal's action is like non-existence, so the animal's action does not drop its inviolability. Since inviolability is not dropped, killing it incurs compensation of its price. For the child and insane, because their action is somewhat regarded, their action is considered to drop their inviolability, so no compensation is due for killing them. The proof that their action is regarded is that if they kill someone, compensation is obligatory on them, though due to lack of legal capacity, qisas is not obligatory. The proof of the respected two sides (Tarafayn): And we have: He killed an inviolable person or destroyed inviolable property that is inviolable due to the right of the owner. The action of the animal is not fit to drop inviolability, nor is their action (the child/insane) even though their inviolability is their right, due to lack of sound free will. This is why qisas is not obligatory from them despite the occurrence of the action, unlike the sane adult, because he has sound free will. Qisas is not obligatory only due to the presence of a permissible act, which is repelling evil. So diyah is obligatory. Translation: Our proof is that he killed an inviolable person or destroyed property that is inviolable due to the owner's right. The action of the animal does not have the capacity to drop inviolability, and likewise their action, even though their inviolability is their right, due to lack of sound free will. For this reason, qisas is not obligatory from them despite the action being committed, unlike the sane adult, because he has sound free will. Qisas is not obligatory only due to the presence of a permissible act, and the permissible act is repelling evil, so diyah is obligatory. Explanation: This is the proof of the respected two sides that in all these cases diyah and compensation of price are obligatory because in the first case the killer killed an inviolable blood person, and in the second case he destroyed property that is inviolable due to the owner's right. And O Abu Yusuf, what you said that the animal's action does not drop inviolability and the child/insane's action drops inviolability is incorrect, because both actions are non-dropping: the animal's action is obviously, and the child/insane's because they lack sound free will. The proof that they lack sound free will is that if the child or insane kills someone, qisas is not obligatory. It is another matter that their inviolability is their own right and the animal's inviolability is due to the owner's right, but in lacking sound free will they are equal. As for the adult who brandished the sword and was killed, compensation was not obligatory on the killer because that adult had sound free will.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses a dispute regarding diyah (blood money) when a person kills a minor, an insane person, or an animal that is attacking him. The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i, with an additional intra-Hanafi difference from Imam Abu Yusuf. The relied-upon Hanafi position (Tarafayn, i.e., the two sides—Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) imposes diyah in all cases, including for killing an animal. The passage first quotes Imam Muhammad's statement from al-Jami' al-Saghir: if an insane person brandishes a weapon and is killed in self-defense, diyah is obligatory on the killer from his own wealth. Al-Shafi'i holds that no compensation is due because the killer acted in defense, analogizing the insane attacker to a sane adult who would forfeit his sanctity by attacking. Abu Yusuf distinguishes between animals (compensation due) and humans (no compensation). The Hanafi response argues that the lack of sound free will (ikhtiyar sahih) in the insane, minor, and animal means their actions cannot drop the inviolability of their own persons or property; thus, killing them still incurs diyah. The commentary stresses that the key factor is the absence of sound free will, not the nature of the attacker's inviolability. The passage also refutes Abu Yusuf's reasoning by asserting that all three classes lack sound free will, so their actions are equally incapable of dropping inviolability.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money or compensation paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of homicide or injury where qisas is not applicable.
عصمت (isma): Inviolability or sanctity that protects a person or property from being lawfully harmed without liability.
اختیار صحیح (ikhtiyar sahih): Sound free will; the capacity for deliberate choice that makes one legally accountable.
مکره (mukrah): A person compelled under threat to perform an act; such compulsion may remove liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Tarafayn), what is the ruling when a sane person kills an insane person who is attacking him with a sword?
A) Qisas is obligatory on the killer.
B) No diyah or compensation is due.
C) Diyah is obligatory on the killer from his own wealth.
D) Only if the insane person is a Muslim, diyah is due.

Key Takeaway
The absence of sound free will (ikhtiyar sahih) prevents the attacker's inviolability from being dropped, so diyah remains wajib on the defender even in self-defense.
