Payment Period for Diyah When One Heir Forgives: Hanafi and Zufar's Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah payment period for partial forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that partial diyah is mu'ajjal in three years and distinguish it from Imam Zufar's position of two years by analyzing the qiyas employed by each side.

Core Idea
Partial diyah follows full diyah's three-year deferment because it is part of the blood price, not a limb compensation.

When qisas is waived by one of two heirs, the diyah payable to the other heir is half the full diyah. A key question arises: should this half-diyah follow the payment period of full diyah (three years) or of arsh for a hand (two years)? Imam Zufar argued for two years based on the equal amount, but the majority Hanafi position, led by Abu Hanifa, held that it remains as diyah and thus is due in three years. This lesson unpacks the qiyas behind each view and the rationale for the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of the dispute
Two heirs of a murder victim; one forgives qisas; the surviving heir claims half diyah. The ruling hinges on whether this half-diyah is classified as diyah or as arsh for the purpose of payment period.
2
State Zufar's position and his qiyas
Zufar says two years; he analogizes half diyah to arsh for a hand (also half diyah) because the amount is equal.
The arsh for a hand in accidental cutting is half diyah and due in two years.
3
State the Hanafi majority position and their qiyas
Three years; they analogize to full diyah because half diyah is part of the blood price (badal al-dam), not a limb price.
Full diyah for intentional killing when forgiven is mu'ajjal in three years.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: the correct analogy is to diyah, not arsh, because the obligation arises from the taking of life (dam) not from injury to a limb (taraf). The whole is three years, so the part follows.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if Zufar's view were taken, the heir would receive full payment in two years; in the Hanafi view, in three annual installments.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (and the majority) and Imam Zufar regarding the payment period of diyah when qisas is partially forgiven. The context: two heirs share the right to qisas; one forgives; qisas falls and converts to diyah of half the full diyah. The question is: should this half-diyah be paid in three years (like full diyah) or in two years (like arsh for limb injuries)? The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that it is paid in three years because it is part of the blood price (badal al-dam). The full diyah is deferred to three years, so its part follows the same rule. Zufar analogizes it to arsh (compensation for limbs) because the amount is half diyah, similar to the arsh for a hand (half diyah), which is paid in two years. The text provides the Hanafi response: diyah should be analogized to diyah, not to arsh, because the nature of the obligation is blood money, not limb compensation. The passage is incomplete at the end, but the reasoning is clear: the Hanafi position is three years; Zufar's position is two years.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money payable for homicide or bodily harm when qisas is not applied; full diyah is 100 camels or equivalent.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injuries to limbs or body parts, assessed as a fraction of diyah.
مؤجل (mu'ajjal): Deferred payment; payable in installments over a period.

Compensation for Healed vs. Fatal Lashes: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for healed lashes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding compensation for healed wounds that leave no trace, and apply the ruling to a scenario where some injuries are fatal and others heal.

Core Idea
Healed wounds without trace incur no financial compensation per Abu Hanifa, only ta'zir.

When multiple blows cause both recoverable and fatal injuries, the Hanafi school has an internal dispute. The basic principle from Abu Hanifa is that a healed wound with no lasting trace does not require financial compensation (arsh). But Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad offer alternative views. In this lesson, we unpack the scenario and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the facts: 100 lashes, victim recovers from 90, dies from 10. Note which lashes healed and which caused death.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's principle
According to Abu Hanifa, healed wounds with no trace do not incur arsh or diyah. So only the fatal 10 incur one diyah. The 90 are considered only for ta'zir.
Principle: wound that heals without effect = no compensation.
3
Compare with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf says hukumat al-'adl is due for the healed wounds. This is an equitable assessment based on the decrease in value of the victim (e.g., if a slave).
4
Compare with Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad says the offender must pay the physician's fee for treating the healed wounds.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, as it is the principle (asl) and the other views are narrations. Confirm from the commentary.

سو کوڑے کسی کو مارے نوے میں تندرست تھا آخری دس سے مر گیا تو دیت کا حکم
قال ومن ضرب رجلا مائة سوط فبرئ من تسعين ومات من عشرة ففيه دية واحدة لانه لما برأ من تلك التسعين لا تبقى معتبرة فى حق الارش وان بقيت معتبرة في حق التعزير فبقى الاعتبار للعشرة وكذلك كل جراحة اندملت ولم يبق لها اثر على اصل ابي حنيفة وعن أبي يوسف فى مثله حكومة عدل وعن محمد انه تجب اجرة الطبيب
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کو سو کوڑے مارے پس وہ نوے سے اچھا ہو گیا اور آخر دس سے مر گیا تو اس میں ایک دیت ہے اس لئے کہ وہ جب کہ نوے سے اچھا ہو گیا تو وہ نوے ارش کے حق میں معتبر بن کر باقی نہیں رہے اگر چہ تعزیر کے حق میں معتبر باقی ہیں تو صرف دس کا اعتبار باقی رہا اور ایسے ہی ہر زخم جو بھر گیا ہو اور اس کا کوئی اثر باقی نہ رہا ہو۔ ابوحنیفہ کی اصل پر اور اس کے مثل میں ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ حکومت عدل ہے اور محمد سے منقول ہے کہ طبیب کی اجرت واجب ہے۔
تشریح زید نے خالد کو ظلماً ناحق سو کوڑے مارے ان میں سے مثلاً نوے کمر پر مارے اور دس سر پر مارے اولاً نوے مارنے کی وجہ سے وہ نہیں مرا بلکہ وہ ٹھیک ہو گیا اور آخری دس کی وجہ سے وہ مر گیا تو صرف آخری دس کوڑے جن سے وہ مرا ہے اسی کا ضمان یعنی دیت واجب ہوگی اور پہلے نوے کوڑوں کا کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔

اور امام محمد سے منقول ہے کہ اس صورت میں زخم لگانے والے پر علاج معالجہ کا صرفہ واجب ہوگا۔
The ruling on someone who strikes another with a hundred lashes, he recovers from ninety and dies from ten: he owes one diyah. Because when he recovered from the ninety, they are no longer considered in regard to compensation (arsh), even though they remain considered in regard to discretionary punishment (ta'zir). So only the ten are considered. Likewise, every wound that healed and left no trace is like this according to the principle of Abu Hanifa. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that in such a case there is hukumat al-'adl (equitable assessment), and from Muhammad that the physician's fee is obligatory. Translation: Muhammad (the author of the matn) said: 'And whoever strikes a person with a hundred lashes, and he recovers from ninety and dies from ten, then on him is one diyah, because when he recovered from those ninety, they are no longer considered in regard to arsh, even though they remain considered in regard to ta'zir. So only the ten are considered. Likewise, every wound that healed and left no trace, according to Abu Hanifa's principle. And from Abu Yusuf regarding the like of this is hukumat al-'adl, and from Muhammad that the physician's fee is obligatory.' Explanation: Zayd unjustly struck Khalid a hundred lashes. For example, ninety on the back and ten on the head. The ninety did not cause death; he recovered. Then the ten caused death. So only the last ten lashes that caused death have liability, i.e., diyah is due. The first ninety lashes have no liability because no effect remained. However, they are considered for ta'zir: the judge may discipline the offender. Similarly, every wound that healed and left no trace has the same ruling according to Abu Hanifa: no compensation is due. From Abu Yusuf, hukumat al-'adl is due: for example, if the victim were a slave, his value without the wound would be one thousand, with the wound eight hundred, so two hundred dirhams are due. From Muhammad, the cost of medical treatment is due.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding multiple injuries where some heal and others cause death. The matn states that if a person strikes another a hundred lashes, the victim recovers from ninety but dies from ten, only one diyah is due for the fatal ten. The reason is that the ninety lashes healed and left no trace, so they are not considered for financial compensation (arsh). They are, however, considered for discretionary punishment (ta'zir), meaning the judge may punish the offender for the non-fatal lashes. Then the text mentions an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa's principle holds that no compensation is due for a wound that heals without trace. Imam Abu Yusuf says hukumat al-'adl is due, which is an equitable assessment based on the decrease in value of the victim (if a slave). Imam Muhammad says the cost of the physician's treatment is obligatory. The commentary clarifies that according to Abu Hanifa, no liability for the healed lashes; only the fatal ones matter. Abu Yusuf's hukumat al-'adl is illustrated by comparing the value of a slave before and after the wound. Muhammad's view is that the offender must pay for medical expenses.

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): Financial compensation for a wound or injury, distinct from full diyah.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-'adl): An equitable assessment of compensation based on the decrease in value caused by the injury, typically applied when fixed arsh is not specified.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment inflicted by the judge for offenses that have no fixed hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Hukumat al-'adl.
C) No financial compensation (only ta'zir).
D) Cost of physician.

Key Takeaway
Healed wounds without a lasting trace incur no financial compensation (arsh) in the Hanafi school according to Abu Hanifa; they only warrant discretionary punishment (ta'zir).

Forgiveness of Injury vs. Consequences: Diyah Liability
States ruling on diyah when victim forgives cutting then dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between forgiveness limited to the injury and forgiveness extending to consequences, and state the resulting diyah liability and estate limitations.

Core Idea
Forgiveness of an injury does not extend to death unless explicitly stated; otherwise, diyah is due.

When a person forgives a bodily injury but later dies from it, the scope of their forgiveness determines whether blood money (diyah) is owed. The Hanafi ruling draws a precise distinction between forgiving the act itself and forgiving all consequences. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its financial implications for the victim's estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of forgiveness
Read the passage and list the two scenarios: (1) forgiveness only of the cutting, (2) forgiveness of the cutting and 'what arises from it' (i.e., consequences including death).
These are explicitly contrasted in the text.
2
Determine the outcome for diyah
For each scenario, state whether diyah is due and why. In the first, diyah is due because death was not forgiven; in the second, no diyah because death was included in the forgiveness.
The passage says 'this is forgiveness of the soul'.
3
Analyze the financial limitation
When forgiveness includes the soul, note that if the cutting was accidental, the forgiveness is effective only from one-third of the victim's estate (as a will). If intentional, it is effective from the entire estate.
This distinction is based on whether the act was accidental or intentional.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Use the Zayd and Khalid illustration: Zayd cuts Khalid's hand (intentionally or accidentally), Khalid forgives the cut only, then dies. Trace why diyah is due despite the forgiveness.
The commentary provides this example.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن قطع يد رجل فعفا المقطوعة يده عن القطع ثم مات من ذلك فعلى القاطع الدية في ماله وان عفا عن القطع وما يحدث منه ثم مات من ذلك فهو عفو عن النفس ثم ان كان خطا فهو من الثلث وان كان عمدا فهو من ماله وهذا فصل ابي حنيفة
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس شخص نے کسی کا ہاتھ کاٹا پس جس کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا ہے اس نے قطع کو معاف کردیا پھر وہ اس قطع کی وجہ سے مرگیا تو قاطع پر دیت واجب ہے۔ قاطع کے مال میں اور اگر مقطوع الید نے قطع اور جو قطع سے پیدا ہو اس کو معاف کر دیا پھر وہ اس قطع کی وجہ سے مر گیا تو یہ نفس کو معاف کر دینا ہے پھر اگر قطع خطاء ہو تو یہ معافی ثلث مال سے ہوگی اور اگر قطع عمدہ ہو تو معافی پورے مال سے ہوگی اور یہ فصل ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔
تشریح زید نے خطاء یا عمداً خالد کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا اور خالد بڑا سخی شخص تھا اس نے اس قطع کو معاف کر دیا تو معاف ہو گیا لہذا ہاتھ کا قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا اور نہ ہاتھ کی دیت واجب ہوگی۔ لیکن اگر اس ہاتھ کاٹنے کی وجہ سے خالد مر گیا تو اب پہلی معافی ختم ہو گئی کیونکہ اس نے قطع کو معاف کیا تھا۔ اور یہ مسئلہ قتل کا ہو گیا لہذا زید کے اوپر دیت واجب ہوگی قطع عمدہ ہو تب بھی اور خطا ہو تب بھی۔ لیکن اگر خالد نے اس طرح معاف کیا ہو کہ میں نے قطع کو معاف کیا اور قطع سے پیدا ہونے والی چیز کو بھی معاف کیا تو اس صورت میں اگر مر جائے تو قتل بھی معاف ہو جائے گا۔
He said: Whoever cuts off the hand of a man, then the one whose hand is cut off forgives the cutting, then dies from that, then the cutter is liable for diyah from his property. And if he forgives the cutting and what arises from it, then dies from that, then it is forgiveness of the soul. Then if the cutting was accidental, it is from one-third of the property; and if intentional, it is from the entire property. And this is the ruling of Abu Hanifa.
Translation: Muhammad said: Whoever cuts off someone's hand, then the person whose hand is cut off forgives the cutting, then he dies from that cutting, then the cutter is liable for diyah from his property. And if the one whose hand is cut off forgives both the cutting and whatever arises from it, then he dies from that cutting, then this is forgiveness of the soul. Then if the cutting was accidental, this forgiveness is effective from one-third of the property; and if it was intentional, the forgiveness is from all of his property. And this is the ruling of Abu Hanifa.
Explanation: Zayd cuts off Khalid's hand, accidentally or intentionally. Khalid is a generous person; he forgives the cutting, so it is forgiven. Hence, no qisas for the hand is due, nor is the diyah for the hand due. But if Khalid dies from this cutting, the first forgiveness ceases because he only forgave the cutting, not the death. This becomes a case of homicide; so Zayd is liable for diyah, whether the cutting was intentional or accidental. However, if Khalid forgave in the manner: 'I forgive the cutting and also what arises from it', then if he dies, the death is also forgiven, and Zayd incurs no liability.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the effect of forgiving a bodily injury that later causes death. The ruling distinguishes between two types of forgiveness. If the victim forgives only the cutting of the hand, that forgiveness applies only to the hand; it does not cover the potential death resulting from the injury. Therefore, if the victim dies from that injury, the perpetrator must pay diyah (blood money) for the death. However, if the victim explicitly forgives both the cutting and 'what arises from it' (i.e., any future death), then that forgiveness extends to the soul/self, and no diyah is due for the death. Additionally, the ruling specifies financial implications: if the cutting was accidental, the forgiveness of the soul (when made by a free person) is effective only from one-third of the victim's estate, as it is considered a will (wasiyyah). If the cutting was intentional, the forgiveness is valid from the entire estate, because intentionally causing harm that leads to death can be forgiven as part of the victim's rights. The commentary illustrates with an example of Zayd and Khalid, emphasizing that forgiveness of the hand does not automatically forgive the death, but explicit broader forgiveness does.

Key Terms
عفو (afw): Forgiveness or remission of a legal right, such as qisas or financial compensation.
دية (diyah): Blood money payable to the heirs of a person killed; here, it is for death resulting from the cutting.
ثلث مال (thuluth mal): One-third of the victim's estate; the maximum that can be disposed of by will or donation that is effective against heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a victim forgives the cutting of his hand and later dies from it, which of the following is true?
A) No diyah because the cut was forgiven.
B) Diyah is due because death was not forgiven.
C) Only diyah for the hand is due, not for death.
D) The perpetrator is liable for qisas.

Key Takeaway
Forgiveness of an injury does not automatically extend to death; explicit inclusion is required to waive diyah for homicide.

Diyat — Blood Money
advanced
12 min
Marriage with Diyah in Accidental Cutting and Marad al-Mawt
Ruling on marriage using diyah as mahr with marad al-mawt implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on marriage using diyah as mahr in accidental injury, including the deduction of mahr mithl from the 'aqila's liability and the treatment of excess as a wasiyyah limited to one-third of the estate due to marad al-mawt.

Core Idea
When a terminally ill man marries using diyah as mahr, the mahr mithl is valid from the entire estate; any excess is a wasiyyah limited to one-third.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from Al-Hidayah: a woman accidentally cuts a man's hand, and he marries her in exchange for the diyah (blood money) he is owed. The passage navigates the intersection of diyat (injuries), marriage contracts, and the restrictions of a death-illness (marad al-mawt). You will learn how the Hanafi school balances these rules and why the mahr mithl is deducted from the diyah owed by the 'aqila, with any surplus treated as a bequest (wasiyyah) that is effective only within one-third of the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and key facts
The case: a woman accidentally cuts a man's hand, so the 'aqila owe diyah to the man. Before he dies of his (unrelated) terminal illness, he marries the woman and sets the diyah as her mahr. Determine the amounts: diyah = 10,000 dirhams, mahr mithl = 7,000 dirhams.
Note the distinction from intentional cutting: diyah is property, so it can serve as mahr.
2
Apply the marad al-mawt rules
The husband is terminally ill. According to Hanafi fiqh, a terminally ill patient's transactions are valid from the entire estate only if they are primary needs (hawa'ij asliyyah). Marriage is a primary need, so the mahr mithl (7,000) is valid from the whole estate. Any excess over mahr mithl is a gift (muhabah) and counts as a wasiyyah, effective only within one-third of the estate.
The excess (3,000) is a disposition in favor of the 'aqila, who are not heirs but can receive a bequest.
3
Deduct mahr mithl from the 'aqila's liability
The 'aqila owe diyah of 10,000 to the husband. However, since the husband set that diyah as the mahr, the woman is entitled to mahr mithl (7,000). But the 'aqila pay diyah on behalf of the woman (the culprit), so they effectively pay her mahr. Thus, the mahr mithl is lifted from the 'aqila; they do not pay it separately. The remaining 3,000 is the excess.
The principle: the woman cannot collect diyah from the 'aqila and also demand her mahr from the husband, as the 'aqila bear liability for her act.
4
Determine the validity of the excess as a wasiyyah
The excess of 3,000 dirhams is a gift from the terminally ill husband to the 'aqila. It is treated as a wasiyyah (bequest) and is only valid within one-third of the estate. Compute: if the estate is at least 9,000 dirhams (three times the excess), the full 3,000 is given to the 'aqila. If the estate is smaller, only one-third of the estate is given, and the rest of the excess is dropped.
In the example, the author says if the estate is double 13,000 (i.e., 26,000), then the 3,000 is fully covered. If the estate is only 3,000, then only 1,000 (one-third) is given.
5
Conclude the final obligations
After all adjustments: The 'aqila originally owed 10,000 diyah. 7,000 is deducted as mahr mithl (valid from entire estate). The remaining 3,000 is subject to the one-third limit. If the estate is large enough, the 'aqila pay only 7,000 (they are relieved of 3,000). If the estate is small, the 'aqila pay 8,000 (7,000 + 1,000) or less. The woman cannot claim any additional amount.
The core rule: mahr mithl is always deducted; the excess is a gift that may be reduced.

وان كان خطاء يرفع عن العاقلة مهر مثلها ولهم ثلث ما ترك وصية لان هذا تزوج على الدية وهى تصلح مهرا الا انه يعتبر بقدر مهر المثل من جميع المال لانه مريض مرض الموت والتزوج من الحوائج الاصلية ولا يصح فى حق الزيادة على مهر المثل نه محاباة فتكون وصية ترجمہ اور اگر قطع یہ خطا ہو تو عاقلہ (برادری) سے عورت کے مہر مثل کی مقدار ساقط کر دی جائے گی ۔ اور دیت کی مقدار میں سے مہر مثل کی مقدار کے علاوہ جو بیچ رہاوہ عاقلہ کے لئے وصیت ہے اس لئے کہ یہ دیت پر نکاح کرنا ہے اور دیت مہر بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے مگر مہر مثل کی مقدار تک معافی پورے مال سے معتبر ہوگی اس لئے کہ وہ مرض الموت کا مریض ہے اور نکاح کرنا حوائج اصلیہ میں سے ہے اور مہرشل پر زیادتی کے حق میں معافی صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ عفو صحابات ہے (عطیہ ہے ) تو محابات وصیت ہو جائے گی۔

لیکن زید اس صورت میں مرض الموت کا مریض شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ مرض الموت کا مریض جو ایسے کام کرے جو حوا
اصلیہ میں داخل ہوں تو وہ پورے مال سے معتبر ہوا کرتے ہیں یعنی ان معاملات میں وہ تندرست لوگوں کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور رہے وہ معاملات جو حوائج اصلیہ میں سے نہ ہوں تو اس میں وہ مرض الموت کا مریض شمار ہوگا اور اس کے تصرفات ثلث میں نافذ ہوں گے یعنی ان معاملات کو وصیت کا درجہ ملے گا۔ اور نکاح کرنا حوائج اصلیہ میں سے ہے تو عورت کا مہر مثل تو پورے مال سے معتبر ہوگا اور ہدیہ وہبہ وغیرہ حوائج اصلیہ میں سے نہیں الہذاوہ ثلث مال سے معتبر ہوں گے۔
بہر حال عاقلہ پر یہاں دیت واجب ہوئی یعنی دس ہزار درہم اور عورت کا مہر مثل نسات ہزار درہم ہے تو عاقلہ کے اوپر سے سان مثل کے ساقط ہو گئے اب باقی بچے تین ہزار اور زید نے پوری دیت کو مہر قرار دیا تھا لہذا یہ تین بھی ساقط ہو جانے چاہئیں لیکہ ہزار تو مہر سات سے زائد میں زید کا تصرف مریض مرض الموت ہونے کی وجہ سے ثلث مال میں جاری ہو گا لہذا اگر زید کا ترکہ اور بھی ہے جو اس تیر ہزار کا دگنا ہے تو عاقلہ کے اوپر سے یہ تین بھی ساقط ہو جائیں گے۔
اگر تین ہزار کے علاوہ اور زید کا مال نہ ہو تو اس میں سے ایک ہزار ساقط ہو جائیں گے اور عورت کی برادری دو ہزار درہم زید کے وہ کو ادا کرے گی۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے اس مضمون کو ادا کیا ہے۔

واپس لے لے؟
تو فرمایا کہ واپس نہیں لے سکتی کیونکہ یہ کہاں کا متک اور کہاں کا انصاف ہے کہ جنایت تو کرے عورت اور عاقلہ اس کی دیت د۔ جس میں اس کا مہر ساقط ہو جائے اور عورت عاقلہ سے پھر اپنے مہر کا مطالبہ کرے لہذا یہ اصول مقرر کیا گیا کہ عورت کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ مثل کی مقدار واپس لے۔
If the woman cut the hand accidentally and the rest of the details are as before, what is the ruling? And if it was accidental, the proper dower (mahr mithl) is lifted from the 'aqila (tribe), and they (the 'aqila) have one-third of what he left as a wasiyyah (bequest), because this is a marriage on the basis of diyah, and diyah is suitable as mahr. But it is considered only to the extent of mahr mithl from the entire estate, because he (Zaid) is a terminally ill patient, and marriage is among the primary needs (hawa'ij asliyyah). And it is not valid for the excess over mahr mithl, as it is a gift (muhabah), so it becomes a wasiyyah. Translation: And if the cutting was accidental, then the amount of the woman's proper dower is deducted from the 'aqila. And from the amount of diyah, what remains after mahr mithl is a wasiyyah for the 'aqila, because this marriage is on the basis of diyah, and diyah is capable of being mahr. But the remission to the extent of mahr mithl is considered from the entire estate because he is a terminally ill patient, and marriage is among primary needs, and the remission for the excess over mahr mithl is not valid, because it is a gift, so it becomes a wasiyyah. Explanation: And if Zainab cut Zaid's hand accidentally and the rest of the details are as before, what is the ruling? He (the author) said: The difference between intentional and accidental is that in the first, the right of a third party is not attached because it is not property, and in the second, due to being property, the right of a third party becomes attached. Therefore, in the first case, both qisas and diyah were terminated, and the woman's mahr mithl was made obligatory for the reason already given. But here the diyah will not be dropped; rather, diyah becomes obligatory because Zaid made diyah the mahr, and diyah, being property, can be mahr. However, Zaid in this case is considered a terminally ill patient. And the principle is that a terminally ill patient, for actions that fall under primary needs, is considered from all of his estate—i.e., in such transactions he is like a healthy person. As for transactions that are not primary needs, he is considered a terminally ill patient, and his dispositions are effective only within one-third of the estate; they get the status of a wasiyyah. Marriage is among primary needs, so the woman's mahr mithl is considered from the entire estate, while gifts and donations are not primary needs, so they are considered within one-third. Anyway, here diyah is obligatory on the 'aqila—i.e., ten thousand dirhams—and the woman's mahr mithl is seven thousand dirhams. So seven thousand are deducted from the 'aqila, leaving three thousand. Since Zaid had made the entire diyah the mahr, these three thousand should also be dropped, but because Zaid's disposition regarding the excess over mahr mithl, being terminally ill, takes effect within one-third, if Zaid's estate is double this thirteen thousand, then these three thousand are also dropped from the 'aqila. If there is no property besides the three thousand, then one thousand is dropped, and the woman's tribe will pay two thousand dirhams to Zaid's estate. In this phrase, the author has expressed this meaning. The reason for lifting mahr mithl from the 'aqila: "And it is lifted from the 'aqila because they bear (the diyah) on her behalf, so it is impossible that she should recourse to them for her own crime. And this excess is a wasiyyah for them because they are eligible for wasiyyah, as they are not killers. If it comes out of one-third, it is dropped; if not, one-third is dropped." Translation: And mahr mithl will be removed from the 'aqila because these people (the 'aqila) bear (the diyah) on behalf of the woman, so it is impossible for the woman to recourse to them regarding her own crime. And the excess is a wasiyyah for the 'aqila because the 'aqila are eligible for wasiyyah since they are not killers. So if the excess comes out of one-third, the excess is dropped; if not, one-third of the excess is dropped. Explanation: The diyah for accidental killing is obligatory on the 'aqila, and mahr mithl is the woman's right. Does the woman have the right to take back her seven thousand from the 'aqila? He said: She cannot take it back, because what sort of logic and justice is this: the woman commits the crime, and the 'aqila pay the diyah, which includes the dropping of her mahr, and then the woman claims her mahr from the 'aqila? Hence this principle is established: the woman has no right to take back the amount of mahr mithl.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, detailing the case of accidental cutting where marriage is contracted in exchange for diyah. The author begins by quoting the Arabic text of al-Hidayah, then explains it. The key difference from the intentional case is that diyah, being property, can serve as valid mahr. However, since Zaid is terminally ill (marad al-mawt), specific rules apply: marriage is a primary need (hajah asliyyah), so the mahr mithl (proper dower) is valid from the entire estate; any excess over mahr mithl in the specified mahr (here the full diyah) is treated as a gift (muhabah) and is only effective within one-third of the estate, like a wasiyyah. The 'aqila are liable for diyah (here 10,000 dirhams), but the woman's mahr mithl (7,000 dirhams) is deducted from that amount because the 'aqila bear the diyah on her behalf. The remaining 3,000 dirhams (excess over mahr mithl) are considered a wasiyyah to the 'aqila, subject to the thuluth rule: if the estate covers it, it is fully deducted from the 'aqila; if not, only one-third of the excess is deducted. Finally, the woman cannot claim her mahr from the 'aqila because they already pay her diyah, and the mahr is effectively part of that payment.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money or compensation paid to the victim's heirs in accidental killing or injury; here it is property and can serve as mahr.
عاقلہ (al-'aqila): The tribe or group of male relatives on the father's side who collectively bear the diyah for accidental killing or injury caused by one of their members.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness (death-illness) where the patient's transactions are restricted to one-third of the estate unless they are among primary needs (hawa'ij asliyyah).
حوائج اصلیہ (hawa'ij asliyyah): Primary or essential needs; marriage is included, so a terminally ill person's marriage is valid from the entire estate up to mahr mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the accidental cutting scenario, if the diyah is 10,000 dirhams and the woman's mahr mithl is 7,000, what happens to the remaining 3,000 dirhams?
A) The woman keeps it as an additional mahr.
B) It is a gift to the 'aqila but only effective within one-third of the estate due to marad al-mawt.
C) It is returned to the husband's estate as a debt.
D) It is dropped entirely because the 'aqila are not liable for excess.

Key Takeaway
In accidental injury, a terminally ill man marrying the perpetrator using diyah as mahr results in mahr mithl being fully valid from the entire estate, while any excess is a bequest limited to one-third of the estate.

Treatment of Excess Over Mahr Mithl as a Bequest to the 'Aqila
Ruling on excess over mahr mithl being treated as bequest to 'Aqila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the excess over mahr mithl in diyah cases and apply the one-third bequest rule to determine the 'Aqila's liability.

Core Idea
Excess over mahr mithl becomes a bequest to the wife's 'Aqila, not diyah.

In Hanafi diyah law, when a husband kills his wife, the husband's 'Aqila are liable for the mahr mithl only. Any amount beyond that is not part of diyah; instead, it is considered a bequest (wasiyyah) from the husband to the wife's 'Aqila. This is because the wife's 'Aqila are neither his heirs nor the killer, so they are eligible to receive a bequest. However, the bequest is subject to the general rule that it cannot exceed one-third of the testator's estate unless the heirs consent. This lesson unpacks this specific ruling and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Consider a husband who kills his wife. The wife's 'Aqila claim diyah. The husband's 'Aqila are liable. Determine what they must pay.
2
Distinguish between mahr mithl and excess
The mahr mithl is completely dropped from the 'Aqila's liability. Any amount beyond that (the excess) is not treated as diyah.
The excess is not a blood money debt.
3
Apply the bequest framework
The excess is treated as if the husband made a bequest to the wife's 'Aqila. This is valid because they are neither his heirs nor the killer. Now apply the bequest limitation: a bequest to a non-heir is effective only up to one-third of the estate.
If the excess exceeds one-third, only one-third is honored.
4
Determine the final liability of the 'Aqila
The 'Aqila's liability is reduced by the amount of the effective bequest. If the full excess is within one-third, it is entirely dropped; otherwise, only one-third is dropped, and the remainder remains payable by the 'Aqila.
Example: If the husband's estate is 6000 and the excess is 2000 (≤ one-third), the whole 2000 is dropped. If estate is 4000, one-third is 1333, so only 1333 is dropped and 667 remains on the 'Aqila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لہذا عاقلہ کے اوپر سے مہر مثل کی مقدار بالکل ساقط شمار کی جائے گی ۔ اور رہی زیادتی تو اس کے بارے میں یہ حکم ہے کہ گویا اس کو زید نے زینب کے عاقلہ کے لئے وصیت کر دیا ہے کیونکہ وہ نہ زید کے وارث ہیں اور نہ قاتل ہیں لہذا وہ اس کے اہل ہیں کہ ان کی وصیت کی جا سکے۔ فان كانت ... پھر اگر اس زیادتی سے دو ثلث یا اس سے زائد تر کہ زید کا ہو تو یہ زیادتی وصیت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گی اور اگر نہ ہو تو حسب مذکور اس کا ایک ثلث ختم ہو جائے گا اور باقی دو ہزار عاقلہ پر واجب الادا ہوں گے۔
Therefore, the amount of mahr mithl is completely dropped from the 'Aqila. As for the excess, the ruling is that it is as if Zayd made a bequest to Zaynab's 'Aqila, because they are neither Zayd's heirs nor the killer, so they are eligible for his bequest. Then if the excess amounts to two-thirds or more of Zayd's estate, this excess will be dropped due to the bequest; otherwise, one-third of it is waived as per the mentioned detail, and the remaining two thousand will be payable by the 'Aqila.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage concludes a discussion on the liability of the 'Aqila for diyah when a husband kills his wife and the wife's 'Aqila seek compensation. Mahr mithl is completely excluded from the 'Aqila's liability. Any amount beyond mahr mithl is treated as a bequest from the husband to the wife's 'Aqila, since they are neither his heirs nor the killer. The bequest is valid but subject to the one-third rule: if the excess exceeds one-third of the estate, only one-third applies; otherwise, the full excess is dropped. The remaining amount (here two thousand) remains on the 'Aqila.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('Aqila): Paternal relatives of the killer obligated to pay diyah in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional homicide.
مهر مثل (Mahr mithl): Proper dower equivalent to that of women of similar status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is treated as a bequest (wasiyyah) to the 'Aqila.
C) It is nullified because the 'Aqila are not heirs.
D) It is paid by the husband's estate alone.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyah, excess over mahr mithl is a bequest to the wife's 'Aqila, limited to one-third of the husband's estate.

Diyat — Blood Money

Definition of Diyat and Arsh, and Ruling on Shibh 'Amd
Defines diyah and arsh, then states ruling on diyah and kaffarah for shibh 'amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define diyah and arsh as Hanafi legal terms and state the ruling for shibh 'amd regarding diyah and kaffarah.

Core Idea
Diyah mughallazah is on the 'aqilah; kaffarah is on the killer in shibh 'amd.

This lesson opens the Book of Diyat. Two key terms are defined: diyah (blood-money for life) and arsh (compensation for injuries). Then the ruling for qatl shibh 'amd is given: the killer's male relatives ('aqilah) must pay a heavy diyah of specific camels, while the killer himself must perform kaffarah. Understanding these distinctions is essential for applying Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Define diyah and arsh
From the text, diyah is the property substituted for a life; arsh is the property wajib for injuries less than loss of life.
Note the distinction: arsh is not a type of diyah but a separate category for injuries.
2
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qatl shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional killing). The ruling: diyah mughallazah (heavy blood-money) and kaffarah (expiation) are both wajib.
Heavy diyah consists of 100 camels of four specific types: bint makhad, hiqaq, bint labun, jadha'.
3
Locate the responsible parties
The diyah is upon the 'aqilah (the killer's male paternal relatives), not the killer himself. The kaffarah is upon the killer personally.
The 'aqilah's obligation is a unique Hanafi feature.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g. Shafi'i, Maliki) do not require kaffarah in shibh 'amd, treating it more like khata' (error).
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

كِتابُ الدِّيات
ترجمہ یہ کتاب دیتوں کے بیان میں ہے

تشریح اولا قصاص کو بیان کیا گیا ہے پھر دیت کو کیونکہ قصاص اصل ہے اور دیت خلیفہ کے مثل ہے۔ نیز حیات اور ا نفس کی حفاظت زیادہ اہم ہے اس لئے قصاص کو مقدم کیا گیا ہے۔ دیت شریعت میں اس مال کو کہتے ہیں جونفس کا بدل قرار دیا گیا ہے یعنی یہ تسمیہ انٹی باسم المصدر کی قبیل سے ہے اور ارش اس مال کو کہتے ہیں جو نفس سے کم میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔

Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary volume 15, page 139. Book of Diyat. Translation: This book is about diyat. Commentary: First qisas was mentioned, then diyah, because qisas is the original and diyah is like a substitute. Also preserving life and self is more important, so qisas was given precedence. Diyah in Shariah is the property that is made the substitute for life, i.e. this naming is of the type of tismiyyah ism al-masdar. And arsh is the property that is wajib for less than life (i.e., injuries). The diyah of qatl shibh 'amd is on the 'aqilah and the kaffarah is on the killer. He (al-Quduri) said: And in shibh 'amd, a heavy diyah is on the 'aqilah and kaffarah on the killer, and we have explained it in the beginning of chapter of injuries. Translation: Quduri said: And in shibh 'amd, on the 'aqilah is a heavy diyah and on the killer is kaffarah, and we have explained shibh 'amd at the start of injuries. Commentary: The diyah of qatl shibh 'amd is on the 'aqilah and kaffarah on the killer; its explanation has passed in al-Hidayah vol.4 p.545, but the manner of taqliz (making heavy) did not pass there, which will be explained here: When one hundred camels are wajib, and these four types are wajib: bint makhad, hiqaq, bint labun, jadha'. This is called diyah mughallazah.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah opens the Book of Diyat. It first defines two key terms: diyah (blood-money) is the property that substitutes for a life in cases where qisas is not applicable or is waived; arsh is the compensation for injuries less than loss of life. The commentator notes that qisas was discussed first because it is the primary remedy, while diyah is a substitute. Then the passage states the ruling for qatl shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional killing): the diyah mughallazah (heavy blood-money) is due on the 'aqilah (the killer's male paternal relatives), while the kaffarah (expiation) is on the killer himself. The reference to al-Hidayah indicates this was already explained, but the details of the heavy diyah – that it consists of 100 camels of specific types (bint makhad, hiqaq, bint labun, jadha') – are given here. This is a straightforward legal statement from the Hanafi school, based on the text of al-Quduri and expanded by the commentator.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): The property that is made the substitute for a life in the Shariah.
أرش (arsh): The property wajib for injuries less than loss of life.
شبه عمد (shibh 'amd): A killing that resembles intentional but is not fully intentional; e.g., striking with an object not normally lethal.
عاقلة ('aqilah): The group of male paternal relatives of the killer who are responsible for paying diyah in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In shibh 'amd, the heavy diyah is on the 'aqilah and the kaffarah is on the killer.

Kaffarah for Qatl Shibh 'Amd: Freeing a Slave or Fasting
States the kaffarah ruling with Quranic proof and reasoning for excluding feeding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the kaffarah for qatl shibh 'amd according to the Hanafi school, identify its Quranic proof, and explain why feeding is not an acceptable alternative.

Core Idea
For qatl shibh 'amd, kaffarah is either freeing a believing slave or fasting two months; feeding is invalid because measures of expiation are divinely prescribed.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn, with commentary from al-Hidayah, establishes the expiation (kaffarah) for killing resembling intentional (shibh 'amd). It provides the Quranic basis and explains why feeding others is not an option, grounding the reasoning in the principle of tawqif (divine prescription).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and what legal ruling applies. The act is qatl shibh 'amd, and the ruling is that kaffarah is wajib.
The kaffarah is either freeing a believing slave or, if unable, fasting two consecutive months.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited. The matn quotes Quran 4:92: 'فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُّؤْمِنَةٍ' (freeing a believing slave).
The full verse mentions 'wa man qatala mu'minan khata'an', but the matn uses the partial quote.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the proof indicates obligation. The imperative form and the letter fa' in 'فَتَحْرِيرُ' indicate the entire required act.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub. The fa' makes freeing the whole wajib, leaving no room for substitution.
4
Note the exclusion of feeding
Identify why feeding (it'am) is not accepted. The commentator states that no text supports it, and measures of expiation are known only by tawqif.
Tawqif means human reasoning (qiyas) cannot expand the prescribed options.
5
Understand subsidiary rulings
Consider the rulings about a breastfeeding infant (radee') and a fetus. The infant with one Muslim parent is considered Muslim and valid; the fetus is not because certainty is lacking.
These rulings follow from the condition that the slave must be a believer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال وكفارته عتق رقبة مؤمنة لقوله تعالى فتحرير رقبة مومنة الآية فان لم يجد فصيام شهرين متتابعين بهذا النص ولا يجزئى فيه الاطعام لانه لم يرد به نص والمقادير تعرف بالتوقيف ولانه جعل المذكور كل الواجب بحرف الفاء اولكونه كل المذكور على ما عرف ويجزئه رضيع احدابویه مسلم لانه مسلم به والظاهر سلامة المرافه ولا يجزى مافى البطن لانه لم تعرف حياته ولا سلامته ترجمہ اور شبہ عمد کا کفارہ مومن غلام کو آزاد کرتا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان فتحرير رقبة مؤمنہ کی وجہ سے پس اگر وہ غلام نہ پائے تو دو لگا تار مہینوں کے روزے ركھنا ہے اسی نص کی وجہ سے اور اس میں کھانا کھلانا کفایت نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ اطعام کے سلسلہ میں کوئی نص وارد نہیں ہے اور مقادیرتوقیف شارع سے معلوم ہوتی ہیں اور اس لئے حرف فاء کی وجہ سے مذکور کو کل واجب قرار دیا جائے گایا مذکور کے کل مذکور ہونے کی وجہ سے ( اس کو کل واجب قرار دیا جائے گا ) جیسا کہ معروف ہے۔ تشریح شبہ عمد کا کفارہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قدرت : د تو مومن غلام آزاد کر دے ارشاد باری ہے و من قتل مؤ مناً خطاً فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة
What is the kaffarah of qatl shibh 'amd? He (al-Quduri) said: Its kaffarah is freeing a believing slave, due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة' (the verse). So if he does not find (a slave), then fasting two consecutive months, by this text. And feeding (others) is not sufficient for it, because no text has come regarding it, and measures (of expiation) are known by tawqif (divine prescription). And because the mentioned (slave and fasting) is made the entire wajib by the letter fa', or because it is the entire mentioned as is known. And a breastfeeding infant (radiy') if one of his parents is Muslim is sufficient because he is Muslim by that, and the apparent condition is safety from imperfection. And what is in the womb is not sufficient because his life and safety are not known. Translation: And the kaffarah of shibh 'amd is freeing a believing slave; due to the command of Allah: 'فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة' (the freeing of a believing slave). So if he does not find a slave, then fasting two consecutive months, by this text. And feeding in it is not sufficient, because no text has come regarding feeding, and measures (of expiation) are known by tawqif. And because the mentioned (slave and fasting) is made the entire wajib by the letter fa', or because it is the entire of the mentioned as is well known. Commentary: The kaffarah of shibh 'amd is that if he has the ability, he frees a believing slave; the command of Allah is: 'وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَأً فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُّؤْمِنَةٍ' (And whoever kills a believer by mistake should free a believing slave).
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the kaffarah (expiation) for qatl shibh 'amd. It begins by quoting the matn from al-Quduri: the kaffarah is freeing a believing slave, based on the Quranic verse (4:92) which in its full form reads 'وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَأً فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُّؤْمِنَةٍ'. If one cannot find a slave or afford one, then fasting two consecutive months is required. The commentator then explains why feeding (it'am) is not acceptable: no scriptural evidence exists for it, and the measures of expiation are determined solely by divine prescription (tawqif). The letter fa' in 'فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُّؤْمِنَةٍ' indicates that the freeing is the entirety of the wajib; similarly, the alternative of fasting is also complete. The passage also addresses two subsidiary issues: a breastfeeding infant (radee') who has at least one Muslim parent is considered Muslim and therefore acceptable for freeing as a slave (if inherited as a Muslim). However, a fetus (ma fi al-batn) is not acceptable because its life and state (whether it is Muslim or complete) are unknown. This reasoning follows the Hanafi principle that legal obligations are based on certainty.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act required from the killer in shibh 'amd and khata', to remove sin or deficiency.
توقيف (tawqif): The principle that the measures and quantities of expiations and punishments are determined solely by divine revelation, not by human reasoning.
رضيع (radee'): A breastfeeding infant who has both parents Muslim or at least one Muslim parent, considered Muslim in ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Feeding sixty poor people
B) Fasting two consecutive months
C) Freeing a non-Muslim slave
D) Paying additional diyah

Key Takeaway
For qatl shibh 'amd, the kaffarah is strictly either freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months; no other form, such as feeding, is valid because the measures are determined solely by divine prescription.

Kaffarah for Qatl Shibh al-Amd and Conditions
Ruling on diyah and kaffarah for semi-intentional homicide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the kaffarah for qatl shibh al-amd and identify the conditions that make a slave acceptable for expiation.

Core Idea
Kaffarah for shibh al-amd is wajib: free a Muslim sound slave or fast two months — feeding does not suffice.

This passage from al-Hidayah explains the ruling of kaffarah for semi-intentional homicide (shibh al-amd). The author cites the Quranic verse (4:92) to establish that the expiation is either freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months. The text also clarifies why feeding the poor is not a valid substitute, based on the principle that the letter 'fa' in the verse indicates the exclusive obligation of the mentioned items. Additionally, the conditions of the slave are discussed: the slave must be Muslim and free from defects; a nursing infant with one Muslim parent is acceptable, but a fetus is not, as its life and soundness are uncertain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that qatl shibh al-amd (semi-intentional homicide) incurs both diyah (heavy blood money on the a'qila) and kaffarah (expiation) on the killer. The ruling level is wajib.
The diyah aspect is mentioned but not the focus here; the passage emphasises the kaffarah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic proof: 'fa-tahriru raqabatin mu'minah' (Quran 4:92). This is the primary evidence for the obligation.
The verse originally addresses qatl khata' (accidental), but the Hanafi school applies it to shibh al-amd by analogy or textual extension.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Understand that the imperative 'tahrir' indicates obligation (wujub), and the letter 'fa' (fa' al-ta'qib) shows that the mentioned items are the entire wajib, excluding others. This is why feeding is not valid.
This is a core usul argument: 'al-fa' yufidu al-hasr' (the fa' implies exclusivity).
4
Examine conditions of the slave
The slave must be Muslim and sound in limbs (saleem al-atraf). A nursing infant with one Muslim parent suffices because of taba'iyyah (following). A fetus does not because life and safety are unknown.
The condition 'mu'minah' requires faith; taba'iyyah makes the infant Muslim based on a parent's Islam.
5
Note the limitation on alternatives
Feeding the poor is rejected because no text (nass) supports it, and measures in expiation are determined by divine limitation (tawqif). Only the two mentioned options are valid.
This highlights the strictness of Hanafi methodology: ibadah are tawqifiyyah (based on revelation), not open to qiyas for expansion.

Source Text

قال وفى شبه العمددية مغلظة على العاقلة وكفارة على القاتل وقد بيناه في اول الجنايات ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور شبہ عمد میں عاقلہ پر دیت مغلظہ ہے اور قاتل پر کفارہ اور ہم شبہ عمد کو جنایات کے شروع میں بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح قتل شبه عمد کی دیت عاقلہ پر ہوتی ہے اور کفارہ قاتل پر ہوتا ہے، ہدا ص ۵۴۵ ج ۴ اس کا بیان گزر چکا ہے لیکن تغلیظ کا طریقہ وہاں نہیں گزرا جس کو یہاں بیان کیا جائے گا جب اونٹ سو واجب ہوں اور ان کی یہ چار انواع واجب ہوں، - اور کفارہ قتل میں مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانا کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مقادیر شرعیہ شریعت کے بتانے ہی سے معلوم ہو سکتی ہیں ۔ حالانکہ کسی نص میں یہ منقول نہیں ہے کہ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانے سے کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اور اصول فقہ کے اندر یہ اصول مقرر ہے، ا کہ فاء کے بعد جو جزاء آتی ہے تو اس میں ضروری ہے کہ پوری جزاء مذکور ہو ورنہ وہاں التباس پیدا ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہاں نص میں قتل خطاء کے بعد فاء کے بعد یہی دو چیزیں مذکور ہیں ۔ تحریر اور صیام ۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہی دو چیزیں بطریق مانعۃ الخلو مطلوب ہیں۔ مقام حاجت بیان میں جو مذکور ہوگا وہی مطلوب ہو گا اور غیر مذکور مراد نہ ہوگا۔ ورنہ اگر غیر مذکور مراد ہوتا تو اس کی احتیاج کی وجہ سے اس کو بھی ضرور بیان کیا جاتا۔ جس غلام کو کفارہ میں ادا کیا جائے اس کا مسلمان ہونا ضروری ہے اور سلیم الاطراف ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لہذا جو بچہ غلام ہوا اور ابھی دودھ پیتا ہےاس کے والدین میں سے کوئی ایک مسلمان ہے تو اس کو آزاد کرنے سے کفارہ ادا ہو جاۓ گا۔ کیونکہ والدین میں سے ایک کے مسلمان ہونے کی وجہ وہ بچہ بھی مسلمان شمار ہوگا اور چونکہ وہ بچہ ماں کے پیٹ میں نہیں ہے بلکہ باہر ہے۔ لہذا اس کے اطراف کی سلامتی بھی ظاہر ہو جائے گی اور جب وہ سلیم الاعضاء ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا آزاد کرنا کافی ہوگا۔ اور جو بچہ ابھی ماں کے پیٹ میں ہے اس کو آزاد کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ ابھی تو یہ بھی معلوم نہیں کہ وہ زندہ بھی ہے یا نہیں اسی طرح یہ بھی معلوم نہیں کہ وہ سلیم الاطراف بھی ہے یا نہیں ۔ تنبیہ ایمان ایک وصف ہے اور وصف میں کمال شرط نہیں اس لئے ایمان کا بر بناء تبعیت ثبوت کافی ہو جائے گا۔
He said: And for shibh al-amd, a heavy diyah is on the aqila and kaffarah is on the killer, and we have explained it at the beginning of Jinaayat. Translation: Quduri said: In shibh al-amd, the diyah mughallaza is on the aqila and the kaffarah on the killer, and we have explained shibh al-amd at the beginning of Jinaayat. Commentary: The diyah of qatl shibh al-amd is on the aqila and the kaffarah on the killer... It has passed. But the method of tighliz (aggravation) has not passed, which will be explained here. When one hundred camels are wajib, these four types are wajib: bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, jadha'a; this is called diyah mughallaza. What is the kaffarah of qatl shibh al-amd? He said: Its kaffarah is freeing a believing slave, due to the saying of Allah: 'فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة' the verse. If he does not find one, then fasting two consecutive months, by this text. And feeding does not suffice in it, because no text has come regarding it, and measures are known by tawqif (divine limitation). And because he made the mentioned [items] all of the wajib by the letter fa', or because it is all of the mentioned as is known. And a nursing infant whose one parent is Muslim suffices, because he is Muslim by that, and the apparent safety of his limbs. And the one in the womb does not suffice, because his life and safety are not known. Translation: And the kaffarah of shibh al-amd is freeing a believing slave due to the command of Allah... etc. Commentary: ... And in usul al-fiqh this principle is established: that after fa' the jaza (result) must be mentioned in full, otherwise confusion arises. Here in the text, after the fa' in the verse about qatl khata', only these two things are mentioned: freeing and fasting. So it is known that these two alone are required in an exclusive manner. The slave to be freed must be Muslim and sound in limbs. Hence, a nursing infant slave who has one Muslim parent suffices... but a child in the womb does not suffice. Tanbih: Iman is a description, and in descriptions perfection is not a condition, so iman based on following (taba'iyya) is sufficient.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli) from the Quran. The passage discusses the diyah mughallaza (heavy blood money) for qatl shibh al-amd (semi-intentional homicide) which is on the aqila (tribal surety) and the kaffarah (expiation) which is on the killer. The kaffarah is either freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months. Feeding the poor is not valid because the text specifies only these two options and the principle that measures are known by divine limitation. The passage also explains the conditions of the slave: must be Muslim and sound in limbs. A nursing child is acceptable if one parent is Muslim, but a fetus is not because its life and soundness are unknown. A 'tanbih' (note) clarifies that iman (faith) as a quality can be considered present through following (taba'iyya) without perfection.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh al-amd): Semi-intentional homicide: an act that is intentional but not intended to kill, or using a tool that is not usually lethal.
دية مغلظة (diyah mughallaza): Aggravated blood money: full diyah of 100 camels in specific categories.
عاقلة (a'qila): The tribal surety responsible for paying diyah on behalf of the killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the kaffarah for qatl shibh al-amd according to this passage?
A) Freeing a believing slave or fasting two months
B) Freeing any slave or feeding sixty poor
C) Paying diyah only
D) Fasting only

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah for shibh al-amd is wajib and strictly limited to freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months; no other substitution is valid.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner
6 min
Diyah for Shibh al-Amd: Composition and Kaffarah
Ruling statement on diyah for shibh al-amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the components of the diyah for shibh al-amd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf and explain the identity of its kaffarah with that of khata.

Core Idea
The diyah for shibh al-amd is 100 camels in four equal categories per the two imams.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the diyah for semi-intentional homicide (shibh al-amd) according to the two shaykhs, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. It also connects the kaffarah to that of accidental homicide (khata). Understanding these categories is essential for diyat calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
Recognize that the passage deals with shibh al-amd (semi-intentional homicide) and states the diyah (blood money) due.
Shibh al-amd is a homicide where the intent to kill is weak, e.g., striking with something not normally lethal.
2
Note the source of authority
The ruling is attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, known as the Shaykhayn. This is a relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani may have a different view, not mentioned here.
3
Break down the diyah composition
The diyah is 100 camels divided equally into four categories of 25 each: bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, and jadha'a.
Each category represents a specific age of female camel.
4
Understand the age definitions
These categories correspond to camels in their second, third, fourth, and fifth years respectively. Learn the definitions from the commentary.
Bint makhad: second-year camel whose mother is pregnant again.
5
Connect the kaffarah identity
The passage states that the kaffarah (expiation) for shibh al-amd is the same as for khata: freeing a believing slave or fasting two months.
This shows that the expiation is linked to the loss of life, not the degree of intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قتل خطاء کا کفارہ قتل شبه عمد والا ہے قبل خطاء کی دیت میں شیخین کا مسلک
قال و هو الكفارة في الخطأ لما تلوناه وديته عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف مائة من الابل ارباعا خمس و عشرون بنت مخاض وخمس وعشرون بنت لبون وخمس وعشرون حقة وخمس وعشرون جذعة ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور یہی ( جو ہم نے شبہ عمد میں بیان کیا ہے تحریر و صیام ) کفارہ ہے خطاء کے اندر اس آیت کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم تلاوت کر چکے، اور شیخین کے نزدیک شبہ عمد کی دیت چار قسم کے سو اونٹ ہیں پچیس بنت مخاض اور پچیس بنت لبون اور پچھیں حقے اور چپس جزعے۔ تشریح اس قال کے فاعل خود مصنف ہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ جو قتل شبہ عمد کا کفارہ ہے وہی قتل خطاء کا کفارہ ہے۔ اور شبہ عد میں سواونٹ واجب ہوں گے جس میں حسب مذکور چار میں ہوں گی اور یہ شیخین کا مذہب ہے۔ بنت مخاض : اونٹ کا وہ بچہ جو دوسرے سال میں لگ گیا ہو اور چونکہ اب اس کی ماں دوسرے بچے کے ساتھ حاملہ ہو چکی ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس کو بنت مخاض کہتے ہیں۔
The kaffarah of qatl khata' is the same as for qatl shibh al-amd; before [this], the maslak of the Shaykhayn regarding the diyah of khata'. He said: And it is the kaffarah in khata' because of what we recited, and its diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is one hundred camels in quarters: twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqa, and twenty-five jadha'a. Translation: The author said: And this (which we have stated in shibh al-amd: freeing and fasting) is the kaffarah in khata' due to that verse, and according to the Shaykhayn, the diyah of shibh al-amd is one hundred camels of four types: twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqa, and twenty-five jadha'a. Commentary: The subject of this 'he said' is the author himself. He says: The kaffarah of qatl shibh al-amd is the same as the kaffarah of qatl khata'. And in shibh al-amd, one hundred camels are wajib, in the four categories as mentioned, and this is the madhhab of the Shaykhayn. Bint makhad: a young camel that has entered its second year, and because its mother is now pregnant with another, it is called bint makhad.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the kaffarah for accidental homicide (khata') is identical to that for semi-intentional homicide (shibh al-amd): freeing a believing slave or fasting two months. It then states the diyah for shibh al-amd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the 'Shaykhayn') as one hundred camels divided equally into four categories: bint makhad (female camel in second year), bint labun (female camel in third year), hiqqa (female camel in fourth year), and jadha'a (female camel in fifth year). The commentator explains the terminology and confirms that this is the relied-upon position of these two imams. Note that the passage does not mention the view of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, indicating a potential intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf not elaborated here.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel in her second year, whose mother is pregnant again.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A female camel in her third year.
حقة (hiqqah): A female camel in her fourth year.
جذعة (jadha'ah): A female camel in her fifth year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 100 camels in 5 categories
C) 80 camels in 4 categories
D) 100 camels in 3 categories

Key Takeaway
The diyah for shibh al-amd is wajib and comprises 100 camels in four equal categories per the Shaykhayn.

Kaffarah for Accidental Killing and Conditions of the Slave
States kaffarah for accidental killing and conditions of the slave to be freed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the kaffarah for qatl al-khata' and identify the conditions required for a slave to be validly freed in expiation.

Core Idea
Only freeing a believing, sound-limbed slave or fasting two months suffices for kaffarah – no alternative like feeding the poor.

This passage from the Hidayah explains the expiation (kaffarah) for accidental killing, clarifying that it is strictly limited to freeing a slave or fasting. It also details the necessary qualities of the slave: the slave must be a believer and free from physical defects. The discussion extends to edge cases like infant slaves and unborn children, reinforcing the importance of certainty in fulfilling the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
Locate the text stating that the kaffarah for accidental killing is freeing a slave or fasting two consecutive months, and note that the Quranic verse (4:92) is the basis.
The proof is both textual and based on the usul principle that the conjunction 'fa' implies completeness of the mentioned options.
2
Understand why feeding the poor is excluded
Analyze the argument: only what is explicitly mentioned in the text is accepted; feeding the poor is not mentioned, so it cannot be used. This is rooted in the principle that legal measures are defined only by revelation.
This highlights the Hanafi method of strict textual adherence in ibadat.
3
List the conditions for the slave
From the passage, extract the requirements: the slave must be Muslim (mu'min) and sound-limbed (salim al-atraf). These conditions ensure the expiation is valid.
The passage also clarifies that an unborn child cannot be freed because life and soundness are unknown.
4
Apply the conditions to a live infant slave
Consider the case of an infant slave born outside the womb. If one parent is Muslim, the child is considered Muslim; being born, soundness of limbs is apparent, so freeing is valid.
Iman (faith) is a trait and perfection is not required; following the parent suffices.
5
Distinguish an unborn child
The passage explicitly states that freeing a fetus is invalid because both life and limb soundness are unknown – key conditions cannot be verified.
This underscores the principle that uncertainty invalidates the act.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ ودية مسلمة الى اهله “ اور اگر غلام نہ ملے تو پھر کفارہ یہ ہے کہ دوماہ کے لگاتار (پے درپے) روزے رکھے (كما هو ثابت بهذا النص ) - اور کفارہ قتل میں مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانا کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مقادیر شرعیہ شریعت کے بتانے ہی سے معلوم ہو سکتی ہیں ۔ حالانکہ کسی نص میں یہ منقول نہیں ہے کہ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانے سے کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اور اصول فقہ کے اندر یہ اصول مقرر ہے، ا کہ فاء کے بعد جو جزاء آتی ہے تو اس میں ضروری ہے کہ پوری جزاء مذکور ہو ورنہ وہاں التباس پیدا ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہاں نص میں قتل خطاء کے بعد فاء کے بعد یہی دو چیزیں مذکور ہیں ۔ تحریر اور صیام ۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہی دو چیز میں بطریق مانعۃ الخلو مطلوب ہیں۔ مقام حاجت بیان میں جو مذکور ہوگا وہی مطلوب ہو گا اور غیر مذکور مراد نہ ہوگا۔ ورنہ اگر غیر مذکور مراد ہوتا تو اس کی احتیاج کی وجہ سے اس کو بھی ضرور بیان کیا جاتا۔ جس غلام کو کفارہ میں ادا کیا جائے اس کا مسلمان ہونا ضروری ہے اور سلیم الاطراف ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لہذا جو بچہ غلام ہوا اور ابھی دودھ پیتا ہےاس کے والدین میں سے کوئی ایک مسلمان ہے تو اس کو آزاد کرنے سے کفارہ ادا ہو جاۓ گا۔ کیونکہ والدین میں سے ایک کے مسلمان ہونے کی وجہ وہ بچہ بھی مسلمان شمار ہوگا اور چونکہ وہ بچہ ماں کے پیٹ میں نہیں ہے بلکہ باہر ہے۔ لہذا اس کے اطراف کی سلامتی بھی ظاہر ہو جائے گی اور جب وہ سلیم الاعضاء ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا آزاد کرنا کافی ہوگا۔ اور جو بچہ ابھی ماں کے پیٹ میں ہے اس کو آزاد کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ ابھی تو یہ بھی معلوم نہیں کہ وہ زندہ بھی ہے یا نہیں اسی طرح یہ بھی معلوم نہیں کہ وہ سلیم الاطراف بھی ہے یا نہیں ۔ تنبیہ ایمان ایک وصف ہے اور وصف میں کمال شرط نہیں اس لئے ایمان کا بر بناء تبعیت ثبوت کافی ہو جائے گا۔
قال و هو الكفارة في الخطأ لما تلوناه
Book of Diyat. 130. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 15. 'And the blood money is paid to his family.' And if a slave is not found, then the expiation is that he fasts two consecutive months, as is established by this text. And in expiation for killing, feeding the poor is not sufficient because legal measures can only be known from what the Shariah indicates, while it is not transmitted in any text that feeding the poor fulfills the expiation. And in Usul al-Fiqh this principle is established: that after fa, the consequence that comes must be complete, otherwise confusion would occur. And here in the text, after the fa of qatl al-khata, these two things are mentioned: freeing and fasting. Hence it is known that these two things are required in an exhaustive manner. At the place of need, whatever is mentioned is required, and what is not mentioned is not intended. Otherwise, if the unmentioned were intended, it would have been mentioned due to need. The slave who is given in expiation must be Muslim and sound-limbed. Therefore, a child who is a slave and is still breast-feeding, if one of his parents is Muslim, then freeing him will fulfill the expiation because due to one parent being Muslim, the child is also considered Muslim. And since the child is not in the mother's womb but outside, the soundness of his limbs is apparent, and when he is proven to be sound-limbed, freeing him is sufficient. And a child still in the womb, freeing him is not sufficient because it is not yet known whether he is alive, nor whether he is sound-limbed. Note: Iman is a property, and in properties, perfection is not a condition; therefore, the establishment of Iman through following suffices. He said: And this is the expiation in accidental killing, because we have recited it.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the kaffarah (expiation) for accidental killing (qatl al-khata'). The author first states that the kaffarah is the same as for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional): freeing a believing slave, and if unable, fasting two consecutive months. The proof is the Quranic verse recited earlier (An-Nisa 4:92). The passage then explains why feeding the poor is not an option: legal measures are determined only by revelation, and the text only mentions freeing and fasting. Using a principle from usul al-fiqh, the conjunction 'fa' implies that the entire consequence is mentioned, and only these two are listed, so they are exhaustive. Next, conditions for the slave are given: the slave must be Muslim and free from physical defects (salim al-atraf). The discussion of a slave infant clarifies: if the child is born and one parent is Muslim, the child is considered Muslim; if the child is outside the womb and sound-limbed, freeing him is valid. However, an unborn child in the womb cannot be freed because his life and soundness are unknown. A note adds that Iman is a trait (wasf) where perfection is not required; following the parent suffices for the child's Islamic status.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for accidental killing, consisting of freeing a slave or fasting.
مؤمن (mu'min): A believer; the slave must be Muslim (iman).
سليم الاطراف (salim al-atraf): Sound-limbed, free from physical defects that prevent normal function.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the slave to be freed for kaffarah is an unborn infant in the mother's womb?
A) It is valid because the child will be Muslim if the mother is Muslim.
B) It is not valid because the child's life and soundness of limbs are unknown.
C) It is valid only if the mother is Muslim.
D) It is not valid unless the child is born and weaned.

Key Takeaway
The kaffarah for accidental killing is exclusively freeing a believing, sound-limbed slave or fasting two months; no other form is accepted.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Diyah for Shibh al-Amd: The Two Views
Presents the dispute on diyah for quasi-intentional killing between Shaykhayn and Muhammad/Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the composition of diyah for shibh al-amd and evaluate the evidence for each.

Core Idea
The diyah for quasi-intentional killing: four equal categories vs. three categories with pregnant camels.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a key dispute within the Hanafi school and between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the precise composition of the diyah (blood money) for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional killing). While both sides agree on the total of 100 camels, they differ on the ages and categories required, reflecting different understandings of taghliz (stringency).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is the composition of the 100 camels that constitute the diyah for shibh al-amd. Both sides agree on 100 camels, but differ in the categories and ages.
The diyah is wajib (obligatory) but the exact types are disputed.
2
State the Shaykhayn position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the 100 camels are divided equally into four categories: 25 bint makhad (2nd year), 25 bint labun (3rd year), 25 hiqqa (4th year), and 25 jadha'a (5th year).
This is the view presented first in the matn of al-Hidayah.
3
State the Muhammad/Shafi'i position
Imam Muhammad (a Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the 100 camels are divided into three categories: 30 jadha'a, 30 hiqqa, and 40 thaniyya (6th year), all of which must be pregnant.
The number of categories is reduced to three, and the thaniyya must be pregnant.
4
Analyze the evidence
The Muhammad/Shafi'i view relies on a hadith that states '40 of which have their young in their bellies' and the practice of 'Umar and Zayd (30 hiqqa, 30 jadha'a). Their rational argument is that shibh al-amd is more severe than khata', so the diyah should have fewer categories to increase stringency.
The Shaykhayn view does not cite a specific hadith; they consider the four-part division itself as taghliz.
5
Determine the khilaf's practical consequence
The difference affects which camels are actually paid: under the Shaykhayn view, 25 each of four types; under Muhammad/Shafi'i, 30, 30, and 40 pregnant thaniyya. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the Shaykhayn view, as indicated by the priority in the matn.
Fatwa is given on the Shaykhayn view.

Kaffarah of qatl al-khata' is like that of shibh al-amd. Before that, the view of the two shaykhs regarding diyah of khata'. He said: And this is the expiation in accidental killing, because we have recited it, and its diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is one hundred camels in quarters: twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqa, and twenty-five jadha'a. Translation: The author said: And this (which we mentioned in shibh al-amd, i.e., freeing and fasting) is the expiation for khata' due to the verse we have recited, and according to the two shaykhs, the diyah for shibh al-amd is one hundred camels of four types: twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqa, and twenty-five jadha'a. Explanation: The doer of 'he said' is the author himself; he says that the expiation for qatl shibh al-amd is the same as for qatl al-khata'. And for shibh al-amd, one hundred camels are obligatory, consisting of four types as mentioned, and this is the school of the two shaykhs. Bint makhad: A young she-camel that has entered the second year, and since its mother has become pregnant with another, it is called bint makhad. Bint labun: A she-camel that has entered the third year, because its mother has given birth and is giving milk, so it is called bint labun. Hiqqa: A she-camel that has entered the fourth year, because it becomes eligible to be ridden and carry loads, so it is called hiqqa. Jadha'a: A she-camel that has entered the fifth year, because it has cut its teeth, so it is called jadha'a. In any case, the detail of one hundred camels according to the two shaykhs is as mentioned. The school of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad regarding diyah of qatl al-khata': And Muhammad and Shafi'i said: In thirds: thirty jadha'a, thirty hiqqa, and forty thaniyya, all pregnant with their young in their bellies, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Beware, the killed of quasi-intentional is the killed of whip and stick, and in it is one hundred camels, forty of which have their young in their bellies.' And from 'Umar and Zayd: thirty hiqqa and thirty jadha'a. And because the diyah of shibh al-amd is more severe, and that is in what we said. Translation: And Muhammad and Shafi'i said: There will be three types of camels: thirty jadha'a, thirty hiqqa, and forty thaniyya (and that is the female of thani), all pregnant, in their bellies their offspring, due to the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Beware, the killed of quasi-intentional is the killed of whip and stick, and in it are one hundred camels, forty of which have their young in their bellies.' And it is narrated from 'Umar and Zayd: thirty hiqqa and thirty jadha'a. And because the diyah of shibh al-amd is more severe, and that is in the form we said. Explanation: Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i divided the one hundred camels into three types instead of four: thirty jadha'a, thirty hiqqa, and forty thaniyya (thani is for masculine, thaniyya for feminine), and all forty thaniyya are pregnant, meaning they have their offspring in their bellies. Everyone agrees that in shibh al-amd diyah there is severity (taghliz). The two shaykhs considered the division into four types as severity, while Imam Muhammad and Shafi'i considered the obligation of thaniyya (which enters the sixth year and is pregnant) as severity. And 'khalifah' means pregnant, 'ula' in their bellies their offspring, 'khalifat' is a description. These scholars argued with this hadith which has passed several times before, but here it is mentioned more extensively; the hadith from 'ala inna to awladiha. In any case, the hadith clearly states that of these hundred, forty should be pregnant. And it is narrated from 'Umar Farooq and Zayd ibn Thabit that thirty hiqqa and thirty jadha'a. From this detail it became known that three types of camels are obligatory: thirty hiqqa, thirty jadha'a, and forty thaniyya. This is the transmitted proof of Imam Muhammad and Shafi'i. Presenting a rational proof, they said that the diyah of shibh al-amd is severe, and severity is in what we say: that one hundred camels are divided into three parts as mentioned. Otherwise, in diyah of qatl al-khata', there are five categories of camels so that there is no severity; here there are three categories so that there is strong severity, and four categories do not have as much severity as three.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school and between schools regarding the composition of diyah (blood money) for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional killing). The matn from al-Hidayah first states the kaffarah is the same as for khata', then transitions to diyah. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the diyah consists of 100 camels divided into four equal categories of 25: bint makhad (2nd year), bint labun (3rd year), hiqqa (4th year), and jadha'a (5th year). The commentary explains each term. Then it presents the view of Imam Muhammad (a Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i: the 100 camels are divided into three categories: 30 jadha'a, 30 hiqqa, and 40 thaniyya (6th year), all of which must be pregnant. Their proofs include a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifying 40 pregnant camels, the practice of 'Umar and Zayd (30 hiqqa and 30 jadha'a), and a rational argument: since shibh al-amd is more severe than khata', the diyah should be more stringent (mugallazah). Reducing the number of categories (from five in khata' to three) increases stringency, whereas four categories (as per Shaykhayn) provide less severity. The commentary does not give a tarjih between these views, but the matn presents the Shaykhayn view first, which is often the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A she-camel that has entered its second year.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A she-camel that has entered its third year.
حقة (hiqqa): A she-camel that has entered its fourth year.
جذعة (jadha'a): A she-camel that has entered its fifth year.
ثنية (thaniyya): A she-camel that has entered its sixth year; in this dispute, required to be pregnant.
خلفة (khalifah): A pregnant she-camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Five categories

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position for diyah of shibh al-amd is the Shaykhayn view: 100 camels in four equal categories of 25 each.
