Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
12 min
Dispute on Camel Composition for Shibh Amd Diyah
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute over diyah camel categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the division of diyah camels for shibh amd and evaluate the proofs for the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school divides the 100 diyah camels into four equal quarters; Muhammad and Shafi'i divide into three categories with 40 pregnant.

This passage delves into a detailed question of diyat: how exactly are the 100 camels for shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing) to be categorized? The dispute is both within the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf vs. their student Muhammad) and across madhhabs (Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad). Understanding the proof structure here will sharpen your ability to weigh conflicting hadith and evaluate the concept of taghliz (severity) in diyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, clearly note the view of the Shaykhain (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): the 100 camels are divided into four equal quarters (25 from each of four age categories). Second, note the view of Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i: three categories – 30 hiqqah, 30 jadha'ah, and 40 pregnant thaniyyah.
The text specifies the camel ages: bint labun (year 3), hiqqah (year 4), jadha'ah (year 5), thaniyyah (year 6).
2
Examine the proofs for Muhammad and Shafi'i
They cite a hadith: 'Beware! The slain of shibh amd... for it is 100 camels, forty of them with their offspring in their bellies.' They also rely on narrations from Umar and Zaid bin Thabit (30 hiqqah and 30 jadha'ah) and a rational argument that three categories achieve greater taghliz.
3
Examine the proofs for the Shaykhain
They rely on the general hadith 'For the life of a believer, 100 camels' and the mawquf narration from Ibn Mas'ud that taghliz is in four quarters, which they treat as marfu'. They also argue that if Muhammad's hadith were well-established, the Companions would not have disagreed on the composition.
Ibn Mas'ud's statement is considered like a marfu' hadith because the matter is not subject to qiyas.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the opposing hadith
The Hanafi school argues that the hadith of 40 pregnant camels is not established (ghayr thabit) because despite its existence, the Companions continued to disagree – if it were authentic, it would have settled the dispute. Therefore, the lesser (four quarters) is taken as certain.
This is a methodological argument about the reliability of the hadith.
5
Identify the thamarah and the mufta bihi
The practical effect: under the Shaykhain, the payer must provide 25 of each of four types; under Muhammad, 30+30+40 with 40 pregnant. The text clearly favors the Shaykhain as the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
The taghliz is achieved by the four-quarter division; it applies only when diyah is paid in camels.

كتاب الديات
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد-۱۵
بنت لبون جو تیسرے سال میں لگ جائے چونکہ اس کی ماں اب دوسرا بچہ دے کر دودھ دینے لگے گی اس لئے اس کو بنت لبون کہتے ہیں۔ حلقہ جو چوتھے سال میں لگ جائے چونکہ اب یہ استحقاق ہو گا کہ اس پر سوار ہو اور اس پر بوجھ رکھا جائے اس لئے اس کو حقہ کہتے ہیں۔ جذعہ جو پانچویں سال میں لگ جائے کیونکہ اب وہ دانت کر چکا ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو جذعہ کہتے ہیں ، بہر حال شیخین کے نزدیک سو اونٹ کی تفصیل یہ ہے جو مذکور ہوئی۔

قتل خطاء کی دیت میں امام شافعی اور امام محمد کا مسلک
وقال محمد والشافعى اثلاثا ثلثون جذعة وثلثون حقة واربعون ثنية كلها خلفات فى بطونها اولادها لقوله عليه السلام الا ان قتيل خطأ العمد قتيل السوط والعصا وفيه مائة من الابل اربعون منها في بطونها اولادها وعن عمر وزيد ثلثون حقة وثلثون جذعة ولان دية شبه العمد اغلظ وذالك فيما قلنا

ترجمہ اور محمد اور شافعی نے فرمایا تین قسم کے اونٹ ہوں گے ہمیں جذعے اور میں حقے اور چالیس ٹینیسے (وہ نیے ) سب کے سب حاملہ ہوں جن کے پیٹوں میں ان کی اولاد ہو، نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے آگاہ ہو جاؤ شبہ عمد کا مقتول وہ کوڑے اور لاٹھی کا مقتول ہے اور اس میں سو اونٹ ہیں ان میں سے چالیس ایسے ہوں جن کے پیٹوں میں ان کی اولاد ہو اور عمر اور زید سے منقول ہے میں حقے ، اور تمہیں جذعے اور اس لئے کہ شبہ عمد کی دیت زیادہ غلیظ ہے اور یہ ایسی صورت میں ہے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہیں۔ تشریح امام محمد اور امام شافعی نے سو اونٹ کو چار قسم کے بجائے تین قسم پر منقسم کیا ہے یعنی جذعے میں ہوں اور حقے تمیں ہوں ٹھی چالیس ہوں بہمنی مذکر کے لئے اور مادہ کے لئے ثنیہ ہے اور یہ سب چالیس ٹیسے حاملہ ہوں ، حاملہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ان کے پیٹ میں ان کی اولاد ہو۔
اس پر تو سب متفق ہیں کہ شبہ عد کے دیت میں تغلیظ ہے حضرات شیخین نے چار تم پر منقسم کرنے کو تغلیظ سمجھا اورامام محمد اورشافعی نے وجوب ثنیہ میں تغلیظ کبھی اور تھی وہ ہے جو چھٹے سال میں لگ جائے اور مؤنث ثنیہ" ہے اس وقت حاملہ ہوگی ۔ اور خلفہ " کے معنی ہیں حاملہ اولى في بطونها اولادها خلفات کی صفت کا شفہ ہے۔
اور ان حضرات نے اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا ہے جو اس سے پہلے چند مرتبہ گزر چکی ہے البتہ یہاں پہلے سے طویل ذکر کی گئی ہے، حدیث الا ان سے اولاد ھا تک ہے، بہر حال حدیث میں صراحت ہے کہ ان سو میں سے چالیس ایسی ہونی چاہئیں جو حاملہ ہوں اور عمر فاروق اور زید بن ثابت سے منقول ہے کہ میں حقے اور میں جذعے ہیں لہذا اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ تین قسم کے اونٹ واجب ہوں گے۔ تمیں حقے اور میں جذعے اور چالیس ثنیات، یہ ہے امام محمد اور شافعی کی دلیل نقلی ۔ دلیل عقلی پیش کرتے ہوئے انہوں نے فرمایا کہ شبہ عمر کی دیت سختہ ہوا کرتی ہے اور تختی اس صورت میں ہے جو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ سو اونٹ کا تین حصوں پر حسب مذکور تقسیم کیا جائے۔ ورنہ قتل خطاء کی دیت میں اونٹوں کی پانچ قسمیں ہوتی ہیں تا کہ تغلیظ نہ ہو تو یہاں تین ہو جائیں تاکہ خوب تغلیظ ہو جائے اور چار میں اتنی تغلیظ نہیں ہے جتنی تین میں ہے۔

شیخین کی دلیل
ولهما قوله عليه السلام فى نفس المؤمن مائة من الابل وما روياه غير ثابت لاختلاف الصحابة في صفة فليظ وابن مسعود قال بالتغليظ ارباعا كما ذكرنا وهو كالمرفوع فيعارض به
ترجمہ اور دلیل شیخین بنی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے مؤمن کے نفس میں سو اونٹ ہیں اور وہ حدیث جس کو انہوں نے ( محمد شافعی ) روایت کیا ہے غیر ثابت ہے تغلیظ کی صفت میں صحابہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے اور ابن مسعود تغلیظ کے قائل ہیں چار حصے کرنے کے ساتھ جیسے ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور یہ حدیث ( موقوف ) مثل مرفوع کے ہے پس اس کے ذریعہ معارضہ ہو گا۔ تشریح یہ شیخین کی دلیل ہے پہلی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے، فى نفس المؤمن مائية من الابل جس کو ابن حبان نے صحیح قرار دیا ہے۔
سوال اس حدیث سے شیخین کا استدلال کیسے درست ہے اس میں تو صرف بتایا گیا ہے کہ سو اونٹ واجب میں فریق مخالف بھی اس کا منکر نہیں ہے؟
جواب ... وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ اس میں صرف مطلق سو اونٹ ہیں اور یہ اضافہ جو آپ نے کیا ہے وہ مقدار واجب پر زیادتی ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسے مواقع میں مقادیر قیاسی تک بندیوں سے معلوم نہیں ہوسکتیں محمد اور شافعی نے جو حدیث بیان کی ہے اگر چہ وہ حدیث مرفوع ہے مگر اس کو غیر ثابت شمار کریں گے اس لئے کہ اگر وہ ثابت ہوتی تو تغلیظ کی صفت میں جو صحابہ کے درمیان اختلاف شدیدہ نہ ہوتا کیونکہ قول مذکور کا قائل حدیث مذکور سے حجت پکڑ کر دوسرے صحابہ کو خاموش کر دیتا حالانکہ اس حدیث سے صحابہ کے درمیان محاجہ جاری نہیں ہوا ی اسی کے غیر ثابت ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ نیز ابن مسعود سے تغلیظ کا وہ طریقہ منقول ہے جو شیخین کا مسلک ہے اگر چہ ابن مسعودؓ نے حدیث مرفوع پیش نہیں کی ۔ لیکن یہ بات غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہے اس وجہ سے اس قول صحابی کو حدیث مرفوع کے درجہ میں رکھا جائے گا۔ اور جب یہ حدیث مرفوع کے درجہ میں ہو گئی تو اب اس میں اور محمد د شافعی والی حدیث کے درمیان معارضہ ہو گا اور بوقت تعارض ادنی کو لینا متیقن ہونے کی وجہ سے اولیٰ ہوگا اور ادنیٰ وہ ہے جس کے ہم قائل ہیں۔ نیز شیخین کی دلیل سائب بن یزید کی یہ حدیث بھی ہے کہ آنحضرت نے دیت میں چار قسم کے سو اونٹوں کا فیصلہ فرمایا تھا۔ سوال ہو سکتا ہے کہ یقتل خطاء میں فرمایا ہو اور ہم شبہ عمد میں گفتگو کر رہے ہیں؟ جواب قتل خطاء میں سو اونٹ پانچ قسم کے واجب ہوتے ہیں لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہ شبہ عمدہی کا ذکر ہے نہ کہ قتل خطا ء کا ۔

تغلیظ صرف اونٹوں میں خاص ہے
قال ولا يثبت التغليظ الاقى والابل خاصة لأن التوقيف فيه فان قضى بالدية فى غير الابل لم يتغلظ لما قلنا
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور تغلیظ ثابت نہ ہو گی مگر خاص طور سے اونٹ ہی میں اس لئے کہ ( شارع کی طرف سے ) تو قیف اونٹ
Book of Diyat. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 15. Bint labun: which enters the third year; since its mother now gives birth to a second calf and begins giving milk, it is called bint labun. Hiqqah: which enters the fourth year; since now it deserves to be ridden and loaded, it is called hiqqah. Jadha'ah: which enters the fifth year; because it has now shed its baby teeth, it is called jadha'ah. In any case, according to the two shaykhs, the detail of one hundred camels is as mentioned.

Madhhab of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad regarding the diyah of qatl khata'. And Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said: in thirds: thirty jadha'ah, thirty hiqqah, and forty thaniyyah, all of them pregnant (khalifat) with their offspring in their bellies, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Beware! The slain of shibh amd is the slain of the whip and stick, and for it is one hundred camels, forty of them with their offspring in their bellies.' And from Umar and Zaid: thirty hiqqah and thirty jadha'ah. And because the diyah of shibh amd is more severe, and that is in what we have said.

Translation: And Muhammad and Shafi'i said: There will be three types of camels: thirty jadha'ah and thirty hiqqah and forty thaniyyah (they are [?]) all of them pregnant, with their offspring in their bellies, due to the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Be aware, the slain of shibh amd is the slain of the whip and stick, and in it are one hundred camels, forty of them with their offspring in their bellies.' And it is narrated from Umar and Zaid: thirty hiqqah and thirty jadha'ah. And because the diyah of shibh amd is more severe, and this is in the case we have described. Explanation: Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i divided the one hundred camels into three types instead of four: thirty jadha'ah, thirty hiqqah, and forty thaniyyah. 'Thaniyyah' is for male and 'thaniyyah' for female, and all these forty thaniyyah are pregnant. Pregnant means they have their offspring in their bellies.

All agree that there is taghliz (severity) in the diyah of shibh amd. The two shaykhs considered division into four parts as taghliz, while Imam Muhammad and Shafi'i considered taghliz in the obligation of thaniyyah; thaniyyah is the one that enters the sixth year, and the feminine is thaniyyah, and at that time it will be pregnant. And 'khalifah' means pregnant. 'Ula fi butuniha awladuha' is a description of 'khalifat'.

And these gentlemen inferred from this hadith which has been mentioned several times before, but here it is mentioned longer. The hadith from 'ala inna' to 'awladuha' is included. In any case, the hadith clearly states that forty of these hundred should be pregnant. And it is narrated from Umar Faruq and Zaid bin Thabit: thirty hiqqah and thirty jadha'ah. Therefore, from this detail it is known that three types of camels are obligatory: thirty hiqqah, thirty jadha'ah, and forty thaniyyat. This is the transmitted proof (dalil naqli) of Imam Muhammad and Shafi'i. Presenting a rational proof (dalil aqli), they said that the diyah of shibh amd is severe, and severity is in the case we have stated, i.e., dividing the hundred camels into three parts as mentioned. Otherwise, in the diyah of qatl khata', there are five types of camels so that there is no taghliz; here there are three types so that there is strong taghliz, and four does not have as much taghliz as three.

Proof of the two shaykhs: And for them is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'For the life of a believer, one hundred camels.' And the hadith they (Muhammad and Shafi'i) narrated is not established due to the ikhtilaf of the Companions regarding the description of taghliz. And Ibn Mas'ud said taghliz is in four quarters as we mentioned, and this is like marfu' and thus contradicts it.

Translation: And the proof of the two shaykhs is the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'For the life of a believer, one hundred camels.' And that hadith which they (Muhammad and Shafi'i) narrated is not established because of the ikhtilaf of the Companions in the description of taghliz. And Ibn Mas'ud is of the opinion of taghliz in four parts as we mentioned, and this hadith (mawquf) is like marfu', so it will contradict. Explanation: This is the proof of the two shaykhs. The first proof is this hadith: 'Fi al-mu'min mi'atu min al-ibil' which Ibn Hibban declared sahih.

Question: How is the inference of the two shaykhs valid from this hadith? It only states that one hundred camels are obligatory, and the opposing party also does not deny that.
Answer: The reason for inference is that it only mentions absolute one hundred camels, and this addition that you have made is an increase over the obligatory amount. Moreover, in such situations, amounts cannot be known through analogical rulings. The hadith that Muhammad and Shafi'i narrated, even if it is marfu', will be considered unestablished because if it were established, there would not have been such strong disagreement among the Companions in the description of taghliz, since the proponent of the said statement would have used the hadith as a proof and silenced other Companions. However, no argumentation occurred among the Companions using this hadith; this is proof of its non-establishment. Also, from Ibn Mas'ud, the method of taghliz that is the madhhab of the two shaykhs is narrated, even though Ibn Mas'ud did not present a marfu' hadith. But this matter is not subject to qiyas, so this Companion's statement will be placed at the level of a marfu' hadith. And when it becomes at the level of marfu', then there will be a contradiction between it and the hadith of Muhammad and Shafi'i. And in case of contradiction, taking the lesser (adna) is preferred because it is certain, and the lesser is what we hold. Also, the proof of the two shaykhs is the hadith of Sa'ib bin Yazid that the Prophet (peace be upon him) adjudicated one hundred camels of four types for diyah. Question: He might have said that in qatl khata', while we are discussing shibh amd? Answer: In qatl khata', one hundred camels are wajib in five types; thus it is known that this is the mention of shibh amd, not qatl khata'.

Taghliz is specific to camels only: He (al-Quduri) said: Taghliz will not be established except specifically in camels, because the tawqif is regarding it. So if diyah is adjudged in other than camels, it will not be severe, due to what we have said. Translation: Quduri said: Taghliz will not be established except specifically in camels, because the tawqif (divine guidance) is regarding camels.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the composition of the diyah (blood money) for shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing). The diyah is 100 camels, but scholars differ on the breakdown by age and condition. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, referred to as al-Shaykhain) holds that the 100 camels are divided into four equal parts of 25 each from four different age categories. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Abu Hanifa's student) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that they are divided into three categories: 30 jadha'ah (5-year-old camels), 30 hiqqah (4-year-old camels), and 40 thaniyyah (6-year-old camels), all 40 of the thaniyyah being pregnant. The text first defines the camel ages, then presents Muhammad and Shafi'i's position, their proofs (a hadith and narrations from Umar and Zaid), and their rational argument that three categories provide greater severity (taghliz) than four. It then presents the Shaykhain's proof: the general hadith 'for a believer's life 100 camels' along with a mawquf narration from Ibn Mas'ud that the division is into four quarters, which is treated as marfu'. They also argue that Muhammad and Shafi'i's hadith is not well-established because it did not resolve the Companions' disagreement. Finally, the text affirms that taghliz applies only when diyah is paid in camels, not in other commodities, as per al-Quduri's statement.

Key Terms
بنت لبون (bint labun): A female camel that has entered its third year and whose mother is now giving milk for a second calf.
حقة (hiqqah): A camel that has entered its fourth year and is ready to be ridden and loaded.
جذعة (jadha'ah): A camel that has entered its fifth year and has shed its baby teeth.
ثنية (thaniyyah): A camel that has entered its sixth year; the feminine form is thāniyyah, and in this context, it is pregnant.
خلفة (khalifah): A pregnant camel with offspring in its belly.
تغليظ (taghliz): Severity or strictness in the diyah, achieved by increasing the value or requiring pregnant camels of higher age categories.
شبہ عمد (shibh amd): Quasi-intentional killing; killing with an instrument that usually does not kill (e.g., whip or stick), where the intent is not to kill but the act leads to death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Shaykhain), the diyah for shibh amd is divided into how many categories of camels?
A) Two categories
B) Three categories
C) Four categories
D) Five categories

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's reliance on the general hadith and Ibn Mas'ud's statement leads to a four-quarter division of the diyah for shibh amd, which is the mufta bihi position despite intra-madhhab disagreement.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
10 min
Proof of Shaykhayn for Aggravated Diyah in Shibh Amd and Its Limitation to Camels
Proving the Hanafi position on aggravated diyah and refuting the opposing narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the composition of aggravated diyah in shibh amd and explain why the aggravation is restricted to camels.

Core Idea
The aggravated diyah in shibh amd is 100 camels in four categories, restricted to camels by textual specification.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi proof for the aggravated diyah (taghliz) in cases of quasi-intentional killing (shibh amd). The text presents the reasoning of the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and refutes the opposing view. You will learn the evidence from hadith and companion statements that establish the four-category division and the exclusive application to camels.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Shaykhayn hold the diyah for shibh amd is 100 camels in four categories (رباع), and taghliz applies only to camels.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing school (Shafi'i) claims a different composition, possibly five categories.
The text attributes this view to Muhammad (possibly al-Shaybani in a different riwayah) and Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the three proofs: hadith 'fi nafs al-mu'min mi'at min al-ibil', Ibn Mas'ud's statement (treated as marfu'), and the hadith of Sa'ib ibn Yazid about four categories.
The first proof establishes the amount; the second specifies the division; the third confirms four categories.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing narration
The opposing narration is rejected because if it were authentic, the Companions would not have disagreed on the description of taghliz.
Ibn Mas'ud's view is given weight as it is not reachable by qiyas, so it is treated as marfu'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis require the diyah to be paid in four categories of camels; Shafi'is require a different categorization, affecting the types and numbers of camels.
Also, if the diyah is paid in other than camels, the aggravation is lost.

ولهما قوله عليه السلام فى نفس المؤمن مائة من الابل وما روياه غير ثابت لاختلاف الصحابة في صفة التغليظ وابن مسعود قال بالتغليظ ارباعا كما ذكرنا وهو كالمرفوع فيعارض به ترجمہ اور دلیل شیخین بنی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے مؤمن کے نفس میں سو اونٹ ہیں اور وہ حدیث جس کو انہوں نے ( محمد و شافعی ) روایت کیا ہے غیر ثابت ہے تغلیظ کی صفت میں صحابہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے اور ابن مسعود تغلیظ کے قائل ہیں چار حصے کرنے کے ساتھ جیسے ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور یہ حدیث ( موقوف ) مثل مرفوع کے ہے پس اس کے ذریعہ معارضہ ہو گا۔ تشریح یہ شیخین کی دلیل ہے پہلی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے، فى نفس المؤمن مائة من الابل جس کو ابن حبان نے صحیح قرار دیا ہے۔ سوال اس حدیث سے شیخین کا استدلال کیسے درست ہے اس میں تو صرف بتایا گیا ہے کہ سو اونٹ واجب میں فریق مخالف بھی اس کا منکر نہیں ہے؟ جواب ... وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ اس میں صرف مطلق سو اونٹ ہیں اور یہ اضافہ جو آپ نے کیا ہے وہ مقدار واجب پر زیادتی ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسے مواقع میں مقادیر قیاسی تک بندیوں سے معلوم نہیں ہوسکتیں محمد اور شافعی نے جو حدیث بیان کی ہے اگر چہ وہ حدیث مرفوع ہے مگر اس کو غیر ثابت شمار کریں گے اس لئے کہ اگر وہ ثابت ہوتی تو تغلیظ کی صفت میں جو صحابہ کے درمیان اختلاف شدیدہ نہ ہوتا کیونکہ قول مذکور کا قائل حدیث مذکور سے حجت پکڑ کر دوسرے صحابہ کو خاموش کر دیتا حالانکہ اس حدیث سے صحابہ کے درمیان محاجہ جاری نہیں ہوا ی اسی کے غیر ثابت ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ نیز ابن مسعود سے تغلیظ کا وہ طریقہ منقول ہے جو شیخین کا مسلک ہے اگر چہ ابن مسعودؓ نے حدیث مرفوع پیش نہیں کی ۔ لیکن یہ بات غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہے اس وجہ سے اس قول صحابی کو حدیث مرفوع کے درجہ میں رکھا جائے گا۔ اور جب یہ حدیث مرفوع کے درجہ میں ہو گئی تو اب اس میں اور محمد و شافعی والی حدیث کے درمیان معارضہ ہو گا اور بوقت تعارض ادنی کو لینا متیقن ہونے کی وجہ سے اولیٰ ہوگا اور ادنیٰ وہ ہے جس کے ہم قائل ہیں۔ نیز شیخین کی دلیل سائب بن یزید کی یہ حدیث بھی ہے کہ آنحضرت نے دیت میں چار قسم کے سو اونٹوں کا فیصلہ فرمایا تھا۔ سوال ہو سکتا ہے کہ یقتل خطاء میں فرمایا ہو اور ہم شبہ عمد میں گفتگو کر رہے ہیں؟ جواب قتل خطاء میں سو اونٹ پانچ قسم کے واجب ہوتے ہیں لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہ شبہ عمدہی کا ذکر ہے نہ کہ قتل خطا ء کا ۔ تغلیظ صرف اونٹوں میں خاص ہے قال ولا يثبت التغليظ إلا في الإبل خاصة لأن التوقيف فيه فان قضى بالدية فى غير الابل لم يتغلظ لما قلنا ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور تغلیظ ثابت نہ ہو گی مگر خاص طور سے اونٹ ہی میں اس لئے کہ ( شارع کی طرف سے ) توقیف اونٹ کے سلسلہ میں ہے پس اگر اونٹ کے غیر میں دیت کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے تو دیت مغلظہ نہ ہوگی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح شبہ عمد میں دیت مغلظہ واجب ہوتی ہے جس کا بیان ابھی گزرا ہے لیکن چونکہ شریعت نے تغلیظ کوصرف اونٹوں میں خاص کر دیا ہے اور اس پر اجماع امت منعقد ہو چکا ہے۔ لہذا تغلیظ کا کوئی اور طریقہ مذکورہ طریقہ کے علاوہ نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ مقدرات شریعہ میں قیاسی تک بندیوں کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے بلکہ معرفت مقدرات شریعہ کے لئے نقل چاہئے اور نقل اونٹوں کے سلسلہ میں ہے لہذا اگر قاضی نے اونٹ کے علاوہ کے ساتھ فیصلہ کر دیا تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ توقیف کے مغائر ہے۔
Proof of the two Shaykhs: And for them (is) his saying, peace be upon him: 'In the life of a believer, one hundred camels.' And what they (Muhammad and Shafi'i) narrated is not established, due to the disagreement of the Companions regarding the description of aggravation. And Ibn Mas'ud said regarding aggravation in four parts, as we mentioned, and it is like a marfu' hadith, so it contradicts (the other). Translation: The proof of the two Shaykhs is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'In the life of a believer, one hundred camels.' And the hadith that they (Muhammad and Shafi'i) narrated is not established, because of the disagreement of the Companions about the description of aggravation. And Ibn Mas'ud is of the view of aggravation in four parts, as we mentioned. And this hadith (mawquf) is like marfu', so it will contradict. Explanation: This is the proof of the two Shaykhs. The first proof is this hadith 'fi nafs al-mu'min mi'at min al-ibil' which Ibn Hibban declared authentic. Question: How is the deduction of the two Shaykhs correct from this hadith? It only states that one hundred camels are obligatory, which even the opponent does not deny. Answer: The reasoning is that it mentions only absolute one hundred camels, and the increase that you made is an addition to the obligatory amount. And in such matters, quantities cannot be known through analogical deductions. The hadith that Muhammad and Shafi'i narrated, although it is marfu', will be considered unestablished, because if it had been established, there would not have been intense disagreement among the Companions regarding the description of aggravation, since the proponent of the mentioned view would have silenced the other Companions by presenting the hadith. Yet, no argumentation based on this hadith occurred among the Companions; this is evidence of its non-establishment. Also, from Ibn Mas'ud, that method of aggravation is transmitted, which is the school of the two Shaykhs. Although Ibn Mas'ud did not present a marfu' hadith, this matter is not reachable by analogy, so this Companion's statement will be placed in the rank of a marfu' hadith. And when it becomes like a marfu' hadith, then between it and the hadith of Muhammad and Shafi'i there will be contradiction. And at the time of contradiction, taking the lesser is preferable due to certainty, and the lesser is what we hold. Also, the proof of the two Shaykhs is the hadith of Sa'ib ibn Yazid that the Prophet adjudicated one hundred camels in four types in diyah. Question: It may be that this was in qatl khat'a, while we are discussing shibh amd. Answer: In qatl khat'a, one hundred camels are obligatory in five types, so it is known that this refers to shibh amd, not qatl khat'a. Aggravation is specific to camels. He said: And aggravation is not established except specifically for camels, because the textual specification (tawqeef) is concerning them. So if he adjudicates diyah in other than camels, it will not be aggravated, due to what we said. Translation: Quduri said: And aggravation will not be established except specifically in camels, because the textual specification is concerning camels. So if a decision is made for diyah in other than camels, the aggravated diyah will not obtain, due to the proof we have mentioned. Explanation: In shibh amd, the aggravated diyah is obligatory, as was mentioned. But since Shari'ah has restricted aggravation to camels specifically, and there is consensus of the Ummah on this, therefore no other method of aggravation besides the mentioned method will be possible, because in the determined quantities of Shari'ah, analogical deductions have no place; rather, for knowledge of the determined quantities of Shari'ah, transmitted text is needed, and the transmitted text is concerning camels. Therefore, if a judge decides with other than camels, his decision will not be implemented, because it contradicts the textual specification.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school (represented by the Shaykhayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the opposing view attributed to Muhammad (possibly another scholar) and Imam al-Shafi'i. The issue is the composition of the aggravated diyah (taghliz) in shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing). The Shaykhayn argue that the diyah is 100 camels in four categories (as per Ibn Mas'ud's statement, treated as marfu'), and that the aggravation applies only to camels, not to other forms of payment. They support this with the hadith 'fi nafs al-mu'min mi'at min al-ibil' (100 camels) and the practice of Ibn Mas'ud. They reject the opposing narration on the grounds that if it were authentic, the Companions would not have differed. The text also argues that the aggravation is specific to camels because it is based on tawqeef (textual specification) and consensus. The commentary explains the reasoning behind the Shaykhayn's position and the importance of adhering to transmitted texts rather than qiyas in matters of divinely determined quantities.

Key Terms
تغلیظ (taghliz): Aggravation, intensification of the diyah due to the gravity of the killing, making it heavier in quantity or quality.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the principal disciples of Abu Hanifa.
شبہ عمد (shibh amd): Quasi-intentional killing: where the act is intentional (e.g., striking) but not intended to kill.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn, what is the proof for the diyah being 100 camels in four categories in shibh amd?
A) A mutawatir hadith from the Prophet directly stating four categories
B) The hadith 'fi nafs al-mu'min mi'at min al-ibil' combined with the statement of Ibn Mas'ud treated as marfu'
C) Consensus of the Companions on four categories
D) Qiyas on the diyah of qatl khat'a

Key Takeaway
The aggravated diyah in shibh amd is 100 camels in four categories, and aggravation applies only to camels due to textual specification.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner
6 min
Diyah on Aqila and Kaffarah on the Killer in Qatl Khat'a
Stating the allocation of diyah and kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which party bears the diyah and which bears the kaffarah in qatl khat'a and explain the basis for this allocation.

Core Idea
In unintentional killing, the financial penalty is on the tribe (aqila), not the killer, while expiation is the killer's personal duty.

This lesson presents a foundational ruling from the matn of al-Quduri concerning unintentional homicide (qatl khat'a). The passage distinguishes the two obligations that arise: the blood money (diyah) and the expiation (kaffarah), and crucially assigns them to different parties. Understanding this allocation is essential for correctly applying the law of jinayat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two obligations
In qatl khat'a, two separate duties arise: diyah (financial compensation) and kaffarah (spiritual expiation). Recognize that both are wajib.
Diyah is a monetary payment; kaffarah is an act of worship (freeing a slave or fasting).
2
Assign each obligation to its responsible party
The text states that diyah is upon the aqila (the killer's tribe or paternal relatives) and kaffarah is upon the killer himself. Memorize this assignment.
The aqila is not the killer; it is a group of relatives who share the financial burden.
3
Note the proof
The commentator refers to a previous proof from the beginning of the Book of Jinayat, based on a Quranic verse. Understand that the ruling is textually grounded.
The specific verse is not repeated here, but the source is authoritative.
4
Understand the wisdom
The killer is excused from the heavy financial burden because the death was unintended; however, he must still expiate the sin.
This balances justice and mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قتل خطاء میں دیت عاقلہ پر اور کفارہ قاتل پر ہے
قال وقتل الخطأ تجب به الدية على العاقلة والكفارة على القاتل لما بينا من قبل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قتل خطاء اس کی وجہ سے عاقلہ پر دیت اور قاتل پر کفارہ واجب ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح آیت میں صراحہ مذکور ہے کہ قتل خطاء میں دیت اور کفارہ واجب ہے لیکن کفارہ قاتل پر ہے اور دیت عاقلہ پر جس کی وجہ اوائل کتاب الجنایات میں مذکور ہے۔
In qatl khat'a, the diyah is on the aqila and the kaffarah is on the killer. He said: And qatl khat'a obligates the diyah upon the aqila and the kaffarah upon the killer, due to what we have previously explained. Translation: Quduri said: And qatl khat'a, because of it, the diyah is wajib on the aqila and the kaffarah on the killer, due to the proof we have mentioned earlier. Explanation: In the verse, it is explicitly mentioned that in qatl khat'a, diyah and kaffarah are wajib, but the kaffarah is on the killer and the diyah is on the aqila, the reason for which was mentioned in the beginning of the Book of Jinayat.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Quduri, as explained by the commentator. It establishes that in unintentional killing (qatl khat'a), two obligations arise: the diyah (blood money) is payable by the aqila (the tribe or group of relatives of the killer), and the kaffarah (expiation) is payable by the killer himself. The commentator notes that this is based on a clear Quranic verse and the detailed proof was given earlier in the Book of Jinayat. The distinction is important: the killer is excused from paying the heavy financial burden because the death was accidental, but he must still expiate his sin.

Key Terms
قتل خطاء (qatl khat'a): Unintentional killing, where there is no intent to kill or cause death.
عاقلہ (aqila): The tribe or group of paternal relatives of the killer who are responsible for paying the diyah in cases of qatl khat'a.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation required for unintentional killing, which is freeing a believing slave or fasting for two consecutive months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In qatl khat'a, who is responsible for paying the diyah?
A) The killer alone
B) The aqila (tribe/relatives) of the killer
C) The state treasury
D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
In qatl khat'a, the diyah is the responsibility of the aqila, while the kaffarah is the personal duty of the killer, based on Quranic text and Hanafi fiqh.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyah in Qatl Khat'a: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Difference on Camel Categories
Explaining the five categories of camels in diyah for unintentional killing and the minor difference with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi composition of diyah for qatl khat'a and explain the Shafi'i alternative, citing the narration of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
The diyah for accidental killing is 100 camels in five categories; only one camel type differs between Hanafi and Shafi'i.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the composition of diyah (blood money) for unintentional killing (qatl khat'a). The diyah consists of 100 camels divided into five age categories, as transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud. We will explore the minor disagreement with the Shafi'i school regarding one specific category and the proof for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
List the five categories of camels in the Hanafi diyah
Identify each type and quantity as stated by Quduri: 20 bint makhad, 20 bint labun, 20 ibn makhad, 20 hiqqah, 20 jadha'ah.
These are standard ages for female and male camels.
2
Identify the disputed category
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i replaces 20 ibn makhad (one-year-old male) with 20 ibn labun (two-year-old male).
All other categories are agreed upon.
3
Examine the common dalil
Both schools rely on the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet adjudicated in a case of qatl khat'a with five categories (akhmās).
The Hanafi school treats this as a marfu' hadith.
4
Analyze the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi version is considered lighter (akhaff) and thus more suitable for the excused mistaken killer. The Hanafi narration is the proof against the Shafi'i alternative.
Lighter here means younger camels, which are generally less valuable.
5
Determine the practical effect
In practice, the value of the diyah differs because ibn makhad (1-year-old male) is typically less valuable than ibn labun (2-year-old male).
The difference is minor and does not affect the overall structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والدية في الخطأ من الابل اخماسًا عشرون بنت مخاض وعشرون بنت لبون وعشرون ابن مخاض وعشرون حقة وعشرون جذعة وهذا قول ابن مسعود
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور خطاء میں پانچ قسم کے سو اونٹ ہیں بیس بنت مخاض اور بیس بنت لبون اور بیس ابن مخاض اور بیس حقے اور بیس جمعے اور یہی ابن مسعود کا قول ہے۔ تشریح قتل خطاء کی دیت اگر اونٹ سے ادا کرنی ہو تو اس کی مقدار سو اونٹ ہے جس کے اندر یہ پانچ قسم کے اونٹ ہوں گے جو یہاں مذکور ہیں اور یہ ابن مسعود کا قول ہے اور اس کو حدیث مرفوع کے درجہ میں شمار کیا گیا ہے۔
وانما اخذنا نحن والشافعی به لروايته ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى فى قتيل قتل خطأ أخماسا على نحو ما قال ولان ما قلناه اخف فكان اليق بحالة الخطأ لان الخاطى معذور غير ان عند الشافعى يقضى بعشرين ابن لبون مكان ابن مخاض والحجة عليه ماروينا
ترجمہ اور ہم نے اور امام شافعی نے اس کو ( قول ابن مسعود گو ) لیا ہے ابن مسعودؓ کے روایت کرنے کی وجہ سے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قتل خطاء کے مقتول میں ان کے قول کے مثل پانچ قسم کے اونٹوں کا فیصلہ فرمایا اور اس لئے کہ یہ جس کے ہم قائل ہیں ہلکا ہے تو یہ حالت خطاء کے مناسب ہے کیونکہ خاطی معذور ہے مگر امام شافعی کے نزدیک ابن مخاض کی جگہ بیس ابن لبون کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا اور ان پر حجت وہ ہے جو ہم نے روایت کیا۔
He said: And the diyah in khat'a from camels is in five parts: twenty bint makhad, twenty bint labun, twenty ibn makhad, twenty hiqqah, and twenty jadha'ah. This is the statement of Ibn Mas'ud. Translation: Quduri said: And in khat'a, there are one hundred camels in five types: twenty bint makhad, twenty bint labun, twenty ibn makhad, twenty hiqqah, and twenty jadha'ah. And this is the statement of Ibn Mas'ud. Explanation: The diyah of qatl khat'a, if it is to be paid with camels, then its quantity is one hundred camels, which include these five types mentioned here. And this is the statement of Ibn Mas'ud, and it is counted in the rank of a marfu' hadith. And we and al-Shafi'i have taken it due to his (Ibn Mas'ud's) narration that the Prophet, peace be upon him, adjudicated in a case of a person killed by mistake in five parts, similar to what he (Ibn Mas'ud) said. And because what we say is lighter, it is more appropriate for the state of khat'a, because the mistaken person is excused. However, according to al-Shafi'i, he adjudicates with twenty ibn labun in place of ibn makhad. And the proof against him is what we have narrated.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage explains the composition of the diyah in qatl khat'a according to the Hanafi school, citing Quduri and Ibn Mas'ud. It states that the diyah is 100 camels divided into five categories: 20 bint makhad (one-year-old female), 20 bint labun (two-year-old female), 20 ibn makhad (one-year-old male), 20 hiqqah (three-year-old female), and 20 jadha'ah (four-year-old female). The commentator notes that this is the view of Ibn Mas'ud, treated as a marfu' hadith. Then it highlights a minor inter-madhhab dispute: both Hanafis and Shafi'is accept the five-category scheme, but Shafi'is replace 20 ibn makhad with 20 ibn labun (two-year-old male). The Hanafi argument is that their version is lighter (and thus more appropriate for an accidental killing) and that their narration is the proof against the Shafi'i position.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel that has entered its second year (one-year-old).
ابن مخاض (ibn makhad): A male camel that has entered its second year.
حقة (hiqqah): A female camel that has entered its fourth year (three-year-old).
جذعة (jadha'ah): A female camel that has entered its fifth year (four-year-old).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which camel is included in the diyah of qatl khat'a that the Shafi'i school replaces with ibn labun?
A) 20 bint makhad
B) 20 ibn makhad
C) 20 hiqqah
D) 20 jadha'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyah for qatl khat'a consists of 100 camels in five categories, with 20 ibn makhad uniquely differentiated from the Shafi'i school's 20 ibn labun.

Diyat — Blood Money

Aggravated Blood Money: Camel-Restricted
States ruling that taghliz is only with camels by shari'ah and ijma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the invalidity of taghliz with non-camel property and explain the proof based on ijma' and the principle that muqaddarat are tawqifi.

Core Idea
Taghliz is only valid with camels; qadi's ruling otherwise is void.

In Hanafi fiqh, aggravated blood money (diyat mughallazah) for quasi-intentional murder is a fixed penalty. This passage clarifies that the aggravation is exclusively tied to camels. If a judge rules otherwise, the decision is null and void. This restriction is based on textual evidence and consensus, not analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Subject
Clearly state what is being ruled upon: a qadi's decision to impose taghliz with property other than camels. The ruling: such a decision is invalid (nafidh nahi).
The ruling concerns the validity of a judicial decision, not the diyat itself.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The passage cites two proofs: (1) the Shari'ah has restricted taghliz to camels (implicitly from texts), and (2) there is consensus (ijma') of the Ummah on this restriction. Identify these as the basis.
The text does not quote a specific verse or hadith, but relies on the established principle.
3
Understand the Principle of Muqaddarat
The passage explains that fixed amounts (muqaddarat) in Shari'ah are not subject to qiyas (analogy); they are known only through transmitted texts (naql). Therefore, one cannot extend taghliz to other property.
This is a key usul principle: tawqif (divine restriction) overrides human reasoning in fixed penalties.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
While not elaborated, the text implies that other schools may allow taghliz with other valuables. Recognize this as an area of legitimate disagreement.
The Hanafi position is based on ijma', which is a strong proof.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the transmitted texts and ijma'. Since qiyas is excluded in muqaddarat, the camel-only rule is definitive. Hence the mufta bihi is that taghliz is exclusively with camels.
This is the basis for invalidating any qadi's ruling to the contrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پس اگر اونٹ کے غیر میں دیت کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے تو دیت مغلظہ نہ ہوگی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح شبہ عمد میں دیت مغلظہ واجب ہوتی ہے جس کا بیان ابھی گزرا ہے لیکن چونکہ شریعت نے تغلیظ کوصرف اونوں میں خاص کر دیا ہے اور اس پر اجماع امت منعقد ہو چکا ہے۔ لہذا تغلیظ کا کوئی اور طریقہ مذکورہ طریقہ کے علاوہ نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ مقدرات شریعہ میں قیاسی تک بندیوں کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے بلکہ معرفت مقدرات شریعہ کے لئے نقل چاہئے اور نقل اونٹوں کے سلسلہ میں ہے لہذا اگر قاضی نے اونٹ کے علاوہ کے ساتھ فیصلہ کر دیا تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ توقیف کے مغائر ہے۔
So if decision of blood money is made with other than camels, then the aggravated blood money will not be. Due to this evidence which we have already mentioned. Explanation: In quasi-intentional killing, aggravated blood money is obligatory as has been discussed earlier, but because the Shari'ah has restricted aggravation only to camels and there is consensus of the ummah on this, therefore any other method of aggravation besides this method will not be, because in the determined amounts of Shari'ah, analogical deductions have no place; rather knowledge of the determined amounts of Shari'ah requires transmitted text, and the transmitted text is concerning camels. Therefore if the judge decided with other than camels, his decision will not be effective, because it contradicts the restriction.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah explaining the ruling on aggravated blood money (diyat mughallazah) in quasi-intentional murder. It states that if a qadi rules that the blood money should be paid with something other than camels, the aggravation is not achieved. The reason is that the Shari'ah explicitly restricted the aggravation to camels, and there is consensus (ijma') of the Ummah on this. Therefore, no other method of aggravation is valid because the fixed amounts (muqaddarat) in Shari'ah are known only through transmitted texts (naql), not through analogy (qiyas). The transmitted texts only mention camels for aggravation. Hence, a qadi's decision to use other property is invalid as it opposes the divine restriction (tawqif).

Key Terms
تغلیظ (taghliz): Aggravation of blood money (diyat) by requiring a higher type or value, here specifically camels.
مقدرات شریعہ (muqaddarat shari'iyya): Fixed amounts determined by Shari'ah, such as the number of camels for diyat; not subject to analogical reasoning.
توقیف (tawqif): A restriction based on divine revelation; here meaning the restriction of taghliz to camels is from Shari'ah and cannot be altered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is invalid because taghliz is only with camels by nass and ijma'.
C) It is valid if the defendant agrees.
D) It is invalid only if the claimant objects.

Key Takeaway
Aggravated blood money (taghliz) in Hanafi fiqh is exclusively payable in camels; any qadi's ruling to the contrary is void.

Categories of Diyat Camels and the Shafi'i Dispute
Specifies the five categories of camels for diyat and discusses the Shafi'i dispute over ibn makhad vs ibn labun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi composition of diyat for accidental killing and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the disputed category and the evidence for each view.

Core Idea
Diyat for accidental killing: 100 camels in five equal categories; only one category (ibn makhad vs ibn labun) is disputed.

This lesson examines the specific composition of blood money (diyah) for accidental killing when paid in camels. While both Hanafis and Shafi'is agree on the five-category division, a minor but notable difference exists regarding one type of camel. We will explore the evidence that leads each school to its position and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the five categories and the total number of camels as recorded in the text from al-Quduri and attributed to Ibn Mas'ud.
The five categories are bint makhad, bint labun, ibn makhad, hiqqah, jadha'ah, each twenty camels.
2
Identify the opposing school and their modification
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with the five-category structure but substitutes ibn labun (two-year-old male) for ibn makhad (one-year-old male).
This is the only point of disagreement in this passage.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (marfu') which explicitly mentions ibn makhad in the five categories.
The hadith is considered strong evidence for the Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing view
The Hanafi response argues that the same hadith is proof against the Shafi'i position because it mentions ibn makhad, not ibn labun. Additionally, the Hanafi composition is lighter (akhaff), which is more suitable for the excused killer in accidental killing.
The principle of ease (takhfif) supports the Hanafi choice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In practice, a Hanafi court includes 20 ibn makhad; a Shafi'i court includes 20 ibn labun instead. This affects the specific camels to be handed over.
The overall number and value may differ slightly depending on camel market conditions.

Also the mistaken person is excused, so there should be leniency in his blood money, and this is a method of leniency. However, there is this difference between our school and Imam al-Shafi'i's school: that (Shafi'i) makes twenty ibn labun obligatory instead of ibn makhad. But the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud will be a proof against him because it mentions ibn makhad, not ibn labun. Khattabi said: I do not know anyone besides Imam al-Shafi'i who made ibn labun obligatory.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the specific composition of the blood money (diyah) for accidental killing when paid in camels. The matn from al-Quduri states that it consists of 100 camels divided into five equal categories of twenty each: bint makhad (one-year-old female), bint labun (two-year-old female), ibn makhad (one-year-old male), hiqqah (three-year-old female), and jadha'ah (four-year-old female). This is attributed to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, which is treated as a marfu' hadith (from the Prophet). The commentary then addresses a minor inter-madhhab dispute: both Hanafis and Shafi'is accept the five-category division based on the hadith, but Shafi'is replace ibn makhad with ibn labun (two-year-old male). The Hanafi position is that ibn makhad is correct because it appears in the hadith narration, and using ibn labun would be a change without evidence. Khattabi is quoted to note that only al-Shafi'i held this view. The Hanafi choice is also argued as being lighter (akhaff) and thus more appropriate for accidental killing where the killer is excused (ma'dhur). The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud is presented as decisive evidence against the Shafi'i position.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel that has entered its second year (one year old).
ابن مخاض (ibn makhad): A male camel that has entered its second year.
ابن لبون (ibn labun): A male camel that has entered its third year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyat composition includes 20 ibn makhad; Shafi'is replace it with ibn labun, but both agree on the five-category system.

Diyah in Gold and Silver: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
States diyah in gold and silver for accidental killing and disputes Shafi'i's amount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi amounts for diyah in gold and silver and explain how the Shafi'i dispute is resolved by weight differences.

Core Idea
The apparent contradiction between 10,000 and 12,000 dirhams is resolved by different weight standards.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling on diyah for accidental killing when paid in gold or silver. It also addresses a well-known dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who cites a hadith suggesting a different silver amount. Understanding how the Hanafi school reconciles the two narrations is crucial for grasping the role of weight standards in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi amounts: 1000 gold dinars or 10,000 silver dirhams of standard weight.
This is the ruling from al-Quduri and the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the silver amount is 12,000 dirhams based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Ibn Abbas narrates that the Prophet judged with 12,000 dirhams for a man from Banu 'Adi.
This hadith is quoted by al-Shafi'i.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school explains that those 12,000 dirhams were of a lighter weight (weight of six), so they equal 10,000 dirhams of the standard weight (weight of seven).
This reconciliation shows that both hadiths yield the same total value.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, a Hanafi judge requires 10,000 standard dirhams; a Shafi'i judge may award 12,000 light dirhams, but the value is the same. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.
The thamarah al-khilaf is minimal because the underlying obligation is identical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن العين الف دينارومن الورق عشرة الاف درهم وقال الشافعى من الورق اثنا عشر الفا لماروى ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قـضـى بذالک ولنا ماروى عن عمر ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قـضـى بالدية في قتيل بعشرة الاف درهم وتاويل ماروى انه قضى من دراهم كان وزنها وزن ستة وقد كانت كذالك ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قتل خطاء کی دیت ) سونے سے ہزار دیوار اور چاندی سے دس ہزار درہم ہیں۔ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ چاندی سے بارہ ہزار درہم ہیں اس لئے کہ ابن عباس نے روایت کیا ہے کہ نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کا فیصلہ فرمایا ( یعنی بارہ ہزار کا بنی عدی کے ایک شخص کے بارے میں ) اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو عمر سے مروی ہے کہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک مقتول کے دس ہزار درہم کی دیت کا فیصلہ فرمایا اور ابن عباس کی روایت کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت کا فیصلہ ان دراہم کے بارے میں تھا۔ جن کا وزن وزن ستہ تھا اور شروع زمانہ میں ایسا ہی تھا۔
تشریح اگر قتل خطاء کی دیت سونے سے ادا کرنا چاہیں تو ایک ہزار دینار اس کی مقدار ہے اور اگر چاندی سے ادا کرنا چاہیں تو اس کی مقدار دس ہزار درہم ہیں ۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کی بارہ ہزار درہم ہے اور امام شافعی نے ابن عباس کی روایت سے استدلال کیا ہے اور صحیفہ نے حضرت عمر کی روایت سے۔ اور حنیفہ نے امام شافعی کی روایت کا جواب یہ دیا ہے کی دراہم کا وزن پہلے کم و بیش رہا ہے ایک زمانہ میں یہ بھی وزن تھا کہ دس درہم اور چھ مثقال کا وزن برابر ہوتا تھا تو ایسی صورت میں درہم کا وزن کم ہو گا اور اس کی مقدار بارہ ہزار درہم مروجہ وزن کے درہم سے دس ہزار بیٹھیں گے لہذا دونوں حدیثوں کا مال ایک ہی ثابت ہوگا۔
تنبیہ ... در هم تین ماشہ ایک رتی اور ایک رتی کا ۱/۵ ہے اور مثقال ۴ ماشہ اور چار رتی کا ہوتا ہے یہ وہی وزن ہے جس میں سات مثقال اور دس درہم کا وزن برابر ہو گا اور اس کو وزن سبعہ کہتے ہیں اور حضرت عمر کے زمانہ سے یہی وزن معتبر ہو گیا تھا۔ باب زکوۃ میں یہی وزن
He said: And from gold a thousand dinars, and from silver ten thousand dirhams. And al-Shafi'i said: from silver twelve thousand, because Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged with that. And we have the narration from Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged for a slain person with ten thousand dirhams. And the interpretation of what is narrated (Ibn Abbas) is that he judged with dirhams whose weight was the weight of six, and it was so in the beginning. Translation: al-Quduri said: And the blood money for accidental killing from gold is a thousand dinars, and from silver ten thousand dirhams. And al-Shafi'i said: from silver twelve thousand dirhams because Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged with that (i.e., twelve thousand for a person of Banu 'Adi). And our evidence is that which is narrated from Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged for a slain person with ten thousand dirhams. And the interpretation of Ibn Abbas' narration is that the Prophet's judgment was concerning dirhams whose weight was the weight of six (i.e., six mithqal for ten dirhams), and that was the case in the early period. Explanation: If one wishes to pay the blood money for accidental killing from gold, then a thousand dinars is its quantity, and if from silver, then its quantity is ten thousand dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is twelve thousand dirhams, and Imam al-Shafi'i argued with the narration of Ibn Abbas, and the Hanafis argued with the narration of Hadrat Umar. And the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i narration is that the weight of dirhams varied in early times. There was a time when ten dirhams and six mithqal were equal in weight, so in that case the dirham weight was light, and its quantity of twelve thousand dirhams (by that light weight) would amount to ten thousand dirhams of the commonly accepted weight. Thus both hadiths yield the same total. Note: The dirham is three mashas, one rati, and one-fifth of a rati; and the mithqal is four mashas and four ratis. This is the same weight in which seven mithqal and ten dirhams are equal, and it is called the weight of seven. From the time of Hadrat Umar, this weight became the standard. In the chapter of zakat, this same weight is used.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage addresses the diyah for accidental killing when paid in gold or silver. According to the Hanafi school (from al-Quduri), it is 1,000 gold dinars or 10,000 silver dirhams. A dispute arises with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that the silver amount is 12,000 dirhams, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi position relies on a hadith from Umar that the Prophet judged with 10,000 dirhams. To reconcile the two narrations, Hanafi scholars explain that the dirhams used in the Prophet's time when the judgment of 12,000 was made were of a lighter weight (a weight system where ten dirhams weighed six mithqals, called 'weight of six'). Under that system, 12,000 light dirhams are equivalent to 10,000 dirhams of the standard weight that became established later (the 'weight of seven' from Umar's time). Thus, the two hadiths do not contradict; they express the same value in different weight standards. The passage concludes with a note (tanbih) clarifying the precise measurements of dirham and mithqal in the Hanafi system: a dirham is approximately 3 mashas and 1.2 ratis (or more precisely, 3 mashas, 1 rati and 1/5 rati), and a mithqal is 4 mashas and 4 ratis. The 'weight of seven' (sab'ah) refers to the system where seven mithqals equal ten dirhams in weight, which became standard from Caliph Umar's reign. This same weight is used in zakat calculations.

Key Terms
دینار (dinar): A gold coin; standard for diyat in gold (1000 dinars).
درہم (dirham): A silver coin; used for diyat (10,000 standard dirhams).
وزن سبعہ (wazn al-sab'ah): The weight system where 10 dirhams equal 7 mithqals; became standard from Umar's time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 12,000 dirhams
B) 10,000 dirhams of standard weight
C) 1,000 dinars
D) 10,000 dirhams of any weight

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes diyah for accidental killing at 1000 gold dinars or 10,000 standard silver dirhams, reconciling conflicting hadiths by recognizing different weight standards.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyat for Accidental Killing: Reconciling the Hadith on Amount
Ruling on diyat amount and reconciliation of conflicting hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the diyat amount for accidental killing and explain how the Hanafi school reconciles the apparently conflicting hadith reports.

Core Idea
Diyat is 10,000 dirhams of standard weight; the 12,000 dirhams report refers to lighter dirhams.

The amount of blood money for accidental killing is established by the Sunna, but two hadith reports seem to give different figures: one from Umar stating 10,000 dirhams, and another from Ibn Abbas stating 12,000 dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i follows the latter, while the Hanafi school holds to the former. This lesson examines how the Hanafis harmonize the two reports by considering the historical variation in the weight of dirhams, a classic example of tawfiq (reconciliation).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the Hanafi ruling on the amount of diyat for accidental killing in gold and silver? Identify the source of this ruling.
The ruling is from Al-Quduri and is Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school disagrees and what amount do they prescribe? What is their evidence?
Imam al-Shafi'i holds 12,000 dirhams based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith from Ibn Abbas: what does it say and why does it appear to contradict the Hanafi position?
The hadith states the Prophet judged 12,000 dirhams for a slain person.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school respond? What is the key insight about the weight of dirhams that resolves the apparent contradiction?
The Hanafis explain that the 12,000 dirhams were of a lighter weight (weight six: 10 dirhams = 6 mithqals), whereas standard weight (weight seven: 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals) yields 10,000 dirhams.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in the ruling between the two schools? Which position is mufta bihi and why?
Hanafis require 10,000 standard dirhams; Shafi'is require 12,000 standard dirhams. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it reconciles both hadiths and relies on the standard weight from Umar's time.

He said: From gold (dinar) one thousand dinars, and from silver (dirham) ten thousand dirhams. Al-Shafi'i said: from silver twelve thousand, because Ibn Abbas (RA) narrated that the Prophet (SAW) judged thus. And our proof is what is narrated from Umar that the Prophet (SAW) judged blood money for a slain person as ten thousand dirhams. And the interpretation of what is narrated (that he judged with twelve thousand) is that he judged with dirhams whose weight was the weight of six (i.e., six dirhams per mithqal), and they were like that. Translation: Quduri said: The diyat for accidental killing from gold is one thousand dinars and from silver ten thousand dirhams. Shafi'i said: from silver twelve thousand dirhams, because Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet judged so (for a person from Banu Adi). And our proof is from Umar that the Prophet judged ten thousand dirhams for a slain person. And the interpretation of Ibn Abbas's narration is that the Prophet's judgment was concerning dirhams whose weight was weight six, and in the beginning it was like that. Explanation: If one wishes to pay diyat for accidental killing from gold, the amount is one thousand dinars; if from silver, ten thousand dirhams. Imam Shafi'i said it is twelve thousand dirhams and he argued with Ibn Abbas's narration. The Hanafis argue with Umar's narration. And the Hanafi response is that the weight of dirhams used to vary; at one time the weight was such that ten dirhams equaled six mithqals, so in that case the dirham's weight would be less, and the amount of twelve thousand dirhams in that weight equals ten thousand in the commonly known weight. Therefore both hadiths agree. Note: A dirham is three mashas and one ratti and one-fifth of a ratti, and a mithqal is four mashas and four rattis. This is the weight where seven mithqals and ten dirhams are equal, called weight seven, and from Umar's time this weight became standard. The same weight is used in the Chapter of Zakat.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the amount of diyat (blood money) for accidental killing (qatl al-khata) and addresses a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i. The author, Al-Quduri, states the ruling: from gold, the diyat is 1,000 dinars; from silver, 10,000 dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that from silver it is 12,000 dirhams, relying on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi school responds with a hadith from Umar ibn al-Khattab that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged 10,000 dirhams. The Hanafis reconcile the two hadiths by explaining that the 12,000 dirhams mentioned in Ibn Abbas's hadith were of a lighter weight (weight six, where 10 dirhams weighed as much as 6 mithqals). In standard weight (weight seven, where 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals), 12,000 of those lighter dirhams equal 10,000 standard dirhams. Thus there is no contradiction. The passage also clarifies the standard weight of dirham and mithqal, which is the same as used in zakat calculations. This is an important example of the Hanafi method of harmonizing apparently conflicting proofs (tawfiq).

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money or monetary compensation paid for unlawful killing (or injury) to the victim's heirs.
القتل الخطأ (qatl al-khata): Accidental killing without intent, e.g., shooting an arrow thinking it was game but killing a person.
وزن سبعة (wazn sab'ah): The standard weight where 10 dirhams equal 7 mithqals; established from Umar's time.

The diyat for accidental killing is 10,000 dirhams of standard weight (or 1,000 dinars), and the conflicting report of 12,000 is reconciled by the lighter weight of those dirhams.

Diyat — Blood Money

Property Types for Diyat: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyat property types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the types of property permissible for diyat, and explain the legal basis for each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa limits diyat to camels, gold, silver; Sahibayn allow also cows, sheep, and garments.

When a killer must pay diyat (blood money), what property types are acceptable? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for applying diyat correctly in practice, as the choice of property affects the obligation's fulfillment and the possibility of taghliz (aggravation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the types allowed by Abu Hanifa (camels, gold, silver) and the additional types allowed by the Sahibayn (cows, sheep, garments). Note that all three types camels, gold, and silver are agreed upon.
The Sahibayn's view includes six total options.
2
Analyze the evidence
For the Sahibayn, the proof is the practice of Caliph Umar (رضي الله عنه). For Abu Hanifa, the proof is rational: estimation (taqdir) requires known monetary value; cows, sheep, and garments have uncertain value, so they cannot serve as a reliable standard.
Abu Hanifa's argument is aqli (rational), while Sahibayn's is naqli (transmitted).
3
Examine the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa counters that Umar's judgment may have been specific to that context, and that generalizing it is problematic because of the unknown value issue. The commentary notes that some jurists later considered the dispute resolved.
The text hints that the difference may be removed (yartafi' al-khilaf).
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: according to Abu Hanifa, the killer has only three options; according to the Sahibayn, he has six. This affects the ease of fulfilling the diyat obligation.
The mufta bihi in the school is the Sahibayn's view, being more flexible and following Umar's precedent.
5
Apply the aggravation rule
Note that taghliz (aggravation) in shibh amd only applies when diyat is paid with camels. If paid with other property, the diyat is identical to khata (accidental killing).
This rule is consistent even under the Sahibayn's view.

He said: Diyat is established only from these three types according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: from them and from cows: two hundred cows, and from sheep: one thousand sheep, and from garments: two hundred garments, each garment being two cloths, because Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) determined thus for each type of property owner. Translation: Quduri said: Diyat is not established except from these three types according to Abu Hanifa. And the two companions said: from these and from cows two hundred cows, and from sheep one thousand sheep, and from garments two hundred garments, each garment two cloths, because Umar decided so for each owner of property. Explanation: When the killer pays diyat, he has a choice among three things: he may pay with camels, or with dinars, or with dirhams, and he may not pay with other than these three things. This is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two companions say that he can also pay from the mentioned three types according to the prescribed amount, and if he pays with cows, it will be two hundred; if with sheep, one thousand; if with garments, two hundred garments, each garment two cloths, which in our custom would be a shirt and a loincloth. Because Umar al-Faruq gave such a judgment for those property owners. This is the proof of the two companions. Note: Some jurists' statements differ here; the question is whether this refers only to accidental killing or both accidental and quasi-intentional. The verified view is that it refers to both, i.e., according to Abu Hanifa, diyat for both quasi-intentional and accidental killing can be paid from the three types, and according to the two companions, from other things mentioned here. Question: Previously it was stated that in quasi-intentional killing, the diyat is aggravated and aggravation applies only to camels; so what is this? Answer: The meaning is that aggravation occurs only with camels, by dividing the camels into the four categories; if diyat is paid with other than camels, aggravation cannot occur. Then there would be no difference between quasi-intentional and accidental killing's diyat, because the method of aggravation is transmitted only for camels. Therefore, if a judge decides aggravation with other than camels, it would not be established due to lack of transmission, and the judge's decision would not be enforced. For details, see Shami volume 5 page 368. The proof of Abu Hanifa: He says: Estimation can only be correct with something of known monetary value, and these things (cows, sheep, garments) are of unknown monetary value, so compensation cannot be estimated with them. Estimation by camels is known through well-known traditions; it is considered from them in other contexts. And it is mentioned in 'Ma'aqil' that if one settles for more than two hundred garments or two hundred cows, it is not permissible. This is a sign that estimation is by that (camels). Then it is said that this is the saying of everyone, so the disagreement is removed.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about the types of property from which diyat (blood money) may be paid. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, diyat is established only from three types: camels, gold (dinars), and silver (dirhams). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) add three more: cows, sheep, and garments (each garment consisting of two cloths, such as a shirt and a loincloth in that time). Their proof is the precedent of Caliph Umar, who applied these categories. The commentary clarifies that this applies to both accidental killing (khata) and quasi-intentional killing (shibh amd) – the diyat for both can be paid from these types. However, the aggravation of diyat (tazhil) in quasi-intentional killing applies only when camels are used, because the method of dividing camels into four categories is transmitted only for camels. If other property is used, no aggravation occurs, and the diyat is the same as for accidental killing. The passage then presents Abu Hanifa's proof: estimation of diyat must be based on something of known monetary value. Cows, sheep, and garments have variable and uncertain values, so they cannot serve as a reliable standard. Camels, on the other hand, have well-established values in the tradition (athar). The passage also notes that some jurists say the disagreement is resolved because the later view of all is that diyat can be paid from these additional types. The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, a killer can only use camels, gold, or dirhams; according to the Sahibayn, he has more options. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn, which is more comprehensive and follows the practice of Umar.

Key Terms
انواع ثلثة (anwa' thalatha): The three types: camels (ibil), gold (dhahab/dinar), silver (fidda/dirham).
حلة (hullah): A garment set consisting of two pieces (e.g., a shirt and a loincloth).
تغليظ (taghliz): Aggravation of diyat by dividing camels into categories (e.g., in shibh amd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, from which types of property can diyat be paid?
A) Camels, gold, and silver only
B) Camels, cows, sheep, and garments
C) Gold and silver only
D) Any type of property

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position allows diyat payment from six types: camels, gold, silver, cows, sheep, and garments; taghliz applies only to camels.

Estimation of Diyat with Cows, Goats, and Suits: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyat estimation items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on diyat estimation using cows, goats, and suits, and explain the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Diyat estimation requires known value; cows, goats, and suits have unknown value, so only camels and cash are valid according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute over the types of property that can be used to estimate diyat (blood money). While Imam Abu Hanifa restricts estimation to items with well-known market values, the Sahibayn argue for a broader list based on a report from Umar ibn al-Khattab. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school navigates between textual evidence and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether diyat can be estimated (taqdir) using cows, goats, and suits of clothing (hulla) in addition to camels, dinars, and dirhams.
The disagreement is intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa argues that estimation is only valid with items whose market value is known and stable. Since cows, goats, and suits have fluctuating values, they cannot be used. He supports this with qiyas (analogy) to guarantee (daman) for property damage, where such items are not used. The well-known reports (athar mashhurah) only establish estimation for camels.
Abu Hanifa acknowledges that camels also have unknown value, but the athar overrides qiyas for camels.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn rely on a narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) transmitted by Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar, which lists specific numbers of cows, goats, and suits for diyat. They take this as establishing a Sharia estimation for those items.
Imam Muhammad's own practice includes all items, but he records that Abu Hanifa only takes camels and cash.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa interprets the Umar report as referring to voluntary reconciliation (sulh), not a fixed Sharia estimation. He maintains that only items with known value (camels, dinars, dirhams) are proper for fixed diyat.
The author states that the more correct view is that the allowance of cows, goats, suits is solely the view of the two companions, not Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the practical consequence and mufta bihi
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, diyat must be paid in camels or cash; under the Sahibayn, payment can also be in cows, goats, or suits if agreed. The mufta bihi (operative position) is the Sahibayn's view for flexibility, but Abu Hanifa's view is also taught.
The author (Ashraf al-Hidaya) gives preference to the view that the permissibility is only the Sahibayn's.

Book of Diyat. And it is said that it is their statement. Translation: Abu Hanifa's proof is that estimation is valid only with something whose value is known, and these items (cow, goat, suit) are of unknown value, therefore estimated guarantee is not established with them. And with the camel, it is known through well-known reports; we found these reports absent in other than the camel. And Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-Aqil that if one reconciles with more than two hundred suits or two hundred cows, it is not permissible, and this is a sign of estimation with them. Then it was said that this is the statement of all, then the disagreement would be removed. And it was said that this is the statement of the two companions. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that estimation can only be correct with something whose value is known, and the value of dinars and dirhams is well-known, so estimation with them is correct. But cows, goats, and suits: their value is unknown, as is apparent. This is the reason that if someone destroys another's property, its guarantee is not assessed with cows, goats, etc. Question: Then the value of the camel is also unknown, so estimation with it should not be correct? Answer: The matter is correct, and analogy also demands this, but what can be done? This estimation is established by well-known reports, so we had to leave analogy. And estimation with cows, goats, etc. is not established by well-known reports, so we acted on analogy. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is complete. Imam Muhammad wrote in the Mabsut, Kitab al-Ma'aqil, that if one reconciles with more than two hundred suits and two hundred cows, the reconciliation will not be valid. Citing this passage, the author says that Imam Muhammad's statement indicates that two hundred suits and two hundred cows are a Sharia estimation. On this, some people said that this mentioned statement is the statement of all, i.e., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad; so if this is established, then there is no disagreement. And some people said that this is only the statement of the two companions (Sahibayn), and this is the correct view, that it is the statement of only the two companions. Because Imam Muhammad narrated in Kitab al-Athar through Abu Hanifa with a sound chain from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that for those of silver, the diyah is ten thousand dirhams; for those of gold, one thousand dinars; for those of cows, two hundred cows; for those of camels, one hundred camels; for those of goats, one thousand goats; and for those of suits, two hundred suits. Then Imam Muhammad said: We adopt all of them, but Abu Hanifa takes from that only the estimation of camels and dirhams and dinars. Hence it is known that the issue of reconciliation is only the statement of the two companions. The response to the two companions' argument can be that in this hadith from which you argued, the two hundred cows and suits are interpreted as referring to reconciliation, and there is no problem with that according to us as well.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the types of property that can be used for the estimation of diyat (blood money). The central issue is whether diyat can be estimated using cows, goats, or suits of clothing (hulla) in addition to camels, dinars, and dirhams. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that estimation is only valid with items whose market value is well-known and stable. Since cows, goats, and suits have fluctuating and unknown values, they cannot be used for estimation; only camels, which have a well-known value established by transmitted reports (athar), and dinars/dirhams, which have known values, can be used. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, relying on a report from Umar ibn al-Khattab that includes these items in the list of diyat payments. Imam Muhammad's citation of that report in Kitab al-Athar, and his statement that he adopts all of them while noting that Abu Hanifa only takes camels and dirhams/dinars, supports the view that the allowance of cows, goats, and suits is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, not Abu Hanifa. The author then mentions a possible reconciliation: the hadith may be interpreted as referring to a voluntary settlement (sulh) rather than a fixed Sharia estimation, thus preserving Abu Hanifa's position. The author concludes that the relied-upon view is that the permissibility of estimation with cows, goats, and suits is solely the view of the two companions.

Key Terms
تقدیر (taqdir): Estimation of the quantity or value of diyat (blood money) as fixed by Sharia.
دیة (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of homicide or bodily harm.
آثار مشہورہ (athar mashhurah): Well-known transmitted reports from the Companions or the Prophet (PBUH) that establish a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why can diyat not be estimated with cows, goats, or suits of clothing?
A) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah
B) Because their market value is unknown and fluctuating
C) Because they are not owned by the type of people who pay diyat
D) Because they are impure animals

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves this ikhtilaf by interpreting the Umar report as a guideline for reconciliation, not a fixed estimation, thus preserving the principle that diyat estimation is only with known-value items, while the mufta bihi allows cows, goats, and suits for practical flexibility.
