Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Woman's Diyat: Always Half? The Hanafi Refutation of al-Shafi'i
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i diyat exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a woman's diyat is half a man's in all cases, identify the Shafi'i exception for limbs with diyat less than one-third, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal using the general hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that a woman's diyat is always half a man's — the Shafi'i exception for minor limbs is rejected by the general hadith and consistent analogy.

The diyat (blood money) for a woman is a point of inter-madhhab disagreement. While all schools agree that a woman's diyat is half a man's for the soul (life), the Shafi'i school makes an exception for injuries to limbs where the diyat amount is less than one-third of the full diyat. In this passage, the Hanafi author vigorously refutes al-Shafi'i's position, relying on a general hadith and analogical reasoning. This lesson unpacks that refutation, showing how the Hanafi school derives its ruling and why it rejects the companion-based proof of al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi rule: a woman's diyat is exactly half of a man's diyat, whether for the soul or for any limb, regardless of the amount of diyat for that limb.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position, with no intra-Hanafi disagreement.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i agrees for the soul and for limbs with diyat of one-third or more, but differs when the diyat for a limb is less than one-third. In that case, he holds the diyat is equal for men and women.
The Shafi'i proof is based on a statement of Zayd ibn Thabit (RA).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand that al-Shafi'i relies on the companion's opinion as a basis for his exception. Note the internal inconsistency: al-Shafi'i does not generally consider taqlid of a companion as binding.
This is a methodological weakness the Hanafi author highlights.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses two arguments: (1) the hadith 'Diyat al-mar'ati 'ala al-nisfi min diyati al-rajul' is general in its wording and covers all cases, and (2) by qiyas: if deficiency is recognized in the full diyat (soul), it must be recognized proportionally in all parts, as a woman's earning capacity and value are consistently lower.
The hadith is transmitted both mawquf and marfu', establishing its authority.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: For a minor injury like cutting a fingertip (diyat less than one-third of full diyat), Hanafis award the woman half the man's amount, while Shafi'is award equal amounts.
This shows the real-world impact of the ikhtilaf.

عورت کی دیت مرد سے نصف ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء

كتاب الديات

قال ودية المرأة على النصف من دية الرجل وقد ورد هذا اللفظ موقوفا على على ومرفوعا الى النبي عليه السلام وقال الشافعى مادون الثلث لا يتنصف وامامه فيه زيد بن ثابت والحجة عليه مارويناه بعمومه ولان حالها انقص من حال الرجل ومنفعتها اقل وقد ظهر اثر النقصان فى التنصيف فى النفس فكذا في اطرافها واجزائها اعتبارا بها وبالثلث وما فوقه

ترجمہ اور عورت کی دیت مرد کی دیت کا نصف ہے اور یہ لفظ وارد ہوا ہے علی پر موقوف ہو کر اور نبی علیہ السلام کی جانب مرفوع ہو کر اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جو تہائی دیت سے کم ہے اس کی تنصیف نہ ہوگی اور ان کے امام اس میں زید بن ثابت ہیں اور شافعی کے خلاف حجت وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ عورت کا حال مرد کے حال سے ناقص ہے اور عورت کی منفعت کم ہے اور نقصان کا اثر نفس کے اندر تنصیف میں ظاہر ہو چکا ہے تو ایسے ہی ظاہر ہو گا عورت کے اطراف واجزاء میں نفس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور تہائی اور اس سے زائد پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔

تشریح عورت کی دیت مطلقا مرد کی دیت کا نصف ہے خواہ نفس میں ہو یا اطراف میں امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ نفس میں تو میں بھی اس سے متفق ہوں اور جب دیت اعضاء میں مہو تو دیکھا جائے کہ وہاں نفس کی دیت کا نصف یا ثلث واجب ہے یا کم ، اگر نصف یا ثلث واجب ہوتا ہو تو اس میں متفق ہوں کہ عورت کی دیت مرد کی دیت کا نصف ہوگی لیکن اگر کوئی ایسا عضو ہے جس میں مرد کی دیت کی تہائی کی دیت سے بھی کم لازم آتی ہے ( کما میجی ) تو وہاں مردو عورت کی دیت برابر ہوگی اور عورت کی دیت مرد کی دیت کا نصف نہ ہوگی۔ اس میں امام شافعی نے زید بن ثابت کے فرمان سے استدلال کیا ہے یعنی ان کی تقلید کی ہے ( حالانکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صحابی کی تقلید حجت نہیں ہے )۔ ہماری دلیل .... یہ حدیث ہے دیة المرأة على النصف من دية الرجل يه موقوفا اور مرفوعا دونوں طرح منقول ہے۔ اور یہ حدیث اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے امام شافعی پر حجت ہے۔ نیز عورت کا حال مرد کے حال سے ناقص ہے اور عورت کی منفعت مرد کی منفعت سے کم ہے لہذا یہ نقصان دیت میں بھی ظاہر ہوگا۔ پھر جب امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفس کی دیت میں نقصان تسلیم ہے اور اسی طرح اطراف کی دیت میں تہائی دیت اور اس سے زیادہ میں نقصان تسلیم ہے تو پھر تہائی سے کم میں عدم تسلیم کی کیا وجہ ہے۔ مسلمان اور ذمی کی دیت برابر ہے، امام شافعی کے ہاں نصرانی اور یہودی کی دیت چار ہزار درہم ہے اور مجوسی کی دیت آٹھ سو درہم ہے، امام مالک کے ہاں یہودی اور نصرانی کی دیت چھ ہزار درہم ہے

قال ودية المسلم والذمى سواء وقال الشافعي دية اليهود والنصراني اربعة الاف درهم ودية المجوسى ثمان مائة درهم و قال مالک دية اليهودي والنصرانى ستة الاف درهم لقوله عليه السلام عقل الكافر نصف عقل المسلم والكل عنده اثنا عشر الفا وللشافعى ماروى ان النبي عليه السلام جعل دية النصراني
Woman's diyat is half of man's diyat or not? Statements of jurists. Book of Diyat. He said: The diyah of a woman is half of the diyah of a man, and this wording has been narrated as a stop (mawquf) on Ali and as raised (marfu') to the Prophet (peace be upon him). Al-Shafi'i said: That which is less than one-third is not halved. His imam in this is Zayd ibn Thabit. The proof against him is what we have narrated in its generality, and because her condition is less than the condition of a man, and her benefit is less. The effect of deficiency has appeared in halving in the soul (nafs), so likewise in her limbs and parts, by analogy to it, and by analogy to one-third and above. Translation: And the diyah of a woman is half of the diyah of a man. This wording has been reported as mawquf on Ali and marfu' to the Prophet (PBUH). Al-Shafi'i said: That which is less than one-third is not halved. His imam in this is Zayd ibn Thabit. The proof against him is the hadith we have narrated in its generality, and because her condition is less than the condition of a man, and her benefit is less. The effect of deficiency has appeared in halving in the soul, so likewise in her limbs and parts, by analogy to it, and by analogy to one-third and above. Explanation: The diyah of a woman is absolutely half of the diyah of a man, whether in the soul or in the limbs. Imam al-Shafi'i says: In the soul, I agree with this. When the diyah of limbs is considered, if it is half or one-third of the diyah of the soul, then I agree that the woman's diyah is half of the man's diyah. But if there is a limb in which less than one-third of the diyah of the man is due (as comes?), then the diyah of the man and woman are equal, and the woman's diyah is not half. In this, Imam al-Shafi'i has argued with the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit, i.e., he has followed him (even though according to al-Shafi'i, following a Companion is not a proof). Our proof is this hadith: 'The diyah of a woman is half of the diyah of a man,' transmitted both as mawquf and marfu'. And this hadith is a proof against al-Shafi'i due to its generality. Also, the condition of a woman is deficient compared to the condition of a man, and the benefit of a woman is less. Therefore, this deficiency will also appear in the diyah. Then when al-Shafi'i admits deficiency in the diyah of the soul, and similarly in the diyah of limbs for one-third and above, what is the reason for not admitting it for less than one-third? The diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi is equal. According to al-Shafi'i, the diyah of a Christian and Jew is four thousand dirhams, and the diyah of a Magian is eight hundred dirhams. According to Malik, the diyah of a Jew and Christian is six thousand dirhams. He said: The diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal. Al-Shafi'i said: The diyah of a Jew and Christian is four thousand dirhams, and the diyah of a Magian is eight hundred dirhams. Malik said: The diyah of a Jew and Christian is six thousand dirhams, due to the saying of the Prophet (PBUH): 'The 'aql of a disbeliever is half of the 'aql of a Muslim,' and all according to him is twelve thousand. And for al-Shafi'i, it is narrated that the Prophet (PBUH) made the diyah of a Christian...
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the diyat (blood money) of a woman. The Hanafi position, stated clearly, is that a woman's diyat is always half of a man's diyat, whether the injury is to the soul (life) or to a limb. This is based on a hadith narrated as mawquf from Ali (RA) and marfu' to the Prophet (PBUH), which has general application. Imam al-Shafi'i agrees that in cases of life (nafs) or when the diyat for a limb is one-third or half of the full diyat, the woman's share is half. However, for limbs where the diyat is less than one-third of the full diyat (e.g., for minor injuries), he holds that the diyat is equal for men and women. The Shafi'i evidence is based on a statement of Zayd ibn Thabit (RA). The Hanafi rebuttal argues that the hadith is general and applies to all cases. Additionally, by analogy (qiyas): since the deficiency in a woman's status and benefit is recognized in the full diyat (life), it should apply proportionally to all limbs. The text also includes a brief discussion about diyat for dhimmis, noting that Hanafis hold equal diyat for Muslims and dhimmis, while Shafi'i and Maliki have different amounts. This secondary point shows the interconnected nature of diyat rulings.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid for homicide or bodily injury. For a woman, it is half a man's diyat according to Hanafis.
تنصيف (tansif): Halving; specifically, reducing a woman's diyat to half of a man's.
نفس (nafs): The soul or life; diyat for killing (full diyat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The diyat is equal for men and women
B) The woman's diyat is half the man's diyat
C) The woman's diyat is one-quarter the man's diyat
D) The woman's diyat is double the man's diyat

Key Takeaway
A woman's diyat is always half a man's diyat in the Hanafi school, based on a general hadith and consistent qiyas, rejecting the Shafi'i exception for minor limb injuries.

6 min
Diyah of a Woman is Half
States the Hanafi ruling and rebuts the Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the diyah of a woman, explain the evidence from the hadith and qiyas, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection for limbs below one-third.

Core Idea
A woman's diyah is always half a man's: the hadith is general and her deficiency is uniform.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute in the law of diyat (blood money). The Hanafi school rules that a woman's diyah is half that of a man in all cases—whether for life (nafs) or for any limb. The Shafi'i school, following Zayd ibn Thabit, restricts the half rule to cases where the prescribed diyah is one-third or more. We will explore the proofs from both sides and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the diyah of a woman is half of the diyah of a man for all injuries, including life and all limbs.
This is based on a hadith and qiyas.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees for limbs where the diyah is less than one-third (e.g., a finger). For such cases, the woman's diyah equals the man's, following Zayd ibn Thabit.
The threshold is one-third of the full diyah.
3
Examine the Hanafi textual proof
Analyze the hadith: 'Diyat al-mar'ah 'ala al-nisf min diyat al-rajul' (the diyah of a woman is half that of a man). The Hanafis argue this is general ('amm) and applies to all cases without exception.
The hadith is transmitted both mawquf (to 'Ali) and marfu' (to the Prophet).
4
Examine the Hanafi qiyas (analogical) proof
The deficiency in a woman's status and benefit (manfa'ah) is consistent. Since this deficiency already manifests as half in the case of life, by analogy it should apply to all limbs and parts.
The analogy extends from the greater (nafs) to the lesser (limbs).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical difference: for a finger wound (diyah less than one-third), under Hanafi law the woman receives half; under Shafi'i law, she receives the same as a man.
This difference affects actual compensation amounts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ودية المرأة على النصف من دية الرجل وقد ورد هذا اللفظ موقوفا على على ومرفوعا الى النبي عليه السلام وقال الشافعى مادون الثلث لا يتنصف وامامه فيه زيد بن ثابت والحجة عليه مارويناه بعمومه ولان حالها انقص من حال الرجل ومنفعتها اقل وقد ظهر اثر النقصان فى التنصيف فى النفس فكذا في اطرافها واجزائها اعتبارا بها وبالثلث وما فوقه
He said: And the diyah of a woman is half of the diyah of a man. This wording has been transmitted as mawquf to 'Ali and marfu' to the Prophet, peace be upon him. Al-Shafi'i said: What is less than a third is not halved. His imam in this is Zayd ibn Thabit. The proof against him is what we narrated with its generality, and because her condition is deficient compared to the condition of a man, and her benefit is less. The effect of deficiency has appeared in the half in the case of life (nafs), so similarly in her limbs and parts, measured by it (the life) and by the third and above.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the diyah of a woman. The author first states the ruling: a woman's diyah is half that of a man. He notes that this ruling is supported by a hadith transmitted both as mawquf from 'Ali and marfu' to the Prophet. Then he presents the objection of Imam al-Shafi'i: that for limbs where the prescribed diyah is less than one-third of the full diyah (e.g., a finger), the woman's diyah is not halved but equals the man's. Al-Shafi'i follows Zayd ibn Thabit in this. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The hadith is general and applies to all cases, including those below one-third. (2) By qiyas: since a woman's status and productive capacity are less than a man's, this deficiency is already manifested in the half diyah for life itself; consistency requires it be applied to all limbs and organs. The argument also uses analogy: if deficiency is acknowledged in cases of one-third or more, there is no reason to deny it for less than one-third. Thus, the Hanafi position is that the half rule applies universally.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money or monetary compensation paid in cases of homicide or bodily harm.
نصف (nisf): Half; the ruling that the woman's diyah is half the man's diyah.
تنصيف (tansif): The act of splitting into halves; refers to the ruling that the woman's diyah is halved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The same
B) Half
C) One-third
D) Two-thirds

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a woman's diyah is universally half a man's diyah, based on a general hadith and qiyas reflecting her consistent deficiency in legal capacity and benefit.

Diyah of Muslim and Dhimmi are Equal
Presents Hanafi ruling that Muslim and dhimmi diyah are equal, with Shafi'i and Maliki positions and Hanafi proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Muslim and dhimmi diyah are equal, explain the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and evaluate the Hanafi proof based on hadith and practice of the Caliphs.

Core Idea
The diyah of every covenanted person is exactly equal to that of a Muslim.

The amount of blood money (diyah) for a non-Muslim protected citizen (dhimmi) versus a Muslim is a matter of classical ikhtilaf between the madhhabs. This lesson presents the Hanafi position of complete equality, contrasts it with the Shafi'i and Maliki views, and examines the evidence each school brings—setting up a critical comparison.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of the Hanafi school: the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal in amount.
This is the first sentence of the passage: 'Wa diyat al-muslim wa al-dhimmi sawa''
2
Identify the opponents and their views
Note the two opposing positions: Imam al-Shafi'i gives different amounts for Jews/Christians vs. Magians; Imam Malik gives half the Muslim diyah for Jews and Christians.
Shafi'i: 4000 dirhams (Jew/Christian), 800 (Magian). Maliki: 6000 dirhams (Jew/Christian), based on full of 12,000.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Examine the dalil each opponent uses: Shafi'i cites a hadith setting specific amounts; Malik cites the hadith 'aql al-kafir nisf 'aql al-muslim'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school attacks the authenticity of the Shafi'i hadith (unknown narrator, not in major collections) and argues that its own hadith is more famous and supported by the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar.
Note the use of 'ashhar' (more famous) and 'amal al-sahaba' (practice of Companions) as tarjih factors.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the difference in ruling affects the actual amount of diyah paid: under Hanafi law, full amount; under Shafi'i, reduced and variable; under Maliki, half.
This practical consequence matters for judges and muftis in multi-madhhab contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ودية المسلم والذمى سواء وقال الشافعي دية اليهود والنصراني اربعة الاف درهم ودية المجوسى ثمان مائة درهم و قال مالک دية اليهودي والنصرانى ستة الالف درهم لقوله عليه السلام عقل الكافر نصف عقل المسلم والكل عنده اثنا عشر الفا وللشافعى ماروى ان النبي عليه السلام جعل دية النصراني واليهودى اربعة الاف درهم ودية المجوسي ثمان مائة درهم ولنا قوله عليه السلام دية كل ذى عهد في عهده الف دينار و کذالک قضی ابو بکر و عمر و ما رواه الشافعي لم يعرف راويه ولم يذكر فى كتب الحديث و ما رويناه اشهر مما رواه مالک فانه ظهر به عمل الصحابة رضى الله عنهم .
He said: And the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal. Al-Shafi'i said: The diyah of a Jew and a Christian is four thousand dirhams, and the diyah of a Magian is eight hundred dirhams. And Malik said: The diyah of a Jew and a Christian is six thousand dirhams, due to his (the Prophet's) saying: 'The blood money of a disbeliever is half the blood money of a Muslim.' And according to him (Malik), the whole (full diyah) is twelve thousand. And for al-Shafi'i, it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, set the diyah of a Christian and a Jew at four thousand dirhams, and the diyah of a Magian at eight hundred dirhams. And we have our proof: the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The diyah of every covenanted person (dhimmi) is one thousand dinars.' And likewise Abu Bakr and Umar judged. And the hadith that al-Shafi'i narrated, its narrator is unknown and it is not mentioned in the books of hadith. And the hadith we have narrated is more famous than that narrated by Malik, because the practice of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, is evident upon it.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage discusses the diyah of a dhimmi (a non-Muslim protected citizen) relative to a Muslim. The author presents the Hanafi ruling: the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal. Then he presents the positions of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. Al-Shafi'i distinguishes between different types of dhimmis: Jews and Christians have a diyah of 4000 dirhams, while Magians (Zoroastrians) have 800 dirhams. Imam Malik holds that the diyah of a Jew or Christian is 6000 dirhams, based on a hadith that the diyah of a disbeliever is half that of a Muslim, and according to Malik, the full diyah for a Muslim is 12,000 dirhams, so half is 6000. Al-Shafi'i relies on a hadith that the Prophet set the diyah at 4000 and 800 respectively. The Hanafi proof is a hadith from the Marasil of Abu Dawud: 'The diyah of every covenanted person is 1000 dinars.' This amount is the same as the full diyah of a Muslim in dinars. Additionally, the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar (the two Caliphs) supports this equality. The author then critiques Shafi'i's hadith as having an unknown narrator and not being recorded in standard hadith collections. He also notes that the Hanafi hadith is more famous than Malik's hadith and is supported by the practice of the Companions. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that Muslim and dhimmi are equal in diyah.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim protected citizen living under Islamic rule with a covenant of protection.
مجوسي (majusi): Zoroastrian, considered a dhimmi in Hanafi law.
عقل (aql): Blood money or diyah; used synonymously with diyah in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Equal
C) Three-quarters
D) One-third

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal, based on the general hadith and the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar.

Diyah of Dhimmis: Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki Views
Inter-madhhab dispute on diyah for dhimmis with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions on the diyah of dhimmis, identify the proofs for each, and explain why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Hanafi: dhimmi diyah equals Muslim diyah based on a prophetic hadith and Companion practice.

In this passage, the author presents a clear inter-madhhab dispute regarding the blood money (diyah) payable for a dhimmi. While all schools agree on the diyah of a free Muslim, they differ on whether a dhimmi receives the same amount. The Hanafi position asserts full equality, supported by a hadith and the practice of the Companions. Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of the proofs and the criteria for accepting a narration.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the Hanafi view: the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi is equal. Locate the primary proof: the hadith from Marasil Abi Dawud (and the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar).
The hadith states: 'Diyat kulli dhi 'ahdin fi 'ahdihi alf dinar.'
2
Identify the Shafi'i and Maliki positions
Note that Shafi'i distinguishes between Christians/Jews (4,000 dirhams) and Magians (800 dirhams), while Malik sets a uniform 6,000 dirhams for Jews and Christians.
Malik bases his view on a different hadith and his figure of Muslim diyah (12,000).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to their proofs
Examine how the Hanafi school rebuts Shafi'i's narration (unknown narrator, not in standard books) and Malik's narration (less famous, not acted upon by Companions).
The Hanafi proof is considered more famous and practically applied.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical difference: Hanafis pay full diyah for a dhimmi; Shafi'is pay 4,000/800; Malikis pay 6,000.
The amount changes based on the school followed.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
State that within the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi is the equality of Muslim and dhimmi diyah, due to stronger proof and Companion practice.
The author presents this as the relied-upon position.

احناف کی دلیل
ولنا قوله عليه السلام دية كل ذى عهد في عهده الف دينار و کذالک قضی ابو بکر و عمر و ما رواه الشافعي لم يعرف راويه ولم يذكر فى كتب الحديث و ما رويناه اشهر مما رواه مالک فانه ظهر به عمل الصحابة رضى الله عنهم .

ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل فرمان نبی علیہ السلام ہے ہر زمی کی دیت جب کہ وہ اپنے عبد ذمہ پر باقی ہو ہزار دینا ہے اور ایسے ہی فیصلہ کیا ابو بکر اور عمر نے اور وہ حدیث جس کو شافعی نے روایت کیا ہے اس کا راوی معلوم نہیں اور کتب حدیث میں مذکور نہیں ہے اور وہ حدیث جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے وہ اس حدیث سے مشہور ہے جس کو مالک نے روایت کیا ہے اس لئے کہ اس پر صحابہ کا عمل ظاہر ہوا ہے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے ابوداؤد کی مراسیل میں روایت ہے کہ ہر ذمی کی دیت ہزار دینار ہے اور یہی ماقبل میں تصریح کے مطابق مسلمان کی دیت ہے اور یہی حضرات شیخین کا فیصلہ ہے۔
اب رہی وہ حدیث جس سے امام شافعی نے استدلال کیا ہے اس کا راوی مجہول ہے اور کتب حدیث میں مذکور نہیں ہے۔ اور رہی وہ روایت جس سے امام مالک نے استدلال کیا ہے اس سے ہماری روایت مشہور بھی ہے اور صحابہ کرام نے اسی کے مطابق عمل کیا ہے۔
And for the Jew, four thousand dirhams, and the diyah of the Magian is eight hundred dirhams. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi is equal. Al-Shafi'i said: The diyah of a Christian and a Jew is four thousand dirhams, and the diyah of a Magian is eight hundred dirhams. Malik said: The diyah of a Jew and a Christian is six thousand dirhams, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The diyah of a disbeliever is half of the diyah of a Muslim,' and the complete diyah according to him is twelve thousand. Al-Shafi'i's proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) set the diyah of a Christian and a Jew as four thousand, and of a Magian as eight hundred dirhams. Explanation: According to us, the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi is equal. In this, Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i differ. According to Imam Shafi'i, if a dhimmi is Christian or Jew, his diyah is four thousand dirhams, and if Magian, then eight hundred dirhams. According to Imam Malik, the diyah of a Jew and Christian is six thousand dirhams. Imam Malik's proof is the hadith of Tirmidhi: 'The diyah of a disbeliever is half of the diyah of a Muslim,' and according to Imam Malik, the diyah of a Muslim is twelve thousand dirhams, so the diyah of a disbeliever becomes six thousand. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the narration from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq that the Prophet (peace be upon him) set the diyah of a Christian and a Jew as four thousand dirhams and of a Magian as eight hundred dirhams. Our proof: The saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The diyah of every person of covenant in his covenant is one thousand dinars,' and similarly Abu Bakr and Umar judged. And the hadith narrated by Shafi'i is not known, its narrator is unknown, and it is not mentioned in the books of hadith. And the hadith we narrated is more famous than that narrated by Malik, because it is apparent that the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) acted upon it. Translation: This is our proof. In the Marasil of Abu Dawud it is narrated that the diyah of every dhimmi is one thousand dinars, and this is equal to the diyah of a Muslim as per previous clarification, and this was the judgment of the two Shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar). As for the hadith used by Imam Shafi'i, its narrator is unknown and it is not mentioned in the books of hadith. And as for the narration used by Imam Malik, our narration is more famous and the Companions acted upon it.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the diyah (blood money) for dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state). The Hanafi position, stated by Al-Quduri, is that the diyah of a Muslim and a dhimmi is equal. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the diyah of a Christian or Jewish dhimmi is 4,000 dirhams, and of a Magian (Zoroastrian) is 800 dirhams. Imam Malik holds that the diyah of a Jew or Christian dhimmi is 6,000 dirhams, based on his view that the Muslim diyah is 12,000 dirhams and the hadith 'the diyah of a disbeliever is half of that of a Muslim.' The author then presents the Hanafi proof: a hadith narrated in Abu Dawud's Marasil that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'The diyah of every dhimmi in his covenant is one thousand dinars'—which equals the Muslim diyah as previously mentioned. Additionally, the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) is cited. The author then critiques the opposing proofs: Shafi'i's narration has an unknown narrator and is not found in standard hadith books; Maliki's narration is less famous than the Hanafi narration and the Companions acted upon the Hanafi one. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is the equality of Muslim and dhimmi diyah.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; compensation paid to the heirs of a victim of homicide or bodily harm.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen living under the protection of an Islamic state.
مجوسي (majusi): Zoroastrian; a follower of the Magian religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Equal to a Muslim's diyah

D) Six thousand dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's position that the diyah of a dhimmi equals that of a Muslim is based on a prophetic hadith and the practice of the Companions, and it is the mufta bihi.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Full Diyah for Specific Organs with Prophetic Proof
States ruling of full diyat for three organs with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that full diyah is wajib for the nose, tongue, and male organ and identify the Prophetic proof (dalil) that establishes it.

Core Idea
Full diyah is due for three organs: nose, tongue, and male organ—established by explicit hadith.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Al-Quduri's matn regarding diyat (blood money) for injuries short of homicide. The text specifies that full diyah is payable for the complete loss of the nose (specifically the soft cartilaginous part called the marin), the tongue, and the male organ. We will explore the Prophetic evidence that grounds this obligation and understand why the Hanafi school deems it wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage states that for complete loss of the nose (marin), tongue, and male organ, full diyah is wajib. Note that diyah is a financial compensation, not a physical penalty.
The ruling applies only to total destruction of these organs, not partial injury.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof cited is a mursal hadith from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab in which the Prophet explicitly assigns diyah to these three organs. Additionally, the Prophet's written directive to 'Amr ibn Hazm for the people of Yemen contained the same ruling.
Mursal hadith means the narrator (a Tabi'i) does not mention the Companion; it is accepted by the majority when corroborated.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah (Indication of Proof)
The explicit statement (laftz) of the Prophet assigns diyah to each organ. In Hanafi usul, a direct command or statement from the Prophet indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is evidence to the contrary. The wording is clear and unambiguous (qati' al-dalalah), though the chain is zanni (mursal).
The Hanafi school considers this proof sufficient to make diyah wajib, not just mustahabb.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Scholarly Disagreement)
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih: some other schools may differentiate between the nose and tongue, or hold that full diyah is not due for these organs without complete loss. The Hanafi school, however, adheres to the explicit hadith.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether full compensation or only hukumat (arbitrated amount) is due.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih (Preponderance)
The Hanafi position is based on a Prophetic text and is supported by the practice recorded in the letter to 'Amr ibn Hazm. It is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school, classified as zahir al-riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this specific ruling.

The Prophet sent a book via 'Amr ibn Hazm to the people of Yemen, which contained details of inheritance, legal penalties, and diyat. In any case, for all mentioned things, full diyah is obligatory. This is established from the hadith of Sa'id and from the book of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof: Al-Quduri, in his matn, states the well-known rule that full diyah (blood money) is due for taking a life (nafs). He then adds that full diyah is also due for three specific organs: the nose (specifically the soft cartilaginous part called the marin), the tongue, and the male organ (dhakar). The author of the commentary notes that the source of this ruling is a hadith narrated by Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, in which the Prophet explicitly mentions diyah for these. Although the narration is mursal (from a Tabi'i directly from the Prophet), it is accepted as proof by the majority of scholars. Additionally, the Prophet's written directive to Amr ibn Hazm, which contained the laws of diyat, also includes this ruling. Thus, for complete loss or destruction of these organs, full diyah is wajib.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; a financial compensation paid to the victim or their heirs in cases of homicide or bodily injury.
مارن (marin): The soft cartilaginous part of the nose.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith narrated by a Tabi'i directly from the Prophet without mentioning a Companion.

General Principle for Full Diyat on Limbs with Total Loss of Benefit or Beauty
Establishes a general rule: full diyah is due when a limb's complete benefit or intended beauty is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi general principle for full diyah on limbs and explain its proof from the Prophet's judgment.

Core Idea
Full diyah is due when a limb's complete benefit or intended beauty is lost—it is treated like destroying the person himself.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah lays down a key legal maxim (qa'idah kulliyyah) in the Hanafi law of diyat. The principle is that if an injury to a limb results in the complete loss of that limb's function (manfa'ah) or the complete removal of its intended beauty (jamal maqsud), then full diyah becomes wajib. The rationale is human dignity: such an injury is considered equivalent to taking the whole life. The proof is the Prophet Muhammad's (peace be upon him) judgment of full diyah for the tongue and the nose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage establishes a general ruling: full diyah is wajib when a limb suffers complete loss of benefit or intended beauty.
Note that this is a qa'idah kulliyyah—a general principle that governs multiple specific cases.
2
Identify the conditions
The two triggering conditions are: (1) complete loss of the limb's benefit (e.g., speech for the tongue), or (2) complete removal of intended beauty (e.g., the nose's aesthetic function).
3
Understand the rationale
The text explains that such an injury is min wajh (from one aspect) like destroying the person himself, and out of honor for human dignity (ta'dhiman li al-adami), it is treated as complete destruction.
This shows the usul principle that human dignity is a key consideration in diyat rulings.
4
Examine the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's judgment of full diyah for the tongue and nose. The tongue represents loss of benefit (speech), the nose loss of beauty.
The dalil is a Sunnah ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but the Hanafi school relies on it as the foundation for this principle.
5
See how the principle extends
Using qiyas, the 'illa (complete loss of benefit or beauty) is extracted from the two cases. Any limb meeting the condition triggers full diyah, not just those explicitly mentioned.
This is the hallmark of Hanafi fiqh: extending rulings via a rationally derived illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

General Principle: The basic principle regarding limbs is that if the complete benefit of its kind is lost, or a purpose of beauty in a human being is completely removed, then full diyah is obligatory; because it is in some way like destroying the life itself, and it is attached to total destruction in every respect out of honor for the human being. Its basis is the judgment of the Messenger of Allah of full diyah for the tongue and the nose. Translation: And regarding limbs, the general principle is that when a limb completely loses its benefit or completely removes the intended beauty of a person, then full diyah is wajib from one aspect, because of destroying the life (in a sense). And it is attached to total destruction in every respect for the honor of the human being. Its proof is the judgment of the Messenger of Allah of full diyah for the tongue and the nose. Commentary: Here a general principle is stated: when a limb's complete benefit is lost due to cutting, or the intended beauty is removed, it is as if the life itself is destroyed. So it is given the rank of complete destruction of life and full diyah is wajib. This is the requirement of human honor. Its proof is that the Prophet judged full diyah for the tongue and nose. So this is a general principle upon which many [branches] depend.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents a core legal maxim (qa'idah kulliyyah) in the Hanafi law of diyat. The principle states that when an injury to a limb results in the complete loss of that limb's function (manfa'ah) or the complete removal of its intended beauty (jamal maqsud), full diyah becomes wajib. The rationale is that such an injury is tantamount to destroying the person (nafs) in a certain respect (min wajh), and out of respect for human dignity (ta'dhiman li al-adami), it is treated like complete destruction. The proof cited is the Prophet's ruling of full diyah for the tongue (where speech is the benefit) and the nose (where beauty is primary). This principle then serves as the basis for deriving rulings on various other limbs.

Key Terms
قاعده کلیه (qa'idah kulliyyah): A general legal principle that governs multiple specific cases.
جمال مقصود (jamal maqsud): Intended beauty; the aesthetic purpose of a body part, e.g., the nose's function in facial beauty.
منفعت (manfa'ah): Benefit; the useful function of a limb, e.g., speech for the tongue.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes a general principle: full diyah is wajib when a limb's complete benefit or intended beauty is lost, based on the Prophet's judgment on the tongue and nose.

Applying the General Principle: Full Diyah for Nose and Tongue Parts
Expands the general diyah rule to specific cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of complete loss of intended beauty/benefit to determine when full diyah is due for cutting parts of the nose and tongue.

Core Idea
Full diyah is due for any part of the nose or tongue because intended beauty or benefit is completely lost.

This passage extends the general rule that complete loss of intended beauty (jamal maqsud) or benefit (manfa'ah maqsudah) triggers full diyah. The author applies it to specific cases: the entire nose, its soft part (marin), its tip (arranah), and the tongue. Even though these are parts of an organ, the ruling of full diyah applies because each part independently carries the beauty or benefit. However, if the marin is cut together with the nasal bone, only one diyah is due because the nose is a single organ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the organ and its intended benefit
For each injury, determine what the organ provides: beauty for the nose, speech for the tongue. The loss must be complete removal (cutting off) to trigger full diyah.
2
Apply the general principle
If the intended benefit is completely removed, full diyah is wajib. This applies even to parts of the organ like the soft part (marin) or tip (arranah) because they contribute to beauty.
3
Check for organ unity
If multiple parts of the same organ are cut together (e.g., marin with nasal bone), only one diyah is due because the organ is single. No doubling for parts of the same unit.
This prevents double counting.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage applies the general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) to specific cases. It first states that full diyah is due for the entire nose because its loss removes intended beauty (jamal maqsud). However, if the marin is cut along with the nasal bone (qsabah), only one full diyah is due, not two, because the nose is considered a single organ. Similarly, full diyah is due for the tongue because its loss removes the intended benefit of speech (nutaq). These rulings are direct applications of the principle: complete loss of benefit or beauty triggers full diyah.

Diyat for Partial Tongue Cutting: Function over Form
Provides rulings for partial tongue cutting with scenarios based on ability to speak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for partial tongue cutting by distinguishing cases based on loss of speech function and identifying the appropriate diyah method.

Core Idea
Diyat for partial tongue cutting depends on loss of speech, not on the amount of tissue cut; full diyat if most letters cannot be pronounced.

This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with an important principle in diyat: compensation for loss of a body part with no fixed share. Unlike limbs where fractions are set, the tongue has no fixed fraction for partial loss. Instead, Hanafi jurists examine the degree of functional loss. You will learn the three scholarly opinions within the school and the preferred ruling based on the victim's ability to speak.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Full diyat is due for complete tongue loss because the primary benefit (speech) is entirely lost. This is established in the school.
This is the baseline from which partial cases are derived.
2
Identify the Problem of Partial Loss
When part of the tongue is cut, the organ remains but speech may be impaired. The text presents multiple scenarios based on the ability to speak letters.
Focus on function, not tissue volume.
3
Follow the Three Intra-Hanafi Opinions
The text mentions three opinions: (1) divide diyat proportionally by total letters, (2) divide by letters related to the tongue only, (3) impose hukumat 'adl if most letters can be pronounced.
These opinions reflect different ways to measure lost function.
4
Determine the Operative Ruling
The preferred view (al-zahir) is that if most letters cannot be pronounced, full diyat is due; otherwise, hukumat 'adl or proportional division applies.
The key is whether the majority of speech function is lost.

Source Text

Likewise in cutting part of it when it prevents speech due to loss of intended benefit, even if the organ remains. And if he is able to speak some letters, it is said that it is divided according to the number of letters, and it is said according to the number of letters that are related to the tongue. So to the extent he is unable, diyah is obligatory. And it is said that if he is able to pronounce most of them, then a just estimation (hukumat 'adl) is obligatory because comprehension is achieved with some disorder. And if he is unable to pronounce most, then full diyah is obligatory because it is apparent that the benefit of speech is not achieved. Translation: Similarly, in cutting part of the tongue when it prevents speech due to loss of intended benefit, even if the organ remains. And if he is able to speak some letters, it is said that it is divided by the number of letters, and it is said by the number of letters related to the tongue. So for the letters he cannot pronounce, diyah is wajib. And it is said that if he is able to pronounce most letters, then just estimation (hukumat 'adl) is wajib because comprehension is achieved with some dysfunction. And if he is unable to pronounce most, then full diyah is wajib because it is apparent that the benefit of speech is not obtained. Commentary: If the tongue is completely cut, full diyah is wajib (as before). But if a part is cut and the rest remains, there are several scenarios: (1) If a part is cut but he cannot speak at all, full diyah is wajib because although the organ remains, the intended benefit is lost. (2) If he can speak some letters, there are different opinions: dividing by letters related to the tongue, or by total letters, etc. (3) If he can pronounce most letters, then hukumat 'adl. (4) If he cannot pronounce most, then full diyah.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for partial cutting of the tongue. The general rule is that if the tongue is completely cut, full diyah is due. However, if only a part is cut and the remaining tongue still functions, several scenarios arise based on the ability to speak. If the injury prevents speech entirely, full diyah is wajib because the intended benefit (speech) is lost even though the organ is partially present. If the person can still speak some letters, there is an ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) among Hanafi scholars: one opinion says diyah is proportional to the number of letters he cannot pronounce (based on the total number of Arabic letters, typically 28 or 29); another opinion says the division should be based only on those letters that are articulated specifically by the tongue (e.g., some letters are guttural or labial). A third opinion states that if the person can pronounce most letters, then a 'just estimation' (hukumat 'adl) is imposed — this is an amount determined by a judge rather than a fixed fraction. If he cannot pronounce most letters, then full diyah is due, because the primary benefit of speech is essentially lost. The commentary also notes that if even a small cut prevents all speech (due to nerve damage, etc.), full diyah is due.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): A just estimation; an amount determined by the judge based on the severity of the injury, not a fixed share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person's partial tongue injury prevents him from speaking most letters, what is the diyah?
A) Full diyah
B) Half diyah
C) Hukumat 'adl
D) No diyah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat, the criterion for partial tongue cutting is the loss of speech function, not the physical extent of the injury; full diyat is due if the majority of speech is lost.

Diyah for the Nose and Tongue: Full Compensation for Loss of Intended Benefit
Applying the general rule of diyah to the nose and tongue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah for the nose and tongue and apply the general principle of intended benefit to other organs.

Core Idea
Full diyah is due for any organ whose intended beauty or function is completely lost.

This passage extends a general rule (qā'ida) to specific cases: the nose and tongue. The rule is that full diyah is wajib when an intended benefit—beauty or function—is completely removed. We will see how this applies to cutting the nose, its parts, and the tongue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize the principle: full diyah is due when the intended benefit (beauty or function) of an organ is completely lost.
2
Apply to the Nose
Explain why full diyah is due for the nose: its beauty is an intended benefit, and cutting it off completely removes that benefit.
3
Examine the Parts
Note that cutting the soft part (maran) or nostril (arnabah) also warrants full diyah because the nose is a single organ.
Even if only part is cut, the intended beauty is lost, so full diyah.
4
Consider the Tongue
Apply the same principle: the intended benefit of the tongue is speech, so cutting it requires full diyah.
5
Confirm the Unified Diyah
Recognize that if multiple parts of the same organ are cut, only one diyah is due because it is one organ.

Source Text

Branches derived from the rule: And upon this many branches extend, so we say: In the nose, full diyah, because he removed beauty completely, and beauty is intended. Similarly, if he cuts the soft part (maran) or the nostril (arnabah), due to what we mentioned. And if he cuts the soft part with the bone, no more than one diyah is added, because it is one organ. Similarly, the tongue, due to loss of an intended benefit, which is speech. Translation: And upon this rule many branches are derived. So we will say: Full diyah is due for the nose, because he removed beauty completely, and beauty is intended. Similarly, when the soft part (soft part of nose) or the nostril is cut, due to the proof we have already mentioned. And if he cuts the soft part with the bone, no addition beyond one diyah, because it is one organ. Likewise, the tongue, due to loss of the intended benefit, which is speech. Commentary: Now some derived particulars are mentioned. Beauty is also intended from the nose, and when the nose is cut, the intended beauty is lost, so full diyah is wajib. Similarly, if the soft part is cut, or the nostril is cut, and if the soft part of the nose is cut, still one diyah is wajib because the nose is one organ. And similarly, if the tongue is cut, full diyah is wajib because the intended benefit from the tongue (speech) is lost.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with reasoning (ta'lil). It extends a previously established general rule (qā'ida) to specific branches (furu'). The rule: full diyah is due when an organ's intended beauty or function is completely lost. The nose is given as an example: its beauty is an intended benefit, so cutting it off warrants full diyah. This applies whether the entire nose, its soft part (maran), or the nostril (arnabah) is cut; even if some bone remains attached, it's still one organ, so only one diyah. The tongue is mentioned briefly: its intended benefit is speech, so full diyah is due when cut. The Urdu commentary elaborates that the nose is a single organ; cutting any part of it (soft part or nostril) does not increase the diyah beyond one. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is part of the matn of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; full compensation for homicide or injury, here specifically the full amount (100 camels or equivalent).
مارن (maran): The soft, fleshy part of the nose (the tip area).
أرنبة (arnabah): The nostril or the soft part including the side flaps.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Half diyah (50 camels)
B) Full diyah (100 camels)
C) One-third diyah
D) No diyah because it's not a vital organ

Key Takeaway
Full diyah is wajib for complete loss of an organ's intended benefit, and the nose and tongue are prime examples.

Diyah for Partial Tongue Amputation: Three Hanafi Opinions
Ruling for partial tongue amputation with three Hanafi opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions for diyah in partial tongue amputation and apply the majority rule (li'l-akthar hukm al-kull) to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Partial tongue loss: if most speech remains, hukumat adl; if most is lost, full diyah.

When the tongue is completely amputated, full diyah is wajib. But what if only part is lost, and the victim retains some speech? The Hanafi school presents three positions, reflecting different ways to measure loss of speech function. This lesson unpacks each opinion and the preferred view that relies on the maxim 'li'l-akthar hukm al-kull'.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the baseline: complete tongue loss
Understand that if the entire tongue is cut, full diyah (100 camels) is wajib because the organ and its function are completely lost.
2
Identify the three Hanafi opinions for partial loss
Three views are transmitted: (1) prorate by all alphabet letters, (2) prorate only by letters articulated by the tongue, (3) if most letters can be spoken, hukumat adl; if not, full diyah.
The third opinion introduces hukumat adl and the majority rule.
3
Apply the majority rule (li'l-akthar hukm al-kull)
The third opinion uses the maxim: if the victim cannot utter most letters, full diyah is due because the benefit of speech is effectively lost.
This maxim is a Hanafi usul principle.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
While al-Hidayah presents these as transmitted opinions without explicit tarjih, later Hanafi fatwa prefers the third view due to its practical basis in the majority rule.
Hukumat adl allows the judge to assess compensation equitably when partial function remains.

اور اگر اکثر حروف کے ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو یہاں پوری دیت واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ للاكثر حکم الکل، لہذا ظاہر یہی ہے کہ منفعت کلام ہی فوت ہوگئی ہے کیونکہ کلام تو حروف ہی سے مرکب ہوتا ہے اور اکثر حروف کو وہ بول نہیں سکتا تو کلام کیسے بنے گا۔
Ruling on diyah for cutting the whole or half of the tongue: Similarly, in cutting some of it when it prevents speech, due to loss of intended benefit, even if the organ remains. And if he is able to speak some letters, it was said: it is divided by the total number of letters. And it was said: it is divided by the number of letters that are related to the tongue. So according to the amount he cannot pronounce, diyah is obligatory. And it was said: if he is able to pronounce most of them, hukumat adl (equitable assessment) is obligatory, because understanding is achieved with some disorder. And if he is unable to pronounce most, full diyah is obligatory, because apparently the benefit of speech is not achieved. Translation: Similarly, in cutting some part of the tongue, when it prevents speech due to loss of intended benefit, even if the tongue exists. If he can speak some letters, it was said: divide by the number of letters. And it was said: divide by the number of letters related to the tongue. So diyah is due proportional to the letters he cannot utter. And it was said: if he can utter most letters, hukumat adl is wajib, because understanding is achieved with some disorder. And if he is unable to utter most, full diyah is wajib, because apparently the benefit of speech is not obtained. Commentary: If the tongue is cut completely, full diyah is wajib (as in the texts). But if a part is cut and remaining tongue exists, several scenarios: 1) A part is cut and he cannot speak at all, then full diyah is wajib because the intended benefit is lost even though the organ exists. 2) He can speak some and not others: first opinion: consider all letters of alphabet; calculate based on those he cannot pronounce. For example, if he can pronounce 14 letters (out of 28? actually half), half diyah is due. Second opinion: only consider letters articulated by the tongue, which are 14 letters (ت ث ج د ذ ر ز ش ص ض ط ظ ل ن). If he cannot pronounce all 14, full diyah; if cannot pronounce 8, then 5000 dirhams; if cannot pronounce 4, then 2500 dirhams. Qiyas on this. 3) Some say: if he can pronounce most letters (more than half), then hukumat adl is wajib because he can make himself understood despite some disorder. 4) If he cannot pronounce most letters, full diyah is wajib because the majority has the same ruling as the whole (li'l-akthar hukm al-kull).
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding diyah for partial tongue amputation. The passage first gives the general ruling: if the tongue is cut completely, full diyah is wajib. Then it treats partial loss, presenting three opinions (aqwal) from Hanafi scholars. The first opinion (qila) prorates diyah by the ratio of letters the victim cannot pronounce out of the total Arabic alphabet (29 letters? the text mentions 14 as example). The second opinion similarly prorates but only counts letters specifically articulated by the tongue (14 letters listed, not including those from throat or lips). The third opinion introduces hukumat adl (equitable assessment) if the victim can pronounce most letters, because he retains some speech function. If he cannot pronounce most letters, full diyah is due. The Urdu commentary explains each view with examples. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but in Hanafi fiqh, the third view (using hukumat adl and the majority rule) is often preferred. The authority of these opinions is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as they are transmitted in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat adl): Equitable assessment by a judge; a monetary compensation determined by the judge based on the extent of injury, not a fixed diyah.
للأكثر حكم الكل (li'l-akthar hukm al-kull): A legal maxim: the majority has the same ruling as the whole; here, if most speech function is lost, treat as complete loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Hanafi opinion introduces the use of hukumat adl for partial tongue amputation?
A) The first opinion (prorating by total letters)
B) The second opinion (prorating by tongue letters)
C) The third opinion (majority rule)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
For partial tongue loss, the Hanafi mufta bihi applies the majority rule: if most letters cannot be spoken, full diyah; if most can be spoken, hukumat adl.

Diyah for the Male Organ: Full Blood Money for Loss of Functions
Ruling for full diyah on the male organ and its glans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah for cutting the male organ or its glans, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the loss of intended benefits.

Core Idea
Full diyah is wajib for the male organ or its glans because all primary functions are lost.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on diyah (blood money) for the male organ (dhakar) and its glans (hashafah). The Hidayah states that cutting the entire organ or even just the glans triggers full diyah because multiple essential functions—urination, intercourse, impregnation, and semen emission—are lost. The reasoning is based on the principle that compensation is proportionate to the loss of primary benefits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Note that the act is cutting the male organ (dhakar) or its glans (hashafah). The ruling is full diyah (100 camels) wajib.
The same ruling applies to both, as stated in the text.
2
List the intended benefits lost
The text enumerates five benefits: urine retention/projection, impregnation, intercourse, normal insertion (for pregnancy), and semen emission. Loss of any one alone might not warrant full diyah, but the organ serves all these collectively.
The benefits are mentioned as a group.
3
Understand the glans ruling
The glans is considered primary (asl) for insertion and emission; the shaft is subordinate (tabi'). Therefore, even cutting only the glans results in loss of the organ's primary functions, warranting full diyah.
'Al-hashafatu aslun fi manfa'ati al-ilaaji wa al-dafqi wa al-qasabatu ka al-tabi'i lahu.'
4
Appreciate the qualification 'usual'
The text adds 'usually' ('aadah) for the means of pregnancy to exclude exceptional cases (e.g., pregnancy from friction), so the rule is based on normal function.
This is a fine point of ta'lil.

Source Text

پورا عضو تناسل یا حشفہ کاٹنے میں دیت کا حکم
وكذا الذكر لانه يفوت به منفعة الوطى والا يلادو استمساک البول والرمی به و دفق الماء والايلاج الذى هو طريق الاعلاق عادة وكذا فى الحشفة الدية كاملة لان الحشفة اصل في منفعة الايلاج والدفق والقصبة كالتابع له.
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی ذکر کہ اس سے وطی کی منفعت اور جنوانے کی منفعت اور پیشاب روکنے اور پیشاب پھینکنے کی اور دفق منی کی اور اس ایلاج کی جو کہ عادة حاملہ ہونے کا طریقہ ہے اور ایسے ہی حشفہ میں پوری دیت ہے اس لئے کہ حشفہ اصل ہے ایلاج کی منفعت میں اور دفق کی منفعت میں اور ڈنڈی حشفہ کے تابع کے مثل ہے۔

Ruling on diyah for cutting the entire male organ or the glans: Similarly, the male organ (dhakar), because through its loss the benefits of intercourse, impregnation, retaining urine, expelling urine, emission of prostatic fluid, and insertion which is the usual means of pregnancy are lost. And similarly, in the glans (hashafah), full diyah is due, because the glans is the primary organ for the benefit of insertion and emission, and the shaft is like a follower. Translation: Similarly, the male organ – through it the benefits of intercourse, impregnation, retaining urine, ejecting urine, emission of semen, and insertion which is the usual means of pregnancy. And similarly, for the glans, full diyah is due, because the glans is primary in the benefit of insertion and emission, and the shaft is like a follower. Commentary: Similarly, if someone's male organ is cut, full diyah is wajib because all its benefits are lost. The benefits of the male organ are: 1) retaining urine, 2) impregnation, 3) ejecting urine, 4) emission of semen, 5) insertion which is the usual means of pregnancy. The condition 'usual' is added because it's possible a woman could become pregnant from mere friction, but that is not the normal manner.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with reasoning (ta'lil). It establishes that full diyah is wajib for cutting the male organ (dhakar) because it results in the loss of multiple intended benefits: intercourse, impregnation, urine control and projection, semen emission, and penile insertion (the normal means of pregnancy). The same ruling applies to cutting the glans (hashafah) alone, because the glans is the primary organ for the benefits of insertion and emission; the shaft is considered subordinate. The Urdu commentary lists these benefits and explains the qualification 'usual' (عاده) to exclude exceptional cases (e.g., pregnancy from friction). This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ذكر (dhakar): The male external genital organ, including the shaft and glans.
حشفة (hashafah): The glans (head) of the male organ.
إيلاج (ilaaj): Insertion of the male organ, here specified as the usual means of pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if someone cuts only the glans (hashafah) of a man's male organ, what diyah is due?
A) Half diyah (50 camels)
B) Full diyah (100 camels)
C) One-third diyah
D) Hukumat adl (equitable assessment)

Key Takeaway
Full diyah is wajib for the male organ or its glans because they are the primary means of the organ's essential functions.

Diya for Partial Speech Loss: Three Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diya for partial speech loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi opinions on diya for loss of some letters and apply the principle 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole'.

Core Idea
Diya for speech loss can be proportional to letters lost, but Hanafis differ on which letters count and when full diya applies.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an internal Hanafi debate on how to assess diya when a person loses the ability to pronounce some letters but not all. Three distinct opinions are outlined: proportional calculation over all letters, proportional calculation limited to 14 tongue-based letters, and a distinction based on whether most or few letters are lost, applying either full diya or just appraisal. Understanding these views illuminates the Hanafi method of balancing precision with practical benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Opinions
Read the passage and list the three distinct methods for calculating diya for partial speech loss. Note the key difference in each: all letters vs. tongue letters vs. majority principle.
The passage uses 'بعض حضرات' for each view; they are not attributed to specific imams.
2
Analyze the First Opinion (All Letters)
The first view considers all letters of the alphabet equally. Diya is proportional to the fraction of letters lost. For example, if half of all letters are lost, half of full diya (5,000 dirhams) is wajib.
This view is straightforward but does not account for the functional importance of different letters.
3
Analyze the Second Opinion (Tongue Letters Only)
The second view restricts the calculation to 14 letters that originate from the tongue (list given: ت, ث, ج, د, ذ, ر, ز, ش, ص, ض, ط, ظ, ل, ن). Full diya is due if all are lost; partial amounts are specified: 8 letters lost = 5,000 dirhams, 4 letters lost = 2,500 dirhams.
This view emphasizes that speech primarily depends on these letters, making them the proper measure.
4
Analyze the Third Opinion (Majority Principle)
The third view distinguishes between ability to pronounce most letters vs. few. If most letters can be spoken, only just appraisal (hukumat 'adl) is due because the benefit of speech is largely retained. If most cannot be spoken, full diya is wajib because the majority has the ruling of the whole (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull).
This view is pragmatic and prioritizes the essence of speech over granular counting.
5
Determine the Prevalent View
The passage concludes with 'ظاہر یہی ہے' (this is apparent/relying on this), indicating the author leans toward the third opinion. In later Hanafi practice, the majority principle is often preferred because it avoids excessive calculation and focuses on the primary benefit.
Tarjih is not absolute; all three views are valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کچھ بول سکتا ہے اور کچھ نہیں بول پاتا تو ایک قول تو یہ ہے کہ تمام حروف اٹھائیں ہیں اب دیکھو کتنے نہیں بول پاتا انہیں حروف کے حساب سے دیت واجب ہوگی، مثلاً ۱۴ حروف بول پاتا ہے اور ہم انہیں بول پاتا تو آدھی دیت واجب کی جائے گی اور تمام حروف میں یہی حساب رکھا جائے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ صرف وہ حروف لئے جائیں جن کا مخرج زبان ہے اور ان میں یہ حساب رکھا جائے اور جو حروف زبان سے نکلتے ہیں وہ ۶ ہیں۔ ت ، ث ، ج ، د، ذ، ر، ز ہیں ، ش ، ص، ض، ط، ظ، ، ل ، ن ، ہی، تو اگر ان تمام حروف کو نہ بول سکے تو پوری دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر ان میں سے ۸ کو نہ بول سکے تو پانچ ہزار درہم اور مچار کونہ بول سکے تو پچیس سو درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ وقس على هذا ۴۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اگر اکثر حروف کے ادا کرنے پر قدرت ہو اور بعض کے اوپر نہ ہو تو حکومت عدل واجب ہے جس کی تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے، کیونکہ وہ یہاں اپنی بات سمجھا سکتا ہے اگر چہ کچھ اختلال وکی ہوگی۔ اور اگر اکثر حروف کے ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو یہاں پوری دیت واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ للاكثر حکم الکل، لہذا ظاہر یہی ہے کہ منفعت کلام ہی فوت ہوگئی ہے کیونکہ کلام تو حروف ہی سے مرکب ہوتا ہے اور اکثر حروف کو وہ بول نہیں سکتا تو کلام کیسے بنے گا۔
If he can speak some and cannot speak some, one opinion is that all letters are considered; then see how many he cannot speak, diya is wajib based on those letters. For example, if he can speak 14 letters and we can speak them, then half diya is wajib, and this calculation is applied to all letters. Some scholars said: only those letters whose makhraj is the tongue should be taken, and this calculation is applied. The letters that come from the tongue are: ت, ث, ج, د, ذ, ر, ز, ش, ص, ض, ط, ظ, ل, ن. So if he cannot speak all these letters, full diya is wajib; if he cannot speak 8 of them, then five thousand dirhams; and if he cannot speak four, then twenty-five hundred dirhams are wajib. Measure upon this. Fourth: Some scholars said that if he has power to pronounce most letters but not some, then just appraisal (hukumat adl) is wajib, the detail of which has passed. And if he is unable to pronounce most letters, then full diya is wajib because the majority has the ruling of the whole. So it is apparent that the benefit of speech is lost, because speech is composed of letters, and if he cannot speak most letters, how will speech be formed?
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents different views within the Hanafi school on calculating diya for loss of speech due to injury. The first view considers all letters of the alphabet equally; the diya is proportional to the number of letters lost. The second view limits the calculation to the 14 letters articulated by the tongue, arguing that these are the basis of speech. For these, if all are lost, full diya; if 8 are lost, half? (5000 dirhams is half of full diya? Full diya is 10000 dirhams? Actually, full diya for a free man is 10000 dirhams, so 5000 is half, and 2500 is quarter). The third view distinguishes between ability to pronounce most versus less: if most can be pronounced, only just appraisal is due; if most cannot, full diya is due based on the principle 'the majority has the ruling of the whole'. The passage does not specify a tarjih, but the later view aligns with the general Hanafi principle of considering the primary benefit.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money; compensation for bodily harm or death.
حکومت عدل (hukumat 'adl): Just appraisal; an estimation of diya based on the reduction in value of the injured part compared to the whole body.
الأكثر له حكم الكل (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull): The majority has the ruling of the whole; a legal principle that when the majority of a benefit is lost, it is treated as total loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second Hanafi opinion (tongue letters only), if a person loses the ability to pronounce 8 out of the 14 tongue-based letters, how much diya is wajib?
A) Full diya (10,000 dirhams)
B) Half diya (5,000 dirhams)
C) Quarter diya (2,500 dirhams)
D) Hukumat 'adl custom appraised

Key Takeaway
For partial loss of speech, the Hanafi school has three methods, but the preferred view applies the majority principle: full diya if most letters are lost, else just appraisal.

Full Diya for Loss of the Penis or Glans
Establishes full diya for loss of penis or glans due to complete loss of benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya for loss of the penis or glans and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the loss of primary benefits.

Core Idea
Full diya is wajib when the primary benefit of a sexual organ is lost, even if the subsidiary part remains.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses the diya (blood money) for cutting off the penis or its glans. The Hanafi school holds that full diya is wajib in both cases because the essential benefits—intercourse, ejaculation, and conception—are entirely lost. This ruling is derived from the principle that compensation corresponds to the loss of the primary function of the organ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: full diya is wajib for cutting off the entire penis and for cutting off only the glans.
The ruling is based on the complete loss of primary benefits.
2
List the Lost Benefits
Identify the five benefits mentioned: retaining urine, propelling urine, begetting children, ejaculation, and insertion for conception. The last two are the primary benefits.
These benefits are enumerated to show complete loss.
3
Understand the Legal Cause (Illah)
The illah is the complete loss of the primary benefits (insertion and ejaculation). The glans is the primary part for these functions; the shaft is subsidiary.
This illah is derived from ta'lil (reasoning).
4
Apply to the Glans
Even if only the glans is cut, full diya is due because the primary benefits are lost. The shaft's remaining urinary function is secondary.
The text explicitly states: 'the glans is primary, the shaft is subsidiary.'
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Shafi'i school holds that if the shaft remains, only appraisal (hukumat adl) or a fraction is due, because some function remains. The Hanafi response is that the primary benefits are lost.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (difference of opinion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا الذكر لانه يفوت به منفعة الوطى والاولاد واستمساک البول والرمی به و دفق الماء والايلاج الذى هو طريق الاعلاق عادة وكذا فى الحشفة الدية كاملة لان الحشفة اصل في منفعة الايلاج والدفق والقصبة كالتابع له. ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی ذکر کہ اس سے وطی کی منفعت اور جنوانے کی منفعت اور پیشاب روکنے اور پیشاب پھینکنے کی اور دفق منی کی اور اس ایلاج کی جو کہ عادة حاملہ ہونے کا طریقہ ہے اور ایسے ہی حشفہ میں پوری دیت ہے اس لئے کہ حشفہ اصل ہے ایلاج کی منفعت میں اور دفق کی منفعت میں اور ڈنڈی حشفہ کے تابع کے مثل ہے۔ تشریح اسی طرح اگر کسی کا ذکر کاٹ دیا تو اس میں بھی پوری دیت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ ذکر کے جو منافع تھے وہ سب زائل ہو گئے ، ذکر کے منافع یہ تھے۔ اولی کی منفعت پیشاب کو روکنا ۲- بچہ جنوانا ۳- پیشاب کو دور پھینکنا ۴- منی کا دفق ۵- وہ ایلاج وادخال جو عادة حمل کا طریقہ ہے۔ عادہ کی قید اس لئے لگادی کہ ممکن ہے کہ محض رگڑ سے بھی عورت حاملہ ہو جائے لیکن عادہ یہ عمل کا طریقہ نہیں ہے ۔ اور اگر ذکر ک حشفہ کاٹ دیا اور صرف ڈنڈی رہ گئی تو بھی پوری دیت واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ جو حشفہ کی منفعت تھی وہ بالکلیہ زائل ہوگئی اور اصل ایلاج اور منی کا دفق حشفہ کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور ڈنڈی حشفہ کے تابع ہے۔
And likewise the penis, because by it the benefit of intercourse, offspring, retaining urine, propelling urine, ejaculation of fluid, and insertion which is the usual way of conception are lost. Likewise in the glans, full diya because the glans is primary in the benefit of insertion and ejaculation, and the shaft is like a subsidiary. Translation: And similarly, for the penis, because by its loss the benefit of intercourse, begetting children, retaining urine, propelling urine, ejaculation of semen, and the insertion which is the usual way of conception are lost. And similarly for the glans, full diya, because the glans is the basis of the benefit of insertion and ejaculation, and the shaft is like its subsidiary. Commentary: Similarly, if someone's penis is cut off, full diya becomes wajib because all the benefits of the penis are lost. The benefits of the penis are: 1. the benefit of retaining urine, 2. begetting children, 3. propelling urine far, 4. ejaculation of semen, 5. the insertion which is the usual way of conception. The qualification 'usual' is added because it is possible that a woman may conceive merely through friction, but that is not the usual method. And if the glans of the penis is cut off and only the shaft remains, even then full diya is wajib, because the benefit of the glans is completely lost, and the primary insertion and ejaculation of semen occur through the glans, while the shaft is subsidiary to the glans.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that cutting off the penis or the glans necessitates full diya. The reason is that the primary benefits of the organ—intercourse, ejaculation, and the ability to conceive in the usual manner—are entirely lost. The text lists five specific benefits: retaining urine, propelling urine, begetting children, ejaculation, and insertion for conception. The glans is considered the principal part because it directly facilitates insertion and ejaculation; the shaft is secondary. Hence, even if only the glans is cut, full diya is due because those essential benefits are gone. This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah as it appears in the matn.

Key Terms
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans of the penis, considered the primary part for the benefits of insertion and ejaculation.
ذکر (dhakar): The male penis, whose loss entails full diya due to removal of multiple benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if only the glans (hashafah) of the penis is cut off and the shaft remains, what diya is wajib?
A) Half diya
B) Just appraisal (hukumat adl)
C) Full diya
D) No diya because the shaft remains

Key Takeaway
Full diya is wajib for cutting off the penis or its glans because the essential benefits (intercourse, ejaculation, conception) are completely lost, regardless of whether the subsidiary shaft remains.

Full Diya for Loss of Intellect Due to a Blow
Ruling with proof (talil) for full diya on loss of intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya for loss of intellect due to a blow and explain the legal cause (illa) that triggers full compensation.

Core Idea
Full diya is wajib because the benefit of perception is entirely lost, and that benefit is essential for worldly and religious affairs.

This lesson explores a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on diyat: if a blow causes complete loss of intellect, the full diya of 100 camels is wajib. We will examine the reasoning (talil) provided by Imam al-Quduri and how the loss of the benefit of perception (manfa'at al-idrak) justifies full compensation. Understanding this ruling gives insight into Hanafi principles of compensation for intangible losses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling upon: loss of intellect (aql) due to a blow. The hukm is that full diya is wajib.
2
Locate the cause (illa)
The passage explicitly states the cause: 'li fawati manfa'at al-idrak' – because the benefit of perception is lost. This is the legal effective cause for the full diya.
This is a direct talil, not a qiyas, as the ruling is derived from the nature of the benefit.
3
Understand the completeness of the loss
The commentary emphasizes that intellect enables a person to benefit in both worldly and religious affairs. The loss is total, hence full compensation. Partial loss might require appraisal, but here it is total.
This distinguishes it from other injuries where partial loss leads to proportional compensation.
4
Note the authority and source
This ruling is from the matn of Quduri, which is part of the zahir al-riwayah. It is agreed upon within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وفى العقل اذا ذهب بالضرب الدية لفوات منفعة الادراك اذبه ينتفع بنفسه في معاشه ومعاده ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور عقل میں جب کہ وہ مار کی وجہ سے ختم ہو جائے دیت ہے ، منفعت ادراک کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ عقل ہی کی وجہ سے وہ اپنے نفس سے منتفع ہو جاتا ہے اپنی دنیا اور آخرت کے بارے میں۔ تشریح اگر چوٹ ماری اور عقل ختم ہوگئی تو پوری دیت واجب ہو گی کیونکہ عقل ہی کی وجہ سے آدمی اپنے نفس کو اپنی دینی اور اخروی ضروریات میں لگاتا ہے تو جنس منفعت اور اک کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے پوری دیت واجب ہوگی۔
He said: And regarding the intellect, when it is lost due to a blow, there is diya because the benefit of perception is lost, whereby one benefits himself in his livelihood and his afterlife. Translation: Imam Quduri said: And in the case of intellect, when it is ended due to a blow, diya is due, due to the loss of the benefit of perception, because it is through intellect that one benefits himself in his worldly and religious affairs. Commentary: If a blow is struck and the intellect is ended, full diya becomes wajib, because through intellect a person engages himself in his religious and worldly necessities. So due to the loss of the genus of benefit and its entirety, full diya is wajib.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage, quoting Imam al-Quduri, rules that full diya is wajib if a blow causes loss of intellect. The reasoning is that intellect is the faculty of perception (idrak) which enables a person to manage his worldly and religious affairs. Since all such benefits are lost, full compensation is due. This ruling is part of the zahir al-riwayah, found in the matn of Quduri and commented upon in Al-Hidayah. The commentary emphasizes that the loss is total, hence full diya.

Key Terms
عقل (aql): Intellect; the faculty of understanding and perception that enables a person to manage his affairs.
منفعت ادراک (manfa'at al-idrak): The benefit of perception; the ability to understand and benefit from one's environment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the benefit of perception for worldly and religious affairs is completely lost
C) Because the person can no longer speak
D) Because of a specific hadith

Key Takeaway
Loss of intellect by blow triggers full diya because the benefit of perception, essential for all affairs, is entirely lost.
