Diya for Permanent Loss of Beard or Head Hair: Hanafi vs. Maliki/Shafi'i
Presents Hanafi ruling of full diya versus Maliki/Shafi'i ruling of just appraisal for lost hair

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on diya for permanent loss of beard or head hair, identify the opposing Maliki/Shafi'i view, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind each position.

Core Idea
Permanent loss of hair that harms beauty warrants full diya in Hanafi school; opponents argue it is only a non-essential addition warranting just appraisal.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri presents the Hanafi ruling that if a person's beard or head hair is shaved and does not regrow, full diya is due because the benefit of beauty is permanently lost. He then cites the counter-position of Malik and al-Shafi'i, who hold that only just appraisal is wajib, as hair is considered a mere addition to the body. Understanding this debate requires analyzing the different weights given to aesthetic benefits and the categorization of body parts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds full diya wajib for permanent loss of beard or head hair. Note that the basis is the loss of the benefit of beauty (manfa'at al-jamal).
The passage uses 'qaala' for Quduri's statement.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that only hukumat adl (just appraisal) is wajib, not full diya.
The text says 'qaala Malik wa huwa qawl al-Shafi'i'.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi reasoning (talil) is that the benefit of beauty is a recognized benefit; its permanent loss through shaving warrants full diya, analogous to other benefits.
No explicit analogy is given in the text, but it is implied by 'lianna yaftu bihi manfa'at al-jamal'.
4
Examine the opposing dalil
Malik and al-Shafi'i argue that hair is an addition (ziyadah) to the body, not an essential part. They analogize it to chest and leg hair, and note that shaving is customary in some lands.
They also mention that for a slave's hair, only diminution of value is due.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, full diya (10,000 dirhams) is due; under Maliki/Shafi'i, the amount is determined by expert appraisal.
This directly affects the quantum of compensation.

He said: And regarding the beard, when it is shaved and does not grow back, diya is due because the benefit of beauty is lost. He said: And regarding the hair of the head, diya is due for the reason we mentioned. And Malik said (and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i): In both of these, just appraisal (hukumat adl) is wajib, because that is an addition (ziyadah) in the human, and because of this, all the hair of the head and part of the beard are shaved in some lands, and it becomes like the hair of the chest and leg, and because of this, in the hair of a slave, the diminution of value is wajib. Translation: Imam Quduri said: And in the beard, when it is shaved and then does not grow, diya is wajib because the benefit of beauty is lost. Imam Quduri said: And in the hair of the head, diya is due for the reason we have stated. And Malik said, and this is also the saying of al-Shafi'i, that in both of these, just appraisal is wajib, because these (beard and head hair) are an addition in the human, and for this reason, all the hair of the head and part of the beard are shaved in some lands, and it becomes like the hair of the chest and leg, and for this reason, in the hair of a slave, the diminution of value is wajib.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding diya for permanent loss of beard or head hair due to shaving. The Hanafi school, as stated by Imam al-Quduri, holds that full diya is wajib because the benefit of beauty (manfa'at al-jamal) is permanently lost. The Maliki and Shafi'i schools, however, argue that only just appraisal (hukumat adl) is due because hair is an addition (ziyadah) to the human body, not an essential part. They analogize it to chest and leg hair, and note that in some cultures, head and beard hair are shaved without compensation. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that beauty is a recognized benefit, and its permanent loss merits full diya. The text does not provide a tarjih, but the Hanafi view is presented first as the matn.

Key Terms
منفعت جمال (manfa'at al-jamal): The benefit of beauty; the aesthetic value of hair on the face or head.
زیادتی (ziyadah): An addition; something not integral to the body's essential structure.
حکومت عدل (hukumat adl): Just appraisal; an amount determined by expert evaluators based on the specific loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The victim can grow a new beard later.
D) Diya is never owed for hair.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school awards full diya for permanent loss of beard or head hair because the benefit of beauty is a recognized compensable benefit, while the Maliki/Shafi'i school awards only just appraisal because hair is considered a non-essential addition.

Full Diyah for Shaving Beard and Head Hair: Hanafi Position and Proof
Presents Hanafi ruling, opponent view, and qiyas proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah for shaving beard or head hair that does not regrow, explain the qiyas jaliy proof using the concept of jamal, and distinguish between the free person and the slave case.

Core Idea
A free person's beard and head hair are sources of beauty; their removal requires full diyah, like ears.

What compensation is due when someone shaves another's beard or head hair, and it never grows back? The Hanafi school answers with a clear rule: full diyah. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that ruling, the objection from the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, and the Hanafi response rooted in the concept of jamal (beauty). We will also examine why the rule differs for a slave. By the end, you will be able to articulate the Hanafi position and its underlying analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Hanafi ruling
First, recognize the precise act: shaving the beard or head hair of another person, where the hair does not regrow. The Hanafi school rules that this requires full diyah (fixed compensation) for a free person.
The ruling applies only when the hair does not regrow; temporary removal does not trigger diyah.
2
Understand the opponent's view
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that only hukumat al-adl (valuation by experts) is due. Their reasoning: these hairs are not original body parts, so they are like chest or leg hair.
This difference in ruling leads to different practical outcomes in court.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (qiyas jaliy)
The Hanafi proof is an analogy (qiyas) with the two prominent ears (udhnan shakhisan). Just as cutting off ears requires full diyah because of total loss of beauty (jamal), shaving beard or head hair destroys their complete beauty, thus full diyah is wajib.
The key shared attribute (illa) is jamal that is intended and completely lost.
4
Refute the opponent's analogy
The opponent compared beard/head hair to chest/leg hair. The Hanafi response: qiyas ma'a al-fariq (invalid analogy) because chest/leg hair has no jamal, whereas beard and head hair do. Evidence: bald people take effort to cover their heads.
This refutation strengthens the Hanafi claim that the intended beauty is the decisive factor.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference on the slave case
For a slave's beard, Zahir al-Riwayah says only loss of value (hukumat al-adl) is due because a slave is for use, not beauty. A nawadir narration from Abu Hanifa says full value, but the mufta bihi is the loss of value.
This shows that the concept of jamal is context-dependent; for a free person, beauty is primary, for a slave, utility dominates.

Source Text

احناف کی دلیل
ولنا ان اللحية في وقتها جمال وفى حلقها تفويته على الكمال فتجب الدية كما فى الاذنين الشاخصين وكذا شعر الرأس جمال الاترى ان من عدمه خلقة يتكلف فى ستره بخلاف شعر الصدر والساق لانه لا يتعلق به جمال واما لحية العبد فعن ابي حنيفة انه يجب فيها كمال القيمة والتخريج على الظاهران المقصود بالعبد المنفعة بالاستعمال دون الجمال بخلاف الحر.
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ داڑھی اپنے وقت پر جمال ہے اور اس کو مونڈنے میں جمال کی مکمل تفویت ہے تو دیت واجب ہوگی جیسے ان دونوں کانوں میں جو ابھرے ہوئے ہیں اور ایسے ہی سر کے بال جمال ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ جو سر کے بال خلقہ معدوم پائے وہ سر کے چھپانے میں تکلف کرتا ہے بخلاف سینہ اور پنڈلی کے اس لئے کہ اس کے ساتھ جمال متعلق نہیں ہے اور بہر حال غلام کی داڑھی پس ابو حنیفہ سے منقول ہے کہ اس میں پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی اور ظاہر الروایہ کی تخریج کے مطابق جواب یہ ہے کہ غلام سے مقصود استعمال کی منفعت ہے نہ کہ جمال بخلاف آزاد کے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے داڑھی کے زمانے میں داڑھی ہونا جمال ہے اور اس کے مونڈنے سے داڑھی کا پورا جمال ختم ہو جاتا ہے لہذا اس میں پوری دیت واجب ہوگی۔ جیسے جو دونوں کان ابھرے ہوئے ہیں اگر چہ ان سے آدمی نہیں سنتا بلکہ اندر سوراخ میں جو پیٹھا بچھا دیا گیا ہے اس کے ذریعے سنتا ہے پھر ان دونوں کو کاٹنے کی وجہ سے پوری دیت واجب ہوتی ہے کیونکہ کانوں کا کامل جمال ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح سر کے بال بھی جمال ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ جو گنجا ہو وہ تکلیف کر کے اپنا سر چھپانے کی کوشش کرتا ہے۔ رہے وہ بال جو سینہ اور پنڈلی پر ہوتے ہیں تو ان سے کوئی جمال مقصود نہیں ہے اس لئے اس میں دیت بھی واجب نہ ہوگی، لہذا امام مالک اور امام شافعی کا داڑھی اور سر کے بالوں کو ان پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اور رہی غلام کی داڑھی تو نوادر میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہ روایت ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی غلام کی پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی لہذا قیاس ہی صحیح نہ ہوگا البتہ ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ قیمت کا نقصان واجب ہوگا۔ تو پھر امام صاحب کی طرف سے یہ جواب ہوگا کہ آزاد میں جمال مقصود ہے اور غلام میں خدمت کی منفعت مقصود ہے جو داڑھی کٹنے کے بعد بھی موجود ہے اس لئے غلام میں نقصان قیمت واجب ہے اور آزاد میں پوری دیت۔
Because of this, in some cities, they shave all head hair and some beard, and this becomes like chest and leg hair, and for this reason, for a slave's hair, loss of value is wajib. Commentary: If someone shaves another's beard or head hair and then the beard or hair does not grow back, then according to the Hanafis, full diyah is wajib on the shaver, because the beauty from both is lost, and this beauty is intended. The school of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i is that in both cases, hukumat al-adl is wajib, not diyah, because beard and head hair are not among the original parts of a person, as they are extra things; in other words, they are completing and adornment parts, so the loss is compensated by hukumat al-adl. This is why in some cities it is customary to shave all head hair, like in India etc., and in some cities to shave part of the beard and keep part, so both have the same ruling as chest and leg hair. And this is why according to the Hanafis, if a slave's hair is shaved, diyah is not wajib, but only the loss in value is wajib, so for shaving a slave's hair, loss of value should be wajib, and this is called hukumat al-adl. The Hanafi proof: 'And for us, the beard at its time is beauty, and shaving it completely destroys that beauty, so diyah becomes necessary, just as for the two prominent ears. Similarly, head hair is beauty. Do you not see that one who is naturally bald goes to great effort to cover his head? Unlike chest and leg hair, because no beauty is attached to them. As for the slave's beard, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that full value is obligatory, but according to the derivation (takhrij) of the Zahir al-Riwayah, the answer is that the intended purpose of a slave is the benefit of use, not beauty, unlike the free person.' Translation: And our proof is that the beard at its time is beauty, and shaving it completely removes the beauty, so diyah is wajib, like the two protruding ears. Similarly, head hair is beauty; do you not see that one who lacks it naturally goes to trouble to cover his head? Unlike chest and leg hair, because no beauty is attached to them. And regarding the slave's beard, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that full value is wajib, but according to the derivation of Zahir al-Riwayah, the answer is that the intended purpose of the slave is the benefit of use, not beauty, unlike the free person. Commentary: This is our proof: the beard at its time is beauty, and shaving it completely destroys the beauty, so full diyah is wajib. Like the two ears that protrude; even though a person does not hear with them, but inside there is a hole with a membrane through which he hears, yet cutting them off requires full diyah because the complete beauty of the ears is lost. Similarly, head hair is beauty; that is why a bald person takes trouble to cover his head. As for the hair on the chest and legs, no beauty is intended from them, so diyah is not wajib. Hence, the analogy of Malik and Shafi'i comparing beard and head hair to them is an analogy with a difference. As for the slave's beard, in the Nawadir there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that in this case also full value is wajib, so the analogy is not correct. However, the Zahir al-Riwayah is that loss of value is wajib. So the answer from Imam Sahib is that beauty is intended in a free person, but in a slave the benefit of service is intended, which still exists after shaving, so for the slave loss of value is wajib, and for the free person full diyah.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school holds that shaving a free person's beard or head hair that does not regrow requires full diyah because these are sources of beauty (jamal) that are intended by nature. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that only hukumat al-adl is due, arguing that these hairs are not original body parts. The Hanafi proof is based on analogy with the prominent ears, where full diyah is due for their removal due to loss of beauty. Also, the fact that bald people cover their heads shows the value of head hair for beauty. Chest and leg hair carry no beauty, so they are not analogous. For a slave's beard, there is a difference: the zahir al-riwayah (the relied-upon transmission) says only loss of value is due because a slave is intended for use, not beauty. However, a nawadir narration from Abu Hanifa says full value is due, but the authoritative view is the loss of value. The commentary follows the author's order: first states the Hanafi ruling, then the opponent's view, then the Hanafi proof, and finally the exception for the slave.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Fixed compensation paid for causing injury or death, equivalent to blood money.
جمال (jamal): Beauty; the quality that makes a body part or feature attractive and desirable.
حکومت عدل (hukumat al-adl): A valuation by just experts to determine the compensation for an injury where no fixed diyah is prescribed.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmissions from the founding imams, particularly from Imam Muhammad's six books.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or isolated narrations from the Hanafi imams, not part of the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on shaving a free person's beard that does not regrow?
A) Full diyah
B) Hukumat al-adl
C) Nothing
D) Compensation for loss of use

Key Takeaway
Beard and head hair are sources of intended beauty; their permanent removal requires full diyah, unless the person is a slave, in which case only loss of value is due.

Ruling on Mustache: Hukumat al-Adl Due
Specifies that shaving a mustache requires hukumat al-adl, not full diyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving the mustache and explain why hukumat al-adl is due instead of full diyah.

Core Idea
If a mustache is shaved, hukumat al-adl is due, not full diyah, because it is subordinate to the beard.

In diyat law, compensation for injuries to the body varies based on the injured part's status. This passage addresses a specific case: the mustache. The Hanafi school classifies the mustache as subordinate (tabi') to the beard, leading to a specific ruling. Let's examine why hukumat al-adl applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Shaving the mustache). What is the type of compensation? (Hukumat al-adl).
2
Understand the legal reason (ta'lil)
Why is hukumat al-adl due? Because the mustache is subordinate (tabi') to the beard.
3
Apply the subordinate principle
Since the mustache is subordinate, it follows the ruling of the beard's parts, which also require hukumat al-adl when shaved.
4
Note the most correct view
The text states 'wa huwa al-ashahh' meaning hukumat al-adl is the most sound view (al-ashahh) and thus the relied-upon position.

قال وفى الشارب حكومة عدل وهو الأصح لانه تابع للحية فصار كبعض اطرافه ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور مونچھ میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اور یہی اصح ہے اس لئے کہ مونچھ داڑھی کے تابع ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے داڑھی کے بعض اطراف۔ تشریح اگر کسی کی پوری مونچھ کاٹ دی تو اس صورت میں حکومت عدل ہے کیونکہ مونچھ داڑھی کے تابع ہے اور داڑھی کے اطراف مونڈنے میں بھی حکومت عدل ہے تو مونچھ مونڈنے میں حکومت عدل ہے۔
He said: Regarding the mustache, hukumat al-adl is due, and that is the most correct (al-ashahh) because the mustache is subordinate to the beard, so it becomes like some of its parts. Translation: The author said: For the mustache, hukumat al-adl is wajib, and this is the most correct, because the mustache is subordinate to the beard, so it is like some of the beard's parts. Commentary: If a person shaves off his entire mustache, in this case hukumat al-adl is due, because the mustache is subordinate to the beard, and in shaving the sides of the beard, hukumat al-adl is also due, so for shaving the mustache, hukumat al-adl is due.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on mustache. The matn states that hukumat al-adl (valuation by expert) is required, and this is the relied-upon position (al-ashahh). The reason is that the mustache is subordinate to the beard, which itself requires hukumat al-adl for its parts (as seen in the previous discussion where shaving the sides of the beard required hukumat al-adl). So by analogy with the beard's parts, the mustache also gets hukumat al-adl, not full diyah.

Key Terms
مونچھ (shaarib): Mustache; the hair that grows on the upper lip.
تابع (tabi'): Subordinate; something that follows the ruling of its principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the most correct ruling for shaving off a person's mustache?
A) Full diyah
B) Hukumat al-adl
C) No compensation
D) Half diyah

Key Takeaway
For shaving the mustache, hukumat al-adl is due because the mustache is subordinate to the beard.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Diyah for Shaving a Kawsaj's Beard: Three Scenarios
Three scenarios for beard shaving compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings for shaving the beard of a kawsaj and explain the basis in the presence or absence of beauty.

Core Idea
Compensation for shaving a kawsaj's beard depends on whether the hair is beautiful or disfiguring.

The Hanafi school gives nuanced rulings for injuries to body parts, including the beard. But what if the beard is so sparse that it is actually unattractive? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses the case of a kawsaj (a man with little or no beard) and explains that compensation varies based on the amount and arrangement of the hair, because the ruling is tied to the loss of beauty.

Guided Path
1
Define kawsaj
Understand that a kawsaj is a person past puberty with little or no beard. The passage uses this term for a man whose beard is sparse or missing, but the ruling depends on the condition of the hair present.
The definition is important because it sets the baseline for the three scenarios.
2
Identify the three scenarios
The passage describes three cases: (1) a few countable hairs on the chin only, (2) more hairs on both chin and cheek but not connected, (3) many hairs that are connected forming a full beard. List each scenario.
The key distinction is the quantity and connectivity of the hair.
3
State the compensation for each
For scenario 1: nothing (because the hair is disfiguring). For scenario 2: hukumat al-adl (fair compensation determined by a judge). For scenario 3: full diyah (complete blood money).
The basis is whether the hair adds beauty or not.
4
Analyze the underlying rationale
Notice that the ruling is not based solely on the body part but on the actual benefit (beauty) lost. If the hair is ugly, its removal is not a loss. If it has some beauty, compensation is proportional. If it is fully beautiful, full diyah applies.
This shows the Hanafi principle of evaluating loss based on actual benefit.

ولحية الكوسج ان كان على ذقنه شعرات معدودة فلا شئ فى حلقة لان وجوده يشينه ولا يزينه وان كان اكثر من ذالك وكان على الخد والذقن جميعا لكنه غير متصل ففيه حكومة عدل لان فيه بعض الجمال وان كان متصلا ففيه كمال الدية لانه ليس بكوسج وفيه معنى الجمال ترجمہ اور کھوسے کی داڑھی اگر اس کی ٹھوڑی پر چند بال ہوں تو اس کے مونڈنے میں کچھ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا وجود اس کو عیب دار کرے گا اور مزین نہیں کرے گا اور اگر اس سے زیادہ ہوں اور گال اور ٹھوڑی دونوں پر ہوں لیکن متصل نہ ہوں تو اس میں حکومت عدل ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں کچھ جمال ہے اگر متصل ہوں تو اس میں پوری دیت ہے اس لئے یہ کھوسہ نہیں ہے اور اس میں جمال کے معنی ہیں ۔ تشریح کھوسہ اس شخص کو کہتے ہیں جس کی داڑھی یعنی داڑھی کا زمانہ آگیا اور بوڑھا ہو گیا لیکن داڑھی نہیں آئی جیسے کچھ لوگ ایسے ہوتے ہیں تو اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں۔ - اس کی ٹھوڑی پر گنے چند بال ہوں تو اس کے رہنے سے کچھ جمال نہ ہوگا بلکہ اور خراب لگے گا لہذا اس کے مونڈنے میں کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کچھ زیادہ ہیں یعنی ٹھوڑی پر بھی ہیں اور رخسار پر بھی لیکن متصل نہیں ہیں تو اس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ اس میں کچھ جمال تھا جو فوت ہو گیا ہے۔ بال کچھ زیادہ ہیں اور گال بھی ہیں تو ان کے مونڈنے میں پوری دیت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ یہ کھوسہ نہیں رہا اور اس میں جمال تھا
And the beard of the kawsaj: if there are a few countable hairs on his chin, then nothing is due for shaving it, because its existence disfigures him and does not adorn him. And if there are more than that, and they are on both the cheek and chin, but they are not connected (mutasil), then hukumat al-adl is due, because there is some beauty in it. And if they are connected, then full diyah is due, because he is not a kawsaj, and there is the meaning of beauty in it. Translation: Regarding the beard of a kawsaj: if there are a few hairs on his chin, then shaving it entails nothing, because its existence would be a defect and would not beautify. And if there are more than that, and they are on both the cheek and chin but not connected, then hukumat al-adl is due because there is some beauty in it. If they are connected, then full diyah is due because he is not a kawsaj and there is beauty. Commentary: A kawsaj is a person whose beard-growing age has come and he has grown old but no beard has appeared, like some people. There are three scenarios: (1) He has a few countable hairs on his chin; keeping them brings no beauty but rather disfigurement, so shaving them entails nothing. (2) He has more hairs, on both chin and cheeks but not connected; then hukumat al-adl is wajib because some beauty existed and is lost. (3) He has many hairs and they are on the cheeks as well; then full diyah is wajib because he is no longer a kawsaj and there was beauty.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person with a sparse beard (kawsaj). The ruling varies based on the amount and arrangement of beard hair. If the beard is so sparse that its presence is actually disfiguring (few scattered hairs on chin only), then shaving it requires no compensation because the hair is not considered beautiful. If there is a moderate amount covering both chin and cheeks but not connected, then some beauty is present, so hukumat al-adl is due for its removal. If the beard is full and connected (i.e., a normal beard), then full diyah is due because this is not a kawsaj case; the beard is a source of beauty. This classification shows that the Hanafi school bases the ruling on the actual presence or absence of beauty (jamal), not merely on the body part.

Key Terms
کوسج (kawsaj): A person who has reached puberty and old age but has little or no beard; a man with sparse facial hair.
شعرات معدودة (sha'arat ma'dudah): A few countable hairs; a very small number of hairs that do not confer beauty.
متصل (mutasil): Connected; in this context, beard hairs that are continuous and form a full growth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man has a few scattered hairs on his chin that are unattractive. If someone shaves them, what compensation is required according to the Hanafi school?
A) Full diyah
B) Hukumat al-adl
C) Nothing
D) One-third diyah

Key Takeaway
Compensation for shaving a kawsaj's beard is determined by the presence of beauty: nothing for disfiguring hair, hukumat al-adl for partial beauty, and full diyah for full beauty.
